Manner of Sitting in Nafl Prayer: Different Opinions
Explains disagreement among Hanafi imams on preferred sitting posture for nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible sitting postures for nafl prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Multiple sitting postures are valid; the difference is only about what is best.

The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq did not specify a single sitting posture for nafl prayer because the Hanafi imams differed. This passage clarifies that all postures are permissible, but the preferred position for fatwa is to sit as in tashahhud throughout, as chosen by Zufar and endorsed by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize why the author omitted the manner of sitting: due to disagreement among the Hanafi imams, all forms are permissible.
2
List the differing opinions
Identify the views of Abu Hanifa (choice), Abu Yusuf (ihtiba'), Muhammad (tarabbu'), and Zufar (sit as in tashahhud).
3
Understand the key terms
Define ihtiba' (wrapping legs) and tarabbu' (cross-legged) as described in the passage.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that Abu al-Layth and al-Sarakhsi preferred Zufar's view, and 'upon it is the fatwa'.
5
Note additional rulings
Recognize that lying on one’s side without excuse invalidates nafl, and starting bent close to bowing is also invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف كيفية القعود في النفل للاختلاف فيه ؛ ففي الذخيرة والنهاية أنه في التشهد يقعد كما يقعد في سائر الصلوات إجماعاً، سواء كان بعذر أو بغيره. فعن أبي حنيفة تخييره بين القعود والتربع والاحتباء ونقله الكرخي عن محمد. وعن أبي يوسف : يحتبي. وعنهما يتربع. ثم قال أبو يوسف محل القعدة عند السجود. وقال محمد عند الركوع وعن زفر إنه يقعد في جميع الصلاة كما في التشهد. قال الفقيه أو الليث : وعليه الفتوى واختاره الإمام السرخسي لأنه المعهود شرعاً في الصلاة، واختار الإمام خواهر زاده الاحتباء لأن عامة صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في آخر العمر كان محتبياً ولأنه يكون أكثر توجيهاً لأعضائه إلى القبلة لأن الساقين يكونان متوجهين كما يكون حالة القيام اهـ. وتفسير الاحتباء أن ينصب ركبتيه ويجمع يديه عند ساقيه كذا في غاية البيان. وذكر في عن أبي حنيفة فيه ثلاث روايات فحينئذ فالإفتاء على إحدى الروايات ولا حاجة إلى أن تضاف إلى زفر كما لا يخفى. وقيد بالتنفل قاعداً لأن المتنفل مضطجعاً لا يجوز عند عدم العذر كما سبق، والشروع وهو منحن قريباً من الركوع لا يصح أيضاً في التنفل كما يشير إليه كلام التجنيس السابق وصرح به في موضع من شرح منية المصلي. الخلاصة على منع إلحاق الشروع بالنذر مطلقاً بل في إيجاب أصل الفعل قوله : (ورجح الثاني) أي القول الثاني المعبر عنه بقوله وعند البعض يلزمه القيام قوله : (ولم يذكر المصنف الخ) قال في النهر : ولم يبين للقعود كيفية لما أن الكلام في الجواز ولا شك في حصوله على أي حال كان، وبه سقط ما في البحر أنه للاختلاف فيه إنما الاختلاف في تعيين ما هو الأفضل، والمختار ما قاله زفر وهو رواية عن الإمام يقعد كما في التشهد قال أبو الليث وعليه الفتوى ولا خلاف أنه إذا جاء أوان التشهد جلس كذلك سواء سقط القيام بعذر أم لا .
And the author did not mention the manner of sitting in nafl due to disagreement about it. In al-Dhakhirah and al-Nihayah: He sits in tashahhud as he sits in all prayers by consensus, whether with an excuse or not. From Abu Hanifa: he has a choice between sitting, cross-legged (tarabbu'), and wrapping legs (ihtiba'). Al-Karkhi narrated it from Muhammad. From Abu Yusuf: he wraps his legs (ihtiba'). From both of them: he sits cross-legged (tarabbu'). Then Abu Yusuf said: The place of sitting is at prostration. Muhammad said: at bowing. From Zufar: he sits in the entire prayer as in tashahhud. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: Upon it is the fatwa, and Imam al-Sarakhsi chose it, because it is what is known in sharia in prayer. Imam Khwajazadah chose ihtiba', because most of the prayer of the Messenger of Allah in the later part of his life was ihtiba', and because it is more directing of his limbs to the qiblah, as the two shins are directed as in the standing posture. End of quote. The interpretation of ihtiba' is to erect his knees and gather his hands at his shins. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is mentioned about Abu Hanifa that there are three narrations concerning him. So then the fatwa is upon one of the narrations, and there is no need to attribute it to Zufar, as is not hidden. And he restricted it to the one performing nafl while sitting, because the one performing nafl lying on his side is not permissible without an excuse, as has preceded. And the commencement while bent close to bowing is also not valid in nafl, as indicated by the earlier statement of al-Tajnis, and stated explicitly in a place from Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. The summary is that it prevents attaching commencement to vow absolutely, but rather in obligating the original action. His saying: (and the second was preponderated) i.e., the second opinion expressed by his saying 'and with some, standing is obligatory'. His saying: (and the author did not mention etc.) He said in al-Nahr: And he did not specify a manner for sitting because the discussion is about permissibility, and there is no doubt that it occurs in any manner. And with this, what is in al-Bahr falls, that it is due to disagreement about it; rather the disagreement is in determining what is best. The chosen is what Zufar said, which is a narration from the Imam: he sits as in tashahhud. Abu al-Layth said: Upon it is the fatwa. And there is no disagreement that when the time of tashahhud comes, he sits like that, whether standing fell due to an excuse or not.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling on the manner of sitting in nafl prayer. It explains why the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq did not specify a posture: because all forms are permissible, and the differences are about the preferred posture, not validity. The author mentions multiple opinions: from Abu Hanifa, the choice between sitting normally (as in tashahhud), sitting cross-legged (tarabbu'), and wrapping legs (ihtiba'); from Abu Yusuf, ihtiba'; from Muhammad, tarabbu'. Abu Yusuf places the sitting at the time of prostration, Muhammad at the time of bowing. Zufar holds that one should sit in the entire prayer as in tashahhud. The fatwa is on Zufar's view (sitting like in tashahhud) according to Abu al-Layth and al-Sarakhsi. Khwajazadeh preferred ihtiba' due to the Prophet's practice. The author concludes that the disagreement is about what is best, not validity. He also clarifies that lying on one's side without excuse is invalid, and starting the prayer while bent close to bowing is invalid.

Key Terms
الاحتباء (al-ihtiba'): A sitting posture where one erects the knees and wraps the arms around the shins.
التربع (al-tarabbu'): Sitting cross-legged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which opinion on sitting posture in nafl prayer is considered the basis for fatwa?
A) Abu Hanifa: choice between sitting and cross-legged.
B) Abu Yusuf: ihtiba'.
C) Zufar: sit as in tashahhud throughout.
D) Muhammad: cross-legged.

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, multiple sitting postures are valid; the fatwa is to sit as in tashahhud, but the final ruling is about permissibility first, preference second.

Ruling on Praying Nawafil on a Riding Animal Outside the Town
Explains permissibility and conditions of nawafil on a mount outside the town

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory prayers on a riding animal, identify the conditions for its permissibility, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference regarding dislike.

Core Idea
You may pray nafl on your mount outside town, gesturing wherever it faces — but not inside the town.

This lesson examines the permissibility of offering supererogatory prayers (nawafil) while riding an animal outside the built-up area. The Hanafi school relies on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as transmitted by Ibn Umar. We will explore the proof, conditions, and nuances including the differing views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon (supererogatory prayer on a riding animal) and the hukm level (mubah/permissible according to the relied-upon view).
The text states it is permissible (ja'iz) but there is a difference about dislike.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: the hadith of Ibn Umar in the Sahihs showing the Prophet ﷺ prayed nawafil on his mount in any direction by gestures.
The hadith is mutafaqun 'alayh (agreed upon by Bukhari and Muslim).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action indicates permissibility. The gesture (ima') and the fact he did not face the Qibla show the ruling applies to voluntary prayers on a mount.
The lowering of prostration more than bowing confirms it is by gestures.
4
Identify conditions
Note the conditions mentioned: must be outside the town (misr), the animal must be walking on its own or standing (not driven by the rider), and Qibla direction is not required at the beginning.
Residents who go out for a need are included; the mount's purity is not required.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf says no harm; Muhammad says permissible but disliked. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is permissibility without dislike.
This difference does not affect the general ruling of permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وراكباً خارج المصر مومياً إلى أي جهة توجهت دابته) أي يتنفل راكباً لحديث الصحيحين عن ابن عمر : رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي النوافل على راحلته في كل وجه يوميء إيماء ولكنه يخفض السجدة من الركعتين . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مسافراً أو مقيمياً خرج إلى بعض النواحي لحاجة وصححه في النهاية وما إذا قدر على النزول أو لا، وقيد بخارج المصر لأنه لا يجوز التنفل عليها في المصر. وقال أبو يوسف: لا بأس به. وقال محمد: يجوز ويكره كذا في الخلاصة واختلفوا في حد خارج المصر والأصح أنها تجوز في كل موضع يجوز للمسافر أن يقصر فيه كما ذكره في الظهيرية وغيرها. وأشار بقوله «توجهت دابته دون أن يقول وجه دابته إليها إلى أن محل جوازها عليها ما إذا كانت واقفة أو سارت بنفسها، أما إذا كانت تسير بتسيير صاحبها فلا تجوز الصلاة عليها لا فرضاً ولا نفلاً كما في الخلاصة. وإلى أنه لا يشترط استقبال القبلة في الابتداء لأنه لما جاز الصلاة إلى غير جهة الكعبة جاز الافتتاح إلى غير جهتها. كذا في غاية البيان وإلى أنه إذا صلى إلى غير ما توجهت به دابته لا يجوز لعدم الضرورة إلى ذلك. كذا في السراج الوهاج. ولم يشترط المصنف طهارة الدابة لأنها ليست بشرط على قول الأكثر ، سواء كانت على السراج أو على الركابين أو الدابة لأن فيها ضرورة فيسقط اعتبارها. وصرح في المحيط والكافي بأنه الأصح، وفي بأنه ظاهر المذهب من غير تفصيل، وعلله في البدائع بأنه لما سقط اعتبار الأركان الأصيلة فلأن يسقط شرط طهارة المكان أولى. وقيد بالنفل لأن الفرض والواجب بأنواعه لا يجوز على الدابة من غير عذر من الوتر والمنذور وما لزمه الإعادة إذا استطاع النزول كما في الظهيرية.
His statement: 'And a rider outside the town, gesturing in whatever direction his mount faces' – meaning he prays supererogatory prayers while riding, due to the hadith in the Sahihs from Ibn Umar: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ praying supererogatory prayers on his mount in every direction, gesturing, but he would lower the prostration more than the bowing.' He gave it absolutely, so it includes whether he is a traveler or a resident who went out to some direction for a need, and he declared it sound in al-Nihayah, and whether he is able to dismount or not. And he restricted it to outside the town because it is not permissible to pray supererogatory prayers on it inside the town. Abu Yusuf said: There is no harm in it. Muhammad said: It is permissible but disliked. So it is in al-Khulasah. And they differed about the definition of outside the town, and the correct view is that it is permissible in every place where a traveler may shorten the prayer, as mentioned in al-Zahiriyyah and others. His statement 'his mount faces' without saying 'he faces his mount toward it' indicates that the place of permissibility on it is when it is standing still or walking by itself. As for when it is walking by the driving of its owner, prayer on it is not permissible, neither obligatory nor supererogatory, as in al-Khulasah. And it indicates that facing the Qibla at the beginning is not required because when prayer is permissible to a direction other than the Kaaba, it is permissible to begin in a direction other than it, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it indicates that if he prays in a direction other than that which his mount faces, it is not permissible due to lack of necessity, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. The author did not require the purity of the mount because it is not a condition according to the majority, whether it is on the saddle, stirrups, or the mount itself, because there is necessity, so its consideration falls away. And it was stated in al-Muhit and al-Kafi that it is the soundest view, and that it is the apparent madhhab without detail. And he reasoned in al-Bada'i: since the essential pillars are dropped, the condition of purity of place is even more worthy of being dropped. And he restricted it to supererogatory prayers because obligatory and wajib prayers of various types are not permissible on a mount without an excuse, such as witr, vows, and what requires repetition if he is able to dismount, as in al-Zahiriyyah.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on performing supererogatory prayers (nawafil) on a riding animal outside the town (misr). The text explains that it is permissible for a rider to pray nawafil by gestures (ima) in whatever direction his mount faces, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar in the Sahihs. The ruling applies whether the person is a traveler or a resident who has gone out for a need, and whether he is able to dismount or not. However, this is only allowed outside the town; inside the town it is not permissible. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf says there is no harm, while Muhammad says it is permissible but disliked (makruh). The correct view is that it is permissible wherever a traveler may shorten prayers. The text specifies that the permissibility is only when the animal is standing or walking on its own. If the owner drives it, prayer is not valid. Facing the Qibla at the beginning is not required because the entire prayer is performed in the direction of travel. The author also does not require the mount to be ritually pure because of necessity; this is the sound view in the madhhab. The ruling is restricted to nawafil; obligatory prayers and wajib prayers like witr and vows require an excuse to be performed on a mount, and if one can dismount, he must do so.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer; voluntary act of worship beyond the obligatory.
مصر (misr): The town or city; the built-up area where one resides.
إيماء (ima'): Gestures with the head or body to indicate bowing and prostration, used when one cannot perform the full actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, is it permissible to pray supererogatory prayers on a riding animal inside the town (misr)?
A) Yes, it is permissible without any restriction.
B) No, it is not permissible inside the town.
C) Yes, but only if one is unable to dismount.
D) No, it is makruh tahrimi.

Key Takeaway
Performing supererogatory prayers on a riding animal outside the town is permissible by gestures, based on the Prophet's practice, provided the animal moves on its own and the rider is not inside the built-up area.

Excuses for Obligatory Prayer on a Riding Animal and the Helper (Muʿīn) Dispute
Lists excuses and explains the helper dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recognized excuses for praying obligatory prayer on a riding animal and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the availability of a helper.

Core Idea
Praying on a riding animal is permitted only with a valid excuse; whether a helper removes that excuse divides Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

When traveling, a person may face legitimate hardships that excuse performing obligatory prayer on an animal rather than on the ground. The Hanafi school enumerates several such excuses, but a key point of disagreement arises: if a helper (muʿīn) is available to assist with mounting and dismounting, does the excuse disappear? Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, take different positions. This lesson examines both the list of excuses and the reasoning behind each position, along with the practical outcome for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Excuses
Read the passage and list the explicit excuses mentioned for performing obligatory prayer on a riding animal: fear of thief/beast, unruly animal requiring a helper, old age without a helper, mud/rain causing face to sink. Note that some examples implicitly refer to the helper issue.
The helper (muʿīn) appears in two contexts: for an unruly animal and for an old man.
2
Understand the Condition for Each Excuse
For mud/rain, the condition is that the face sinks into mud; otherwise, prayer on the ground is required. For other excuses, the common element is the inability to dismount or mount safely without hardship or danger.
These are not just any travel situations; they involve actual harm or inability.
3
Locate the Helper (Muʿīn) Issue
The passage notes that consideration of the helper is according to the Sahibayn, because Abu Hanifa does not consider ability through another as one's own ability. Identify the two examples that seem contradictory: the unruly animal (helper not considered) and the old man (helper considered).
The commentary reconciles them by attributing each to a different imam's view.
4
Compare the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa: the helper's ability is not the rider's ability; the excuse remains. Sahibayn: if a helper is available, the hardship is removed, so dismounting is obligatory. Note the evidence each uses: Abu Hanifa relies on the principle of personal capability; the Sahibayn rely on qiyas (analogy) to the removal of hardship.
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school, not between schools.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
The commentary cites later fatwa collections (Fatawa Qadikhan, al-Zahiriyya) that follow the Sahibayn's view. Additionally, the discussion about the woman traveling with her husband or mahram shows the practical application: if she can be helped, she should dismount according to the Sahibayn. The mufta bihi is therefore the Sahibayn's position.
However, Abu Hanifa's view may still be considered in cases of extreme difficulty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغيرها. ومن الأعذار أن يخاف اللص أو السبع على نفسه أو ماله ولم يقف له رفقاؤه، وكذا إذا كانت الدابة جموحاً لا يقدر على ركوبها إلا بمعين أو هو شيخ كبير لا يجد من يركبه، ومن الأعذار الطين والمطر بشرط أن يكون بحال يغيب وجهه في الطين، أما إذا لم يكن كذلك والأرض ندية فإنه يصلي هناك كما في الخلاصة والظاهر أن اعتبار المعين هنا إنما هو على قولهما لما عرف أن أبا حنيفة لا يعتبر قدرة الغير وفي فتاوى قاضيخان والظهيرية : الرجل إذا حمل امرأته من القرية إلى المصر كان لها أن تصلي على الدابة في الطريق إذا كانت لا تقدر على الركوب والنزول انتهى . والظاهر منه أنها لا تقدر بنفسها من غير معين حتى إذا قدرت على الركوب والنزول بمحرمها أو زوجها فإنه لا يجب عليها ذلك، ويجوز لها صلاة الفرض على الدابة لأن أبا حنيفة لا يجعل قدرة الإنسان بغيره كقدرته بنفسه، لكن ذكر في منية المصلي أنه إذا لم يكن معها محرم فإنه تجوز صلاتها على الدابة إذا لم تقدر على النزول والظاهر أن اشتراط عدم المحرم معها مفرع على قولهما فقط، ولم أر حكم ما إذا كان راكباً مع امرأته أو أمه كما وقع للفقير مع أمه في سفر الحج ولم تقدر المرأة على النزول والركوب أيجوز للرجل المعادل لها أن يصلي الفرض على الدابة كما يجوز للمرأة إذا كان لا يتمكن من النزول وحده لميل المحمل بنزوله وحده، وينبغي أن يكون له ذلك كما لا يخفى

قوله : (والظاهر أن اعتبار المعين هنا الخ) أي في قوله : (وكذا إذا كانت الدابة جموحاً الخ) لكن فيه أنه لم يعتبر المعين إذ لو اعتبر لزمه النزول إذا وجد المعين نعم قوله «أو شيخ كبير لا يجد من يركبه يدل بمفهومه على أنه لو وجد من يركبه يلزمه النزول فيدل على اعتبار المعين، فالمسألة الأولى دلت على عدم اعتبار المعين والثانية دلت على اعتباره .

قوله : ( وينبغي أن يكون له ذلك قد يقال بخلافه لأن الرجل في هذه الصورة قادر على النزول والعجز من المرأة ليس عذراً قائماً فيه بل هو قائم فيها إلا أن يقال: إن الكلام هو عند عدم إمكان ركوب المرأة إذا نزل الرجل وإذا كان كذلك يلزم من نزوله سقوط المحمل على الأرض أو عقر الجمل أو هلاك المرأة أو نحو ذلك فيكون عذراً قائماً فيه راجعاً إليه كخوفه على نفسه أو ماله تأمل .
And among the excuses are: fear of a thief or a beast for oneself or one's property and his companions did not stop for him. Likewise, if the animal is unruly and he cannot ride it except with a helper, or he is a very old man who cannot find someone to mount him. Among the excuses are mud and rain, provided that his face sinks in the mud. If it is not like that and the ground is moist, then he prays there as in al-Khulasa. And evidently, consideration of the helper here is according to their (the Sahibayn) view because it is known that Abu Hanifa does not consider the ability of another. And in the Fatawa of Qadikhan and al-Zahiriyya: if a man carries his wife from the village to the city, she may pray on the animal on the road if she cannot mount and dismount. End. And apparently, she cannot do it herself without a helper, such that if she can mount and dismount with her mahram or husband, it is not obligatory upon her, and it is permissible for her to pray the obligatory prayer on the animal because Abu Hanifa does not consider a person's ability through another as his own ability. But in Munyat al-Musalli, it is mentioned that if she has no mahram with her, then her prayer on the animal is permissible if she cannot dismount. Apparently, the condition of having no mahram with her is a branch of their (Sahibayn) view only. And I have not seen the ruling when a man rides with his wife or mother, as happened to the poor man with his mother in the journey of Hajj, and the woman could not dismount and mount: is it permissible for the man who is with her to pray the obligatory prayer on the animal, just as it is permissible for the woman if he cannot dismount alone due to the leaning of the howdah by his dismounting alone? And it should be that he may do so, as is not hidden. His statement: (And evidently, consideration of the helper here etc.) meaning in his statement: (Likewise, if the animal is unruly etc.) but there is that he did not consider the helper, for if he considered, dismounting would be obligatory upon him when he finds a helper. Yes, his statement 'or a very old man who cannot find someone to mount him' indicates by its implication that if he finds someone to mount him, dismounting is obligatory upon him, indicating consideration of the helper. So the first issue indicates non-consideration of the helper, and the second indicates its consideration. His statement: (And it should be that he may do so) might be objected to because the man in this situation is able to dismount, and the woman's inability is not an excuse present in him but is present in her, unless it is said: the discussion is when it is impossible for the woman to ride if the man dismounts, and if so, his dismounting leads to the howdah falling to the ground, or the camel being hamstrung, or the woman being killed, etc., so it becomes an excuse present in him that reverts to him, like his fear for himself or his property. Reflect.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the excuses that permit performing obligatory prayer on a riding animal, as well as the issue of whether the availability of a helper (muʿīn) obligates dismounting. The text begins by listing the excuses: fear of a thief or beast, an unruly animal, old age, and mud/rain. The commentary clarifies that the consideration of a helper (i.e., if a helper is available, must one dismount?) is based on the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), who consider the ability of another as one's own ability. In contrast, Abu Hanifa does not consider ability through another as one's own. This difference is then applied to the case of a woman traveling with her husband or mahram. According to Abu Hanifa, she may continue praying on the animal even if her husband is present and could help her, because his ability is not her ability. The commentary also reconciles two contradictory examples in the matn: the case of an unruly animal (where a helper is not considered) and the case of an old man (where a helper is considered). The reconciliation is that the first example follows Abu Hanifa's view, and the second follows the Sahibayn's view. The passage ends with a discussion of whether a man can also pray on the animal when accompanying a woman who cannot ride without him, concluding that it is permissible due to the harm that would result from his dismounting.

Key Terms
معين (muʿīn): A person who can help the rider mount, dismount, or manage the animal.
قدرة الغير (qudrat al-ghayr): The ability of another person to assist; Abu Hanifa does not consider this as the rider's own ability.
قولهما (qawlihimā): The legal opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Abu Hanifa regarding a helper (muʿīn) for a person praying obligatory prayer on a riding animal?
A) The presence of a helper makes it obligatory to dismount.
B) The helper's ability is considered as the rider's own ability.
C) Abu Hanifa does not consider ability through another as one's own ability.
D) Abu Hanifa agrees with the Sahibayn on this issue.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa does not consider ability through another as one's own; the Sahibayn do, and later fatwa follows them – but both views are part of the Hanafi tradition.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
8 min
Building (Binā') Upon Descending from a Mount in Supererogatory Prayer
Explains ruling on building and distinction between gesture types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building upon descending during supererogatory prayer and explain the key distinction between a rider's gesture and a sick person's gesture.

Core Idea
A rider's gesture is not a substitute (badal) but a direct permission, so descending does not break the prayer's continuity.

When a person prays a supererogatory prayer while riding a mount, the Lawgiver permits gesturing (īmā') instead of full bows and prostrations, even though the rider could potentially perform full postures. But what happens if the rider dismounts mid-prayer? May he continue from where he left off, or must he restart? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position on building (binā') upon descending, exploring the reasoning behind a classic intra-madhhab dispute with the Sahibayn and the essential distinction between a rider's gesture and that of a sick person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act in question is 'building' (al-binā') – continuing a prayer after changing from riding to dismounted state. The ruling according to Abu Hanifa is that one may build (continue) if the prayer is supererogatory, because the initial iḥrām was contracted with permission to gesture.
This applies only when the prayer began while riding and the person then descends.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the person must start the prayer anew when descending, because they view the gesture as a weak substitute that cannot support a 'strong' full-posture continuation. Muhammad makes an exception if one rakʿah was completed before descending.
The difference stems from whether the rider's gesture is considered a badal (substitute) or a direct permission.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
The Sahibayn's proof relies on an analogy with a sick person: if a sick person prays part with gestures and then recovers, he cannot build because the gesture was a substitute for the actual pillars, so building the strong upon the weak would be invalid. They argue the same applies to the rider.
This is the 'strong upon weak' argument.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes the rider's gesture from the sick person's. The sick person's gesture is a badal (substitute) because he is completely incapable of full postures. The rider, however, can potentially perform full postures (e.g., standing on stirrups) even while riding; the Lawgiver permitted the gesture not as a substitute but as a direct concession. Hence the rider's gesture is 'strong in itself,' and descending does not create a weak foundation.
Another distinction: the sick person cannot begin prayer with gestures if able, while the rider can. This is a key difference in the permissibility of initiating the prayer with gestures.
5
Note the limitation to supererogatory prayers
The ruling in al-Hidāyah explicitly restricts the permissibility of building upon descending to supererogatory (nafl) prayers. For obligatory prayers (farḍ), if one begins riding and then descends, he must restart, because he is obligated to perform full postures from the start and cannot rely on the gesture permission.
Thus, the building rule does not apply to farḍ prayers, except perhaps in cases of genuine excuse where the prayer itself was permissible on the mount.

Source Text

His saying (and he builds) upon descending, not upon the opposite: i.e., if he begins the supererogatory prayer riding then descends, he builds; and he does not build if he begins it while dismounted and then mounts, because the iḥrām of the rider is a contract that permits bowing and prostration due to his ability to dismount, so if he performs them, it is valid; while the iḥrām of the one who dismounted is contracted necessitating bowing and prostration, so he cannot abandon what has become obligatory without excuse. And from Abu Yusuf that he should start anew if he also descends; similarly with Muhammad if he descends after having prayed one rakʿah. (And when he prays on the mount, etc.) al-Ramli said: i.e., the obligatory prayer; reflect. I said: there is no need for reflection because the discussion is about the obligatory prayer, evidenced by the rest of the expression of al-Ẓahīriyyah distinguishing between the state of an excuse and other than it, and that the author will soon state that after the completion of the expression. He said: (As for praying on the carriage, etc.) one should consider the difference between it in the state of not moving and the litter if it is on sticks on the ground, for the carriage whose side is on the mount is like the litter if it is on the mount and under it are sticks on the ground, so let one reflect. Perhaps the intended meaning of 'carriage' is other than its famous meaning, for the famous one is in al-Mughrib that it is something like a litter on which loads are carried, and it is clear that its base is on the ground but it is tied with a rope etc. and pulled by cows or camels; but what is intended here is what is called in our custom 'takht', which is a litter having four sticks at its ends like a bier, carried on two camels or two mules. His saying: (And it is appropriate to carry it, etc.) ... And the seal once with a sitting after every four to the extent of it, and he performs witr in congregation only in Ramadan. And his saying: without an excuse is an explanation of the reality, not as a distinction for the excuse, for what is transmitted in al-Khāniyyah is that if the praying person mounts the mount, his prayer becomes invalid. And it was refuted in Ghāyat al-Bayān for the reasoning of one who distinguished between them that descending is a small action and mounting is a large action, that it is prohibited because if the praying person lifted and placed on the saddle, he would not build even though the action did not occur, let alone a large action; and the correct distinction is what is in al-Hidāyah. End. And in al-Nihāyah it was presented that the saying of building when he descends leads to building the strong upon the weak, and that is not permissible, like a sick person who prayed part of his prayer with gestures and then was able to perform the pillars, it is not permissible for him to build, to avoid what we said. And he answered that the gesture of the sick person is not like the gesture of the rider because the gesture of the sick person is a substitute for the pillars, while the gesture of the rider is not a substitute for them, because the substitute in acts of worship is the name for what is resorted to when another is incapable, and the sick person was prevented by his illness from the pillars, so the gesture became a substitute for them; but the rider was not prevented by the riding from the pillars because he can erect himself on the stirrups, so that from him constitutes standing, and likewise he can fall as bowing and prostrating; yet despite this, the Lawgiver has authorized the gesture, so the gesture is not a substitute, thus it is strong in itself, so it does not lead to building the strong upon the weak. And in al-Muḥīṭ he distinguished in another way: that the sick person cannot begin prayer with gestures while being able to bow and prostrate; therefore if he becomes able during his prayer, he does not build. As for the rider here, he can begin prayer with gestures on the mount while being able, so descending does not prevent him from building. It is said in al-Nihāyah: In my view, according to this distinction, one should not build in the obligatory prayer when he begins it riding and then descends, because he cannot begin it with gestures on the mount when able; therefore the issue in al-Hidāyah is restricted to supererogatory prayer. And Imam al-Asbijābī mentioned that the sick person's starting anew when he recovers during his prayer is only in the obligatory prayer, and there is no narration from them regarding supererogatory prayer concerning the sick person. So it is possible that the sick person also does not start anew in supererogatory prayer, in which case there is no need for a distinction; and it is possible that he does start anew, contrary to the rider, and the distinction is what we have explained. End.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq is an expansion probe on the rulings of prayer upon a mount. It opens with a ruling on 'building' (al-bināʾ) when one changes from riding to dismounted state during supererogatory prayer. The foundational principle: if one begins a nafl prayer while riding and then descends, he may continue (build) from where he left off, because his initial iḥrām was contracted with the permission to use gestures (īmāʾ) due to his potential ability to dismount. Conversely, if he begins while dismounted (thus obligated to perform full bows and prostrations) and then mounts, he cannot build; he must start anew, as his iḥrām obligated the full posture and he cannot abandon that without excuse. The text then notes an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require starting over even when descending, with the latter making an exception only if one descended after having completed one rakʿah. The commentary then turns to the prayer on a mount itself, distinguishing between obligatory (farḍ) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers. For farḍ, it is only permissible when one has a legitimate excuse (such as inability to dismount) and is performed with gestures, making the prostration lower than the bowing without placing the head on anything. For nafl, it is permissible absolutely, even without excuse. The text then discusses details about carriages (ʿajalah) and litters (maḥmil), explaining that if the carriage rests partly on the mount, it is treated like praying on the mount; if it is entirely on the ground, it is like praying on a bed and requires full postures. The latter part of the passage addresses a crucial objection: why can a rider descend and build while a sick person who recovers during prayer cannot? The distinction is that the sick person's gesture is a substitute (badal) for the actual pillars, because he is incapable of performing them; when he becomes capable, the substitute falls away and he must restart. The rider's gesture, however, is not a substitute—the Lawgiver permitted it directly even though the rider can potentially perform full postures (e.g., by standing on stirrups). Hence the rider's gesture retains its strength, and descending does not invalidate the prayer's continuity. The passage concludes by noting that this building only applies to supererogatory prayers, as is explicitly stated in al-Hidāyah, and that for obligatory prayers, even a rider who begins on a mount must start over if he descends, because he is capable of full postures from the start.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-īmāʾ): Gesture with the head or body to indicate bowing (rukūʿ) and prostration (sujūd) in prayer when unable to perform full physical movements.
البناء (al-bināʾ): Continuing the prayer from where one left off after an interruption or change of state, without restarting from the beginning.
البدل (al-badal): A substitute or replacement for an integral act of worship (rukn) when the primary act is impossible. In prayer, īmāʾ is a badal for rukūʿ and sujūd for a sick person, but not for a rider.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a person begins a supererogatory prayer while riding a mount and then dismounts, what should he do?
A) He must restart the prayer from the beginning.
B) He may continue (build) from where he left off.
C) His prayer becomes invalid because of the change of state.
D) He must perform the remaining rakʿahs with full postures but does not need to restart.

Key Takeaway
The rider's gesture is not a substitute (badal) but a direct permission (rukhṣah), so descending from a mount during a supererogatory prayer does not break its continuity, and the prayer may be continued.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling of Tarawih: Sunnah, Twenty Rak'ahs, and Congregation
Explains the ruling, number of rak'ahs, and congregation of Tarawih.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih (its legal category, number of rak'ahs, and congregation) and explain how the intra-Hanafi dispute was resolved.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah of twenty rak'ahs performed in congregation after Isha before Witr.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq expands on the ruling of Tarawih prayer, clarifying its status as an emphatic sunnah, its specific number of rak'ahs, and the distinguishing feature of congregation. It also addresses an earlier internal Hanafi disagreement and explains how it was settled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states 'wa sunna fī Ramaḍān 'ishrūna rak'ah' - 'and it is sunnah in Ramadan twenty rak'ahs'. The commentator confirms this is an emphatic sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah).
Note the deliberate use of 'sunna' not 'wajib' or 'fard'.
2
Determine the specifics
The prayer consists of twenty rak'ahs, performed after Isha and before Witr, in congregation. There is a sitting (rest) after every four rak'ahs.
The congregation is a distinguishing feature from other sunnah prayers.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi resolution
The text reports that some early Hanafi scholars doubted whether Tarawih is a sunnah, but the disagreement was cut off by the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa affirming it as sunnah.
This shows how madhhab positions are established through riwāyah and consensus.
4
Understand the term 'Tarawih'
Tarawih is the plural of tarwīḥah, meaning 'a rest'. The name derives from the practice of resting after every four rak'ahs.
The term itself reflects the sunnah of taking a brief pause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وسن في رمضان عشرون ركعة بعد العشاء قبل الوتر وبعده بجماعة والختم مرة بجلسة بعد كل أربع بقدرها بيان لصلاة التراويح وإنما لم يذكرها مع السنن المؤكدة قبل النوافل المطلقة لكثرة شعبها ولاختصاصها بحكم من بين سائر السنن والنوافل وهو الأداء بجماعة. والتراويح جمع ترويحة وهي في الأصل مصدر بمعنى الاستراحة سميت به الأربع ركعات المخصوصة لاستلزامها استراحة بعدها كما هو السنة فيها. وصرح المصنف بأنها سنة وصححه صاحب الهداية والظهيرية وذكر في الخلاصة أن المشايخ اختلفوا في كونها سنة وانقطع الاختلاف برواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها سنة. وذكر في الاختيار أن أبا يوسف قال في النهر : لا حاجة إليه إذا المنتفي إنما هو كونه سجوداً ا هـ فليتأمل قوله : (وقوله من غير عذر) أي قول صاحب الهداية في تعليل المسألة قوله : (فشمل الرجال والنساء) أي خلافاً لما قاله بعض
His saying: (And it is sunnah in Ramadan twenty rakʿahs after Isha before Witr and after it in congregation, and the seal once with a sitting after every four to the extent of it) is an explanation of the Tarawih prayer. He only did not mention it with the emphatic sunnahs before the absolute supererogatory prayers due to the multiplicity of its branches and its specificity with a ruling among all other sunnahs and supererogatory prayers, which is performing it in congregation. Tarawih is the plural of tarwīḥah, which originally is a verbal noun meaning 'rest'; the four specific rakʿahs are named by it because they entail a rest after them, as is the sunnah in them. The author states that it is sunnah, and the author of al-Hidāyah and al-Ẓahīriyyah verified it. And it is mentioned in al-Khulāṣah that the scholars differed concerning it being sunnah, and the difference was cut off by the narration of al-Ḥasan from Abū Ḥanīfah that it is sunnah. And it is mentioned in al-Ikhtiyār that Abū Yūsuf said in al-Nahr: There is no need for it, for what is negated is only its being a prostration. End. So let one consider his saying: (And his saying: without an excuse) is the saying of the author of al-Hidāyah in his reasoning of the issue; his saying: (so it includes men and women) contrary to what some said.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rāʾiq is an expansion probe on the ruling of Tarawih prayers in Ramadan. It begins by quoting the matn phrase: 'And it is sunnah in Ramadan twenty rakʿahs after Isha before Witr and after it in congregation, and the seal once with a sitting after every four to the extent of it.' The commentator explains that this is the explanation of Tarawih prayer. He then clarifies why the author did not include Tarawih among the emphatic sunnahs (sunan muʾakkadah) before the absolute supererogatory prayers: because Tarawih has many branches and is distinguished from all other sunnahs and supererogatory prayers by being performed in congregation. The term 'Tarawih' is the plural of 'tarwīḥah', which originally means 'rest'; the specific four rakʿahs are so named because they entail a rest after them, as is the sunnah. The author of the matn explicitly states that it is a sunnah, and this is confirmed by the author of al-Hidāyah and al-Ẓahīriyyah. The text then notes that in al-Khulāṣah, the early scholars disagreed about whether it is sunnah, but the disagreement was resolved by the narration of al-Ḥasan from Abū Ḥanīfah that it is indeed a sunnah. In al-Ikhtiyār, it is mentioned that Abū Yūsuf said in al-Nahr: 'There is no need for it, for what is negated is only its being a prostration.' The passage then returns to an earlier commentary about the phrase 'without an excuse' from the discussion on prayer on a mount, stating that it is the saying of the author of al-Hidāyah in his reasoning of the issue, and that it includes men and women, contrary to what some said. The passage covers the foundational ruling: Tarawih is a sunnah (not wajib or fard), performed in congregation, consisting of twenty rakʿahs, with a rest (sitting) after every four rakʿahs, and it is performed after Isha and before Witr.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarāwīḥ): Plural of tarwīḥah; the supererogatory night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan, consisting of twenty rakʿahs with a sitting (rest) after every four rakʿahs.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-muʾakkadah): An emphatic sunnah, which is a recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, though not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many rakʿahs constitute the Tarawih prayer, and when is it performed?
A) Eight rakʿahs, performed after Witr.
B) Twenty rakʿahs, performed after Isha and before Witr in congregation.
C) Twelve rakʿahs, performed in congregation after Maghrib.
D) Twenty rakʿahs, performed individually at home.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah of twenty rak'ahs performed in congregation after Isha before Witr, with the ruling confirmed by the Hanafi school through the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa.

Building Prayer After Descending from a Riding Animal: Nafl vs Fard
Explains the condition 'without excuse' and the ruling on building prayer after descending

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building prayer after descending from a riding animal and distinguish between nafl and fard based on the ability to initiate with gestures.

Core Idea
For nafl, a rider may build after descending; for fard, he must restart because he could not have initiated with gestures.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a nuanced ruling in Hanafi fiqh: whether a person who begins prayer on a riding animal can continue without restarting after dismounting. The text establishes that the concession applies only to supererogatory prayers (nafl) and distinguishes the rider from the sick person, grounding the ruling in the ability to initiate prayer with full performance. Through qiyas and refutation of objections, the relied-upon position is that for nafl, building is allowed; for fard, it is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what act is being discussed (building prayer after descending from a mount) and what the ruling is for nafl and fard prayers.
The ruling is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah: building is allowed for nafl but not for fard.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is based on qiyas with the sick person. Identify the asl (sick person), the far (rider), and the illa (ability to initiate with gestures).
The text also refutes a weaker distinction based on quantity of action.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the illa connects the cases: the sick person cannot initiate with gestures when able, so he cannot build; the rider can initiate nafl with gestures while mounted, so he can build.
This shows that the concession of gestures for the rider is not a substitute (badal) but a genuine allowance.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Objections)
The author of al-Nihayah argued that building leads to building the strong upon the weak, similar to the sick person. Understand the objection and the Hanafi response.
The response highlights that the rider's gestures are strong because he could perform actual pillars.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi Tarjih
The relied-upon position is that the distinction based on ability to initiate with gestures is correct. For fard, since one cannot initiate with gestures, building is not allowed.
Imam al-Isbajabi suggested that the sick person might also build in nafl, but the matter is restricted by the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله من غير عذر بيان للواقع لا للاحتراز عن العذر فإن المنقول في الخانية أن المصلي إذا ركب الدابة فسدت صلاته. ورد في غاية البيان تعليل من فرق بينهما بأن النزول عمل قليل والركوب عمل كثير بأنه ممنوع لأنه لو رفع المصلي ووضع على السرج لا يبني مع أن العمل لم يوجد فضلاً عن العمل الكثير والفرق الصحيح ما في الهداية .اهـ. وأورد في النهاية أن القول بالبناء فيما إذا نزل يؤدي إلى بناء القوي على الضعيف وذلك لا يجوز كالمريض إذا صلى بعض صلاته بالإيماء ثم قدر على الأركان لا يجوز له البناء تحرزاً عما قلنا وأجاب بأن الإيماء من المريض دون الإيماء من الراكب لأن الإيماء من المريض بدل عن الأركان والإيماء من الراكب ليس ببدل عنها لأن البدل في العبادات اسم لما يصار إليه عند عجز غيره والمريض أعجزه زه مرضه عن الأركان فكان الإيماء بدلاً عنها والراكب لم يعجزه الركوب عن الأركان لأنه يملك الانتصاب على الركابين فيكون ذلك منه قياماً، وكذلك يمكنه أن يخر راكعاً وساجداً، ومع هذا أطلق الشارع في الإيماء فلا يكون الإيماء بدلاً فكان قوياً في نفسه فلا يؤدي إلى بناء القوي على الضعيف. وفرق في المحيط بوجه آخر هو أن في المريض ليس له أن يفتتح الصلاة بالإيماء مع القدرة على الركوع والسجود فلذلك إذا قدر على ذلك في خلال صلاته لا يبني، أما الراكب هنا له أن يفتتح الصلاة بالايماء على الدابة مع القدرة فالنزول لا يمنعه من البناء. قال في النهاية قلت : وعلى هذا الفرق يجب أن لا يبنى في المكتوبة فيما إذا افتتحها راكباً ثم نزل لأنه ليس له أن يفتتحها بالإيماء على الدابة عند القدرة فلذلك قيد المسألة في الهداية بالتطوع. وذكر الإمام الاسبيجابي أن استقبال المريض فيما إذا صح في خلال صلاته إنما كان في المكتوبة ولا رواية عنهم في التطوع في حق المريض، فاحتمل أن المريض لا يستقبل أيضاً في التطوع فحينئذ لا يحتاج إلى الفرق ويحتمل أنه يستقبل بخلاف الراكب والفرق ما بيناه اهـ . .
And his saying: 'without an excuse' is an explanation of the reality, not to guard against an excuse. For it is transmitted in al-Khaniyyah that if a praying person mounts an animal, his prayer becomes invalid. It was refuted in Ghayat al-Bayan that the reasoning of one who distinguished between them by saying that descending is a small action and mounting is a great action is refuted because if the praying person lifts and places [himself] on the saddle, he does not build, whereas the action has not occurred, let alone a great action. The correct distinction is what is in al-Hidayah. .end quote. And it was raised in al-Nihayah that saying that he builds when he descends leads to building the strong upon the weak, which is not permissible, like the sick person who prays part of his prayer with gestures, then becomes able to perform the pillars; he is not allowed to build, as a precaution against what we said. He answered: the gestures of the sick person are not like the gestures of the rider, because the gestures of the sick person are a substitute for the pillars, and the gestures of the rider are not a substitute for them, because a substitute in acts of worship is a name for what one resorts to due to the inability of something else. The sick person was prevented by his illness from the pillars, so his gestures were a substitute for them. The rider is not prevented by riding from the pillars, because he can stand upright on the stirrups, so that from him is standing. Likewise, he can bow and prostrate while descending. Despite this, the Lawgiver permitted gestures, so the gestures are not a substitute, so it is strong in itself, and does not lead to building the strong upon the weak. And it was distinguished in al-Muhit with another way: that the sick person may not initiate the prayer with gestures while able to bow and prostrate, so when he becomes able during his prayer, he does not build. But the rider here may initiate the prayer with gestures on the animal while able, so descending does not prevent him from building. He said in al-Nihayah: I say: Based on this distinction, one should not build in the obligatory prayer if he initiated it as a rider and then descended, because he may not initiate it with gestures on the animal while able, so the matter was restricted in al-Hidayah to supererogatory prayers. Imam al-Isbajabi mentioned that the sick person's returning (to face the qibla) when he recovers during his prayer was only in obligatory prayers, and there is no narration from them regarding supererogatory prayers for the sick person. So it is possible that the sick person also does not return in supererogatory prayers; then there is no need for the distinction. And it is possible that he returns, unlike the rider, and the distinction is what we explained. End quote.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on whether a person who begins prayer on a riding animal and then descends can continue (build) without restarting. The commentator clarifies the condition 'without excuse' in the matn. The key ruling from al-Hidayah is that for supererogatory (nafl) prayer, if one initiates on a mount with gestures and then descends, he may continue; but for obligatory (fard) prayer, he cannot, because he was able to initiate with full performance. The proof uses istihsan (juristic preference) and qiyas comparing the rider to the sick person. The text discusses various opinions and refutes a weak distinction. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that the distinction is based on the ability to initiate with gestures: the sick person cannot initiate with gestures when able, so he cannot build; the rider can initiate with gestures, so he can build for nafl. This is a nuanced ruling showing the Hanafi method of distinguishing cases based on the nature of the concession.

Key Terms
بناء (bina'): Continuing the same prayer without restarting after an interruption like descending from a mount
إيماء (ima'): Gesturing with the head for bowing and prostrating as a concession when unable to perform actual movements
بدل (badal): A substitute that stands in for the original obligation, like gestures for a sick person

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a person who begins a supererogatory prayer on a riding animal with gestures, then descends, continue the prayer without restarting?
A) Yes, he may build (continue) the prayer.
B) No, he must restart the prayer from the beginning.
C) It is invalid to begin prayer on a riding animal.
D) It depends on whether he had an excuse.

Key Takeaway
For nafl, building after descending is allowed; for fard, it is not, because the rider could not have initiated fard with gestures while able.

Tarawih: Its Ruling, Number, and Evidence
Establishes Tarawih as sunnah mu'akkadah with 20 rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Tarawih in the Hanafi school, explain its number of rak'ahs, and cite the evidence from the practice of the Companions and prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) of 20 rak'ahs, established by the practice of Umar with consensus of the Companions.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes the Tarawih prayer as a sunnah mu'akkadah, clarifying its number and refuting claims of innovation. It explains how the Prophet's initial practice, then left for fear of obligation, was revived by Umar with the agreement of the Companions, forming the basis for the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Tarawih prayer in Ramadan. The Hanafi ruling is that it is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not wajib or mustahabb.
The text explicitly says 'wa hiya sunnah' and confirms it from Abu Hanifah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab with the consensus of the Companions, and the hadith 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs' (Abu Dawud).
The passage also cites the narration from Abu Hanifah via al-Hasan.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet (peace be upon him) initially performed Tarawih and then left it for fear of obligation. This establishes its desirability. Umar's revival with consensus confirms it is sunnah, not innovation.
The hadith of Aishah about 11 rak'ahs does not negate the 20 because the Companions added based on ijtihad.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some earlier Hanafis (e.g., al-Quduri) considered it mustahabb. The Rawafidh (Shia) reject it entirely. The passage refutes both.
Al-Quduri's statement is reinterpreted to refer to congregation, not the prayer itself.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah of 20 rak'ahs, as affirmed by the majority of later Hanafi scholars and the practice of the ummah.
The mufta bihi is for both men and women, in congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وسن في رمضان عشرون ركعة بعد العشاء قبل الوتر وبعده بجماعة والختم مرة بجلسة بعد كل أربع بقدرها بيان لصلاة التراويح وإنما لم يذكرها مع السنن المؤكدة قبل النوافل المطلقة لكثرة شعبها ولاختصاصها بحكم من بين سائر السنن والنوافل وهو الأداء بجماعة. والتراويح جمع ترويحة وهي في الأصل مصدر بمعنى الاستراحة سميت به الأربع ركعات المخصوصة لاستلزامها استراحة بعدها كما هو السنة فيها. وصرح المصنف بأنها سنة وصححه صاحب الهداية والظهيرية وذكر في الخلاصة أن المشايخ اختلفوا في كونها سنة وانقطع الاختلاف برواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنها سنة. وذكر في الاختيار أن أبا يوسف قال في النهر : لا حاجة إليه إذا المنتفي إنما هو كونه سجوداً ا هـ فليتأمل قوله : (وقوله من غير عذر) أي قول صاحب الهداية في تعليل المسألة قوله : (فشمل الرجال والنساء) أي خلافاً لما قاله بعض  كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل ١١٧ تلقاء يجتمع سأل أبا حنيفة عنها وما فعله عمر فقال : التراويح سنة مؤكدة. ولم يتخرجه عمر من نفسه ولم يكن فيه مبتدعاً ولم يأمر به إلا عن أصل لديه وعهد من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : ولا ينافيه قول القدوري أنها مستحبة كما فهمه في الهداية عنه لأنه إنما قال يستحب أن الناس وهو يدل على أن الاجتماع مستحب وليس فيه دلالة على أن التراويح مستحبة. كذا في العناية. وفي شرح منية المصلي : وحكى غير واحد الإجماع على سنيتها. وقد سنها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وندبنا إليها وأقامها في بعض الليالي ثم تركها خشية أن تكتب على أمته كما ثبت ذلك في الصحيحين وغيرهما، ثم وقعت المواظبة عليها في أثناء خلافة عمر رضي الله عنه ووافقه على ذلك عامة الصحابة رضي الله ورد ذلك في السنن، ثم ما زال الناس من ذلك الصدر إلى يومنا هذا على إقامتها من غير نكير وكيف لا وقد ثبت عنه عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين المهديين عضوا عليها بالنواجذ»(١) كما رواه أبو داود. وأطلقه فشمل الرجال والنساء كما صرح به في الخانية والظهيرية وقوله «عشرون ركعة» بيان لكميتها وهو قول الجمهور لما في الموطأ عن يزيد بن رومان قال: كان الناس يقومون في زمن عمر بن الخطاب بثلاث وعشرين ركعة. وعليه عمل الناس شرقاً وغرباً لكن ذكر المحقق في فتح القدير ما حاصله أن الدليل يقتضي أن تكون السنة من العشرين ما فعله منها ثم تركه خشية أن تكتب علينا والباقي مستحب، وقد ثبت أن ذلك كان إحدى عشرة ركعة بالوتر كما ثبت في الصحيحين من حديث عائشة، فإن يكون المسنون على أصول مشايخنا ثمانية منها والمستحب اثنا عشر انتهى . وذكر العلامة الحلبي أن الحكمة في كونها عشرين أن السنن شرعت مكملات للواجبات وهي عشرون بالوتر فكانت التراويح كذلك لتقع المساواة بين المكمل والمكمل انتهى. وأراد بالعشرين أن تكون بعشر تسليمات كما هو المتوارث يسلم على رأس كل ركعتين، فلو صلى الإمام أربعاً بتسليمة ولم يقعد في الثانية الروافض من أنها سنة الرجال فقط كما في الدرر، وعزاه نوح أفندي إلى الكافي ثم قال: لكن المشهور عنهم أنها ليست بسنة أصلاً. قال في البرهان قد اجتمعت الأمة على شرعية التراويح وجوازها ولم ينكرها أحد من أهل القبلة إلا الروافض ا هـ . قوله : (كما ثبت في الصحيحين (الخ أي الحديث السابق عند قول المتن والأفضل فيهما رباع وفيه ما كان يزيد في رمضان ولا غيره على إحدى عشرة ركعة . قال في الفتح : وأما ما روى ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه والطبراني وعند البيهقي من حديث ابن عباس عنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم كان يصلي رمضان عشرين ركعة سوى الوتر، فضعيف بأبي شيبة ابراهيم بن عثمان جد الإمام أبي بكر بن أبي (۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب السنة باب ٥. الترمذي في كتاب العلم باب ١٦ ابن ماجه في كتاب المقدمة باب ٦. الدارمي في كتاب المقدمة باب .١٦ أحمد في مسنده (٤ / ١٢٦، ١٢٧).
His saying: (And it is sunnah in Ramadan: twenty rak'ahs after Isha, before Witr and after it, in congregation, and completing [the Quran] once with a sitting after every four of its measure) is an explanation of the prayer of Tarawih. He only did not mention it with the emphasized sunnahs before the absolute supererogatory prayers because of its many branches and its specificity to a ruling among other sunnahs and nawafil, which is performing it in congregation. Tarawih is the plural of tarwiha, which originally is a verbal noun meaning rest; it is named for the four specific rak'ahs because they necessitate a rest after them, as is the sunnah in them. The author explicitly stated that it is a sunnah, and the author of al-Hidayah and al-Zahiriyyah confirmed it. It was mentioned in al-Khulasah that the mashayikh differed on it being sunnah, and the difference ceased with the narration from Hasan from Abu Hanifah that it is sunnah. And it was mentioned in al-Ikhtiyar that Abu Yusuf said in al-Nahr: 'There is no need for it since the only thing negated is its being a prostration. . .' So ponder his saying. His saying: (And his saying without an excuse) means the saying of the author of al-Hidayah in explaining the issue. His saying: (So it includes men and women) differentiating from what some said . . . [PAGE_117] Kitab al-Salah Bab al-Witr wa al-Nawafil 117 tilaqa yajtama' He asked Abu Hanifah about it and what Umar did, so he said: Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah. Umar did not originate it from himself, nor was he an innovator in it, and he only ordered it based on a source he had and a covenant from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). He said: And the saying of al-Quduri that it is mustahabb does not contradict it, as understood in al-Hidayah from him, because he only said 'it is recommended that people . . .' which indicates that the congregation is recommended, not that Tarawih itself is mustahabb. Thus in al-Inayah. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: More than one has reported consensus on its being sunnah. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) legislated it, encouraged us to it, and performed it some nights, then left it for fear that it would be made obligatory on his ummah, as established in the Sahihayn and others. Then persistence upon it occurred during the caliphate of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him), and the general body of Companions agreed with him on that, and that is reported in the Sunan. Then people from that time to this day have continued to perform it without denial. How could it be otherwise when it is established from him: 'Adhere to my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs; cling to it with your molars' as narrated by Abu Dawud. And he made it general, so it includes men and women, as stated in al-Khaniyyah and al-Zahiriyyah. His saying: 'twenty rak'ahs' is an explanation of its quantity, and it is the saying of the majority because of what is in al-Muwatta from Yazid ibn Ruman who said: The people used to perform qiyam in the time of Umar ibn al-Khattab with twenty-three rak'ahs. And upon this is the practice of people, east and west. But the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir mentioned that the evidence requires that the sunnah from the twenty is what he (peace be upon him) did and then left for fear it would be made obligatory, and the rest is mustahabb. It has been established that that was eleven rak'ahs including witr, as established in the Sahihayn from the hadith of Aishah. So the sunnah according to our mashayikh is eight of them, and the mustahabb is twelve. End quote. Allamah al-Halabi mentioned that the wisdom in its being twenty is that the sunnahs are legislated as complements to the obligatory acts, and they are twenty with witr, so Tarawih is likewise to achieve equality between the complement and the complemented. End quote. By 'twenty' he meant ten taslims, as transmitted, saying salam at the end of every two rak'ahs. If the imam prays four with one taslim and does not sit in the second... the rawafidh say that it is sunnah only for men, as in al-Durar, and attributing it to al-Kafi, then he said: But the well-known from them is that it is not sunnah at all. He said in al-Burhan: The ummah has agreed on the legality of Tarawih and its permissibility, and no one from the people of the qiblah has denied it except the rawafidh. End quote. His saying: (as established in the Sahihayn) meaning the previous hadith at the author's saying 'and the best in them is four' and it contains: 'He never used to increase in Ramadan or otherwise beyond eleven rak'ahs.' Al-Fath said: As for what Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated in his Musannaf, al-Tabarani, and al-Bayhaqi from Ibn Abbas that he (peace be upon him) used to pray twenty rak'ahs in Ramadan besides witr, it is weak due to Abu Shaybah Ibrahim ibn Uthman, the grandfather of Imam Abu Bakr ibn Abi... (1) Narrated by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Sunnah, bab 5; al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Ilm, bab 16; Ibn Majah in Kitab al-Muqaddimah, bab 6; al-Darimi in Kitab al-Muqaddimah, bab 16; Ahmad in his Musnad (4/126-127).
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling establishing the Tarawih prayer. The commentator explains that Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not a mustahabb, despite some opinions. The key evidence is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who performed it for several nights and then stopped for fear of it being made obligatory, and then the consensus of the Companions under Umar's caliphate to continue it in congregation. The number is 20 rak'ahs, based on the practice of the people of Madinah as reported by Yazid ibn Ruman, and this is the majority view. There is a nuance: some scholars distinguish between the sunnah part (8 rak'ahs matching the Prophet's actual practice) and the mustahabb part (12 rak'ahs added by later practice). The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that all 20 rak'ahs are sunnah mu'akkadah, as narrated from Abu Hanifah. The passage also refutes the Rafidah who deny Tarawih or restrict it to men. The ruling is general for men and women.

Key Terms
تراويح (tarawih): Plural of tarwiha; the twenty rak'ahs prayed after Isha in Ramadan with a rest after every four rak'ahs
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphasized recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, leaving it only for fear of obligation
جماعة (jama'ah): Prayer performed in congregation; for Tarawih, it is a sunnah to pray in congregation in the mosque

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the ruling on Tarawih prayer?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
C) It is mustahabb (recommended).
D) It is mubah (permissible).

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah of 20 rak'ahs, rooted in the Prophet's practice and revived by Umar with consensus.

Ruling of Tarawih: Sunnah Mu'akkadah with 20 Rak'ahs
Establishes Tarawih as Sunnah Mu'akkadah with 20 rak'ahs, providing evidence and addressing objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih, explain its evidence, and respond to objections regarding its status and number of rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a confirmed Sunnah, established by the Prophet and revived by Umar, with twenty rak'ahs as the relied-upon practice.

Tarawih is one of the most visible acts of worship in Ramadan, but its legal status and specific number of rak'ahs have been subjects of discussion. This passage from the Hanafi tradition provides a definitive ruling, grounding it in the Prophet's practice, the consensus of the Companions, and the continuous practice of the Ummah. You will learn why the Hanafi school considers it a confirmed Sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) and how it defends the twenty-rak'ah format against objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its legal level
Locate Imam Abu Hanifa's direct statement: 'Tarawih is a confirmed Sunnah.' Understand that 'sunnah mu'akkadah' in Hanafi terminology means a highly emphasized recommended act, not obligatory but consistently performed.
The ruling is not fard or wajib; it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Examine the primary evidence
The passage cites the Prophet's own practice (though he left it fearing obligation), the revival under Umar with companion consensus, and the hadith to adhere to the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs. Also, explicit mention of ijma (consensus) on its legitimacy.
Ijma is a strong proof (qat'i thubut and dalala).
3
Address the apparent contradiction from al-Quduri
Al-Quduri's statement that Tarawih is 'mustahabb' is harmonized: he meant the congregation is mustahabb, not the prayer itself. This shows careful textual reconciliation within the Hanafi school.
This is an example of intra-madhhab harmonization.
4
Analyze the number of rak'ahs: twenty as the majority view
The passage mentions the practice of twenty rak'ahs (plus three witr = twenty-three) during Umar's time, and the wisdom from al-Halabi that it parallels the daily obligatory prayers. Also discussed is a distinction between what the Prophet performed (eleven including witr) as the core sunnah and the additional rak'ahs as mustahabb.
The relied-upon position is twenty rak'ahs.
5
Evaluate the hadith of twenty rak'ahs and respond to weakness claims
The passage defends the hadith of Ibn Abbas (twenty rak'ahs) by noting its strengthening through consensus and the practice of the Companions, despite its chain being criticized.
This shows how practice (amal) can reinforce a weak hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل تلقاء يجتمع سأل أبا حنيفة عنها وما فعله عمر فقال : التراويح سنة مؤكدة. ولم يتخرجه عمر من نفسه ولم يكن فيه مبتدعاً ولم يأمر به إلا عن أصل لديه وعهد من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : ولا ينافيه قول القدوري أنها مستحبة كما فهمه في الهداية عنه لأنه إنما قال يستحب أن الناس وهو يدل على أن الاجتماع مستحب وليس فيه دلالة على أن التراويح مستحبة. كذا في العناية. وفي شرح منية المصلي : وحكى غير واحد الإجماع على سنيتها. وقد سنها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وندبنا إليها وأقامها في بعض الليالي ثم تركها خشية أن تكتب على أمته كما ثبت ذلك في الصحيحين وغيرهما، ثم وقعت المواظبة عليها في أثناء خلافة عمر رضي الله عنه ووافقه على ذلك عامة الصحابة رضي الله ورد ذلك في السنن، ثم ما زال عنهم الناس من ذلك الصدر إلى يومنا هذا على إقامتها من غير نكير وكيف لا وقد ثبت عنه عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين المهديين عضوا عليها بالنواجذ» كما رواه أبو داود. وأطلقه فشمل الرجال والنساء كما صرح به في الخانية والظهيرية وقوله «عشرون ركعة» بيان لكميتها وهو قول الجمهور لما في الموطأ عن يزيد بن رومان قال: كان الناس يقومون في زمن عمر بن الخطاب بثلاث وعشرين ركعة. وعليه عمل الناس شرقاً وغرباً لكن ذكر المحقق في فتح القدير ما حاصله أن الدليل يقتضي أن تكون السنة من العشرين ما فعله منها ثم تركه خشية أن تكتب علينا والباقي مستحب، وقد ثبت أن ذلك كان إحدى عشرة ركعة بالوتر كما ثبت في الصحيحين من حديث عائشة، فإن يكون المسنون على أصول مشايخنا ثمانية منها والمستحب اثنا عشر انتهى . وذكر العلامة الحلبي أن الحكمة في كونها عشرين أن السنن شرعت مكملات للواجبات وهي عشرون بالوتر فكانت التراويح كذلك لتقع المساواة بين المكمل والمكمل انتهى. وأراد بالعشرين أن تكون بعشر تسليمات كما هو المتوارث يسلم على رأس كل ركعتين، فلو صلى الإمام أربعاً بتسليمة ولم يقعد في الثانية الروافض من أنها سنة الرجال فقط كما في الدرر، وعزاه نوح أفندي إلى الكافي ثم قال: لكن المشهور عنهم أنها ليست بسنة أصلاً. قال في البرهان قد اجتمعت الأمة على شرعية التراويح وجوازها ولم ينكرها أحد من أهل القبلة إلا الروافض ا هـ . قوله : (كما ثبت في الصحيحين (الخ أي الحديث السابق عند قول المتن والأفضل فيهما رباع وفيه ما كان يزيد في رمضان ولا غيره على إحدى عشرة ركعة . قال في الفتح : وأما ما روى ابن أبي شيبة في مصنفه والطبراني وعند البيهقي من حديث ابن عباس عنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم كان يصلي رمضان عشرين ركعة سوى الوتر، فضعيف بأبي شيبة ابراهيم بن عثمان جد الإمام أبي بكر بن أبي شيبة متفق على ضعفه مع مخالفته للصحيح ا هـ . قلت : أما مخالفته للصحيح فقد يجاب عنها بأن ما في الصحيح مبني على ما هو الغالب من أحواله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وهذا كان ليلتين فقط ثم تركه عليه الصلاة والسلام فلذا لم تذكره عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها. وأما تضعيف الحديث بمن ذكر فقد يقال : إنه اعتضد بما مر من نقل الإجماع على سنيتها من غير تفصيل مع قول الإمام رحمه الله أن ما فعله عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه لم يتخرجه من تلقاء نفسه ولم يكن فيه مبتدعاً ولم يأمر به إلا عن أصل لديه وعهد من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فتأمل منصفاً
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. It is narrated that someone asked Abu Hanifa about Tarawih and what Umar did, and he said: 'Tarawih is a confirmed Sunnah. Umar did not invent it from himself, nor was he an innovator in it, nor did he command it except based on a foundation he had and a covenant from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him.' He said: 'And this does not contradict al-Quduri's statement that it is mustahabb, as understood by al-Hidayah about him, because he only said that it is mustahabb for people to congregate, which indicates that the congregation is mustahabb, but does not indicate that Tarawih itself is mustahabb.' So it is in al-Inayah. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: 'More than one have reported consensus on its being Sunnah. The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, instituted it, encouraged us to it, and performed it on some nights, then left it fearing that it would be made obligatory upon his Ummah, as established in the Sahihayn and elsewhere. Then regularity in performing it occurred during the caliphate of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and the generality of the Companions agreed with him on that, and that is recorded in the Sunan. Then people from that early period to our day have continued to perform it without disapproval. How could it not be so, when it is established from him: 'Adhere to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs after me, cling to it with your molars,' as narrated by Abu Dawud.' And he made it general, so it includes men and women, as stated explicitly in al-Khaniyyah and al-Zahiriyyah. And his statement 'twenty rak'ahs' is an explanation of its quantity, and it is the view of the majority based on what is in al-Muwatta from Yazid ibn Ruman: 'The people used to pray during the time of Umar ibn al-Khattab with twenty-three rak'ahs.' And the practice of the people, east and west, is upon that. However, the investigator in Fath al-Qadir summarized that evidence requires that the Sunnah from the twenty is what he performed then left for fear it would be written upon us, and the rest is mustahabb. It has been established that that was eleven rak'ahs including Witr, as established in the Sahihayn from the hadith of Aisha. Therefore, according to the principles of our scholars, eight of them are Sunnah and twelve are mustahabb, end. And Allamah al-Halabi mentioned that the wisdom in its being twenty is that the supererogatory prayers are prescribed as completions of the obligatory prayers, and they are twenty with Witr, so Tarawih is likewise to make equality between the completer and the completed, end. And he meant by 'twenty' that it be with ten taslimahs, as is inherited, making taslim at the end of every two rak'ahs. Then if the imam prays four with one taslimah and does not sit in the second, the Rafidah claim that it is only a Sunnah for men as in al-Durar, and Nuh Afandi attributed it to al-Kafi then said: but the well-known from them is that it is not a Sunnah at all. Al-Burhan said: The Ummah has agreed on the legitimacy of Tarawih and its permissibility, and none of the people of the Qibla have denied it except the Rafidah, end. Then his saying (as established in the Sahihayn) meaning the previous hadith at the statement of the text: 'And the best in them is four by four' and in it: 'He did not increase in Ramadan or otherwise beyond eleven rak'ahs.' Al-Fath said: 'As for what Ibn Abi Shayba narrated in his Musannaf, and al-Tabarani and al-Bayhaqi from Ibn Abbas from him, peace be upon him, that he used to pray twenty rak'ahs in Ramadan besides Witr, it is weak due to Abu Shayba Ibrahim ibn Uthman, the grandfather of Imam Abu Bakr ibn Abi Shayba, who is unanimously weak, and it contradicts the authentic report, end.' I say: 'As for its contradiction of the authentic report, it can be answered that what is in the authentic is based on his usual state, and this was only for two nights, then he left it, so Aisha did not mention it. As for the weakening of the hadith by the mentioned person, it can be said that it is strengthened by what has passed of the transmission of consensus on its being Sunnah without distinction, along with the statement of the Imam that what Umar did he did not invent from himself, nor was he an innovator, nor did he command it except from a foundation he had and a covenant from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. So reflect fairly.'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof concerning the legal status of Tarawih prayers and their specific number of rak'ahs. The commentator begins by quoting a question to Imam Abu Hanifa about Tarawih and Umar's practice, to which Abu Hanifa replied that Tarawih is a Sunnah Mu'akkadah (confirmed Sunnah). He asserts that Umar did not innovate this prayer but acted upon a foundation from the Prophet himself. The commentator then addresses a potential objection from al-Quduri's text which might suggest Tarawih is merely mustahabb (recommended). He clarifies that al-Quduri's statement about istihbab refers to the congregation, not the prayer itself. The commentator then cites the consensus (ijma') of the Ummah on the sunnah status of Tarawih, supported by the Prophet's own practice and his encouragement, and notes that he left it only out of fear of it becoming obligatory. The practice was revived and regularized during Umar's caliphate with the agreement of the Companions. The passage also discusses the number of rak'ahs: twenty rak'ahs is the majority view, based on the practice of the people during Umar's time (twenty-three rak'ahs including Witr). The commentator refers to Fath al-Qadir which distinguishes between what the Prophet performed (eleven rak'ahs including Witr) as Sunnah and the additional rak'ahs as mustahabb. He also mentions a wisdom from al-Halabi that the twenty rak'ahs parallel the twenty rak'ahs of the daily obligatory prayers with Witr. The passage ends with a defense of the hadith of twenty rak'ahs narrated by Ibn Abbas, which some consider weak, but the commentator argues it is strengthened by consensus and the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarāwīḥ): The night prayers performed during Ramadan after Isha, consisting of 20 rak'ahs (or more) with taslim after every two rak'ahs.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed Sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended, but which is not obligatory (fard).
الشفع (al-shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in Tarawih, each taslimah marks the end of a shaf' (two rak'ahs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Tarawih according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) It is mustahabb (recommended)
B) It is fard kifayah (communal obligation)
C) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed Sunnah)
D) It is mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a confirmed Sunnah with 20 rak'ahs, supported by ijma and the practice of the Companions.
