Four Rak'ahs with One Taslimah in Tarawih: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validiy and counting of taslimahs in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when four rak'ahs of Tarawih are performed with one taslimah, explain the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on counting taslimahs, and identify when sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Praying four rak'ahs with one taslimah in Tarawih is valid but counts as one taslimah and requires sajdah al-sahw if forgetful.

Tarawih is traditionally prayed in sets of two rak'ahs (shaf'), each concluded with a taslimah. But what if an imam inadvertently or intentionally prays four rak'ahs with a single taslimah? The Hanafi school addresses this scenario with a nuanced dispute. This lesson unpacks the two narrations from the founding imams, the distinction between forgetfulness and intention, and the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base act and the problem
Start by identifying the act under discussion: an imam leads four rak'ahs of Tarawih with only one taslimah, omitting the sitting after the second rak'ah. This contravenes the usual practice of one taslimah per two rak'ahs.
The usual Tarawih structure: 4 rak'ahs → 2 taslimahs; here only 1 taslimah for 4 rak'ahs.
2
Distinguish forgetfulness vs. intention
The text contrasts two scenarios: forgetful (sahw) vs. intentional ('amd). For forgetfulness, there is a possibility of compensation via sajdah al-sahw; for intentional, compensation is weak (da'if).
The leading opinion prefers that sajdah al-sahw only suffices for forgetfulness, not intentional violation.
3
Locate the two narrations (riwayatayn)
From Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, there are two transmitted views: one holding that the prayer is corrupt (fasad), the other holding no corruption (la fasad). The more apparent (azhar) report is that it is not corrupt.
The 'azhar riwayah' is the basis for the fatwa in later texts.
4
Analyse the sub-dispute on counting taslimahs
Assuming validity, scholars differ: Abu al-Layth says the single taslimah counts as two taslimahs, while Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl say it counts as one. The correct (sahih) view, according to al-Zahiriyyah, al-Khaniyyah, and al-Mujtaba, is that it counts as one taslimah.
This sub-dispute affects whether the imam must still perform 19 taslimahs total or only 18 (since one taslimah covers two shaf').
5
Consider the exception: sitting after two
If the imam sits at the end of the second rak'ah (even without taslimah), then the prayer is considered to have two taslimahs – this is the general view and the relied-upon position.
Sitting after two rak'ahs serves as a functional substitute for the missing taslimah, preserving the intended structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم اختلفوا الخ) قال الرملي : أقول على القولين يجب سجود السهو فتأمل ا.هـ. قلت: هذا في السهو، أما العمد فسيأتي أن انجباره بالسجود ضعيف فأظهر الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف عدم الفساد ثم اختلفوا هل تتوب عن تسليمة أو تسليمتين؛ قال أبو الليث : تنوب عن تسليمتين. وقال أبو جعفر وابن الفضل: تنوب عن واحدة وهو الصحيح. كذا في الظهيرية والخانية وفي المجتبي وعليه الفتوى. ولو قعد على رأس الركعتين فالصحيح أنه يجوز عن تسليمتين وهو قول العامة.
His saying: (then they differed etc.) al-Ramli said: I say that on both views, sajdah al-sahw is obligatory, so ponder, end. I said: This relates to forgetfulness; as for intentional, it will come that compensation by sajdah is weak. Then the more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that there is no corruption. Then they differed: does it count as one taslimah or two? Abu al-Layth said: it counts as two. Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl said: it counts as one, and that is the correct view. So it is in al-Zahiriyyah, al-Khaniyyah, and al-Mujtaba, and upon it is the fatwa. If he sat at the end of the two rak'ahs, the correct view is that it is permissible for two taslimahs, and that is the general view.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the imam who prays Tarawih and mistakenly or intentionally combines four rak'ahs into one taslimah without sitting after the second rak'ah. The commentator first notes the opinion of al-Ramli that on both views (whether the prayer is valid or not), sajdah al-sahw is obligatory. However, the author clarifies that this applies to forgetfulness; if intentional, sajdah does not suffice. The main dispute is between two narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the more apparent (azhar al-riwayatayn) is that the prayer is not corrupted (la fasad). Then within that, the scholars differ on whether this single taslimah counts for one taslimah or two. Abu al-Layth holds it counts for two taslimahs, while Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl hold it counts for one, which is considered the correct view and is the basis for fatwa. A further sub-dispute: if the imam merely sits after two rak'ahs but then prays four with one taslimah, the correct view is that it is permissible for two taslimahs, i.e., the sitting rectifies it, and that is the general view.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): A set of two rak'ahs in Tarawih; each shaf' is considered an independent unit.
التسليمة (al-taslīmah): The act of saying 'assalamu alaykum' to end a prayer; in Tarawih, each taslimah typically ends a shaf'.
الروايتين (al-riwāyatayn): The two narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the validity of combining four rak'ahs with one taslimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the Hanafi school, if an imam prays four rak'ahs of Tarawih with one taslimah (without sitting after two), what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and counts as two taslimahs.
C) The prayer is valid but counts as one taslimah, and sajdah al-sahw is required if done forgetfully.
D) The prayer is valid without any need for sajdah.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, praying four rak'ahs of Tarawih with one taslimah is valid but counts as one taslimah, and if done forgetfully, sajdah al-sahw is obligatory; if intentional, the imam is advised to repeat the prayer for caution.

Mistakes and Uncertainty in Tarawih Prayers
Rulings on forgetfulness and uncertainty in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for two common Tarawih errors: uncertainty about the number of taslimahs and the imam's accidental early salam, applying the Hanafi principle that each shaf' is an independent prayer.

Core Idea
Each two-rak'ah pair in Tarawih is an independent prayer; a mistake in one does not necessarily corrupt the others.

Tarawih prayers are performed in pairs (shaf') of two rak'ahs. The Hanafi school treats each pair as a separate prayer for the purposes of errors. This lesson examines two scenarios: when the congregation is uncertain about how many taslimahs they have completed, and when the imam accidentally says salam after one rak'ah. The rulings depend on whether the error breaks the continuity of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of Tarawih
Recognize that Tarawih is performed in sets of two rak'ahs (shaf'), each concluded with a taslimah. Each shaf' is considered an independent prayer.
This independence is key to understanding the rulings below.
2
Scenario 1: Uncertainty about number of taslimahs
If the congregation doubts whether they have prayed nine or ten taslimahs, they should pray an additional taslimah individually (not in congregation) because leading in nafl is disliked except in Tarawih, and adding another congregational pair would be excessive.
The correct view is based on avoiding unnecessary congregational nafl.
3
Scenario 2: Imam accidentally says salam after one rak'ah
If the imam says salam after one rak'ah (i.e., breaks the pair early), there are two views: (a) Scholars of Bukhara: only the first pair is invalid, and he must repeat just that pair. (b) Scholars of Samarkand: the entire Tarawih is invalid because the forgetful salam does not fully exit him from prayer, and subsequent pairs are built on error, causing omission of required sitting after each two rak'ahs.
The passage suggests that if the imam did nothing to break the prayer (like eating), the first view (Bukhara) applies.
4
Trace the legal reasoning
Each shaf' is a separate prayer, so exiting one by mistake does not automatically affect later ones. However, if the imam's mistake is not corrected and he proceeds, his actions in later pairs may be invalid due to continued forgetfulness.
The key is whether the imam's action (salam) removed him from the prayer's sanctity.
5
Note the condition
The ruling in Scenario 2 is conditioned by the type of forgetfulness. If the imam performed an invalidating act (like eating or talking) after the mistake, the first view does not apply.
This condition is derived from the final line of the passage: 'وقيد بالسلام' (it is conditioned by the salam).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والصحيح الخ) قال الرملي : إنما كان كذلك لكراهة الإمامة في النفل في غير التراويح فلما احتمل أنها عشرة وهذه زائدة عليها كان الأفضل كونها فرادى قوله : (ثم صلى ما بقي على وجهها) أي قبل أن يعيد ذلك الشفع قوله : (يقضي الشفع الأول لا غير) أي لأن كل شفع صلاة على حدة وقد خرج من الشفع الأول بشروعه في الشفع الثاني فلا يفسد ما بعد الشفع الأول فلا يلزمه إلا قضاؤه قوله : (عليه قضاء الكل) أي كل التراويح لفسادها كلها لأن ذلك السلام لا يخرجه من حرمة الصلاة لكونه سهواً فإذا قام إلى الشفع الثاني صح شروعه فيه وكان قعوده فيه على الثالثة ، فإذا سلم كان سلامه سهواً بناء على السهو الأول فلم يخرج من ا الصلاة ولا يصح شروعه في الشفع الثالث وحصل قعوده وسلامه فيه على الخامسة سهواً وهكذا إلى آخره الأشفاع فقد ترك القعدة على الركعتين في الأشفاع كلها فتفسد بأسرها. وقيد بالسلام
His saying: (and the correct etc.) al-Ramli said: It is only like that because leading prayer in nafl is discouraged except in Tarawih. When it is possible that they are ten taslimahs and this is extra, then it is better that they pray individually. His saying: (then he prayed what remained in its proper manner) meaning before repeating that pair. His saying: (he makes up only the first pair) meaning because each pair is a separate prayer, and he has exited from the first pair by starting the second, so what comes after the first pair is not invalidated, so he is only obliged to make up that pair. His saying: (he must make up all) meaning all the Tarawih because they are all invalidated, because that salam does not remove him from the sanctity of the prayer due to being forgetful. So when he stands for the second pair, his commencement is valid, and his sitting in it is upon the third pair, then if he says salam, his salam is forgetful based on the first forgetfulness, so he does not exit the prayer, and his commencement of the third pair is not valid, and his sitting and salam in it is upon the fifth pair forgetfully, and so on to the end of the sets. Thus he has omitted the sitting after two rak'ahs in all the pairs, so they are all corrupted. And it is conditioned by the salam.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings (with commentary) on different scenarios during Tarawih prayers. First, regarding uncertainty: if the congregation is unsure whether they have performed nine or ten taslimahs, the correct view is that they should pray an additional taslimah individually (not in congregation) because leading in nafl is disliked except in Tarawih, and since it is possible they have already done ten, adding one more in congregation would be excessive. Second, if the imam accidentally says salam after one rak'ah (in a shaf' pair) and then continues to pray the rest properly, the scholars of Bukhara hold that he only needs to make up the first pair (the one he exited by mistake), because each shaf' is an independent prayer. The scholars of Samarkand, however, hold that he must make up the entire Tarawih, because the initial salam due to forgetfulness did not fully exit him from the prayer; thus when he proceeds to later pairs, his actions are built on a mistake, and he fails to sit correctly after each two rak'ahs, thereby invalidating all pairs. The passage ends by noting that the ruling is conditioned by the salam (i.e., the mistake is only considered if he actually said salam).

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): A unit of two rak'ahs in Tarawih, considered an independent prayer.
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer that may require sajdah al-sahw or affect validity.
القضاء (al-qadā'): Making up a missed or invalidated part of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the congregation is uncertain whether they have prayed nine or ten taslimahs in Tarawih, what is the correct action according to the passage?
A) They should continue with the imam and pray another taslimah in congregation.
B) They should not add any more prayers.
C) They should pray an additional taslimah individually.
D) They should repeat the entire Tarawih.

Key Takeaway
Each two-rak'ah pair in Tarawih is an independent prayer; a mistake in one does not necessarily invalidate the others, but the nature of the error matters.

Ruling on Praying Multiple Rak'ahs with One Taslim and Its Sufficiency
Statements of ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on taslim count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying multiple rak'ahs with one taslim and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sufficiency.

Core Idea
One taslim for multiple rak'ahs is valid; its sufficiency for one or two units depends on whether the worshipper sits after each pair.

This passage addresses a practical question in night prayers like Tarawih: can you perform four rak'ahs with a single salutation? The Hanafi school, based on the Zahir al-Riwayah, affirms the prayer's validity. The debate among later Hanafi scholars focuses on how many units that single taslim completes. Understanding this nuance ensures correct intention and practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
State the fundamental ruling from the apparent narration: praying multiple rak'ahs with one taslim is valid (no invalidity).
From Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
2
Locate the Point of Disagreement
Identify that the dispute is not about validity but about sufficiency: does one taslim count for one shaf' (two rak'ahs) or two shaf' (four rak'ahs)?
Intra-Hanafi difference among later scholars.
3
Contrast the Two Intra-Hanafi Positions
Compare the view of Abu al-Layth (suffices for two) with that of Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl (suffices for one).
The mufta bihi follows Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl.
4
Apply the Exception: Sitting After Two Rak'ahs
Note that if the worshipper sits (performs tashahhud) after every two rak'ahs, then one taslim suffices for two taslims (i.e., counts as two units).
This is the general statement (qawl al-'ammah).
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Outcome)
Understand that without sitting, four rak'ahs with one taslim counts as only one shaf' (two rak'ahs); with sitting, it counts as two shaf' (four rak'ahs). This affects the total count in Tarawih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأظهر الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف عدم الفساد ثم اختلفوا هل تتوب عن تسليمة أو تسليمتين؛ قال أبو الليث : تنوب عن تسليمتين. وقال أبو جعفر وابن الفضل: تنوب عن واحدة وهو الصحيح. كذا في الظهيرية والخانية وفي المجتبي وعليه الفتوى. ولو قعد على رأس الركعتين فالصحيح أنه يجوز عن تسليمتين وهو قول العامة.
The more apparent of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that there is no invalidity. Then they differed: does it suffice for one taslim or two? Abu al-Layth said: it suffices for two. Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl said: it suffices for one, and that is the correct view. Thus in al-Zahiriya and al-Khaniya and in al-Mujtaba, and upon it is the fatwa. If one sat at the end of two rak'ahs, the correct view is that it suffices for two taslims, and it is the general statement.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding praying multiple rak'ahs of night prayers (like Tarawih) with a single taslim (salutation). The two most authoritative narrations from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that such a prayer is valid—it is not invalidated by the single taslim. The disagreement then is whether that single taslim counts as the equivalent of one or two taslims (i.e., does it complete the salutation for one 'shaf' or a pair of rak'ahs, or for two such units?). Abu al-Layth says it suffices for two taslims, meaning it finishes two separate two-rak'ah units. Abu Ja'far and Ibn al-Fadl say it only suffices for one taslim, and this is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position). However, if the worshipper sits after every two rak'ahs (i.e., performs the tashahhud), the correct view is that it counts for two taslims, which is the general position. The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah via the six books.

Key Terms
الشفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; the basic unit of night prayers like Tarawih.
التسليمة (al-taslīmah): The final salutation (salam) that concludes the prayer.
تتوب (tanūbu): Suffices for; stands in place of.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position, how many taslims does a single salutation suffice for if the worshipper sits after every two rak'ahs?
A) One taslim
B) Two taslims
C) None, it invalidates the prayer
D) One taslim for every four rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits multiple rak'ahs with one taslim, but its sufficiency for the count depends on whether the worshipper sits after every two rak'ahs.

Ruling on Doubt in Taslim Count for Tarawih
Statement of the correct ruling with mention of disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a Tarawih congregation doubts the number of taslims and apply the mufta bihi opinion.

Core Idea
Doubt in taslim count is resolved by adding one more taslim individually, not in congregation.

Tarawih is prayed in taslims of two rak'ahs. Sometimes the congregation loses count. This passage from Munyat al-Musalli provides the relied-upon ruling: they should pray one additional taslim individually. Although there was difference of opinion, the correct view according to later Hanafi authorities is to pray it alone.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
Identify that the congregation doubts between nine and ten taslims (i.e., 18 or 20 rak'ahs). This is the specific doubt addressed in the text.
2
Understand the ikhtilaf
Note that there is a difference of opinion: some scholars allowed the extra taslim to be prayed in congregation, but the correct (sahih) view is to pray it individually.
The text explicitly says 'fihi ikhtilaf wa al-sahih... furada'.
3
Apply the ruling
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that each person should pray one more taslim (two rak'ahs) individually, not behind the imam. This is because Tarawih congregation is only for the full 20 rak'ahs; additional nafl should be prayed alone.
The term 'furada' means individually, not in congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي منية المصلي : إذا شكوا أنهم صلوا تسع تسليمات أو عشر تسليمات ففيه اختلاف والصحيح أنهم يصلون بتسليمة أخرى فرادى.
In Munyat al-Musalli: If they doubt that they prayed nine taslims or ten taslims, there is difference, and the correct view is that they pray one more taslim individually.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling for a congregation of Tarawih who are uncertain whether they completed nine or ten taslims (i.e., 18 or 20 rak'ahs). There was a difference of opinion, but the correct and relied-upon position (as per the text) is that they should pray one additional taslim (two rak'ahs) individually, not in congregation. This is because the doubt makes it likely they are short, and adding one individually avoids the problem of imam leading an optional prayer in congregation besides Tarawih. The ruling is from the later fatwa works (Munyat al-Musalli).

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslīmah): A unit of two rak'ahs concluded with salam; equivalent to one shaf' in Tarawih.
فرادى (furādā): Individually, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Ignore the doubt and continue

Key Takeaway
When a Tarawih congregation doubts the count of taslims, the relied-upon solution is to pray one more taslim (two rak'ahs) individually, not in congregation.

Imam's Forgetful Salam After One Rak'ah in Tarawih
Intra-Hanafi dispute on forgetful salam in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the imam's forgetful salam in Tarawih and apply the condition that determines whether only the first shaf' or the entire prayer is repeated.

Core Idea
A forgetful salam in Tarawih does not necessarily invalidate everything—the later rak'ahs may be salvageable depending on whether nullifying acts occurred.

This lesson deals with a specific scenario in Tarawih prayer where the imam forgetfully says salam after just one rak'ah. The Hanafi school has two divergent opinions on what must be repeated—only the first two-rak'ah unit or the entire Tarawih. The key to understanding the practical outcome lies in a crucial condition: whether the imam performed any invalidating act after the mistaken salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The imam says salam after one rak'ah in the first shaf' of Tarawih, forgetfully (sahyan). Then he continues and prays the remaining rak'ahs in the correct manner.
This is the specific situation addressed by the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand.
2
State the dispute
Scholars of Bukhara hold that only the first shaf' (pair of rak'ahs) needs to be repeated. Scholars of Samarkand hold that the entire Tarawih must be repeated.
The difference arises from their view on the effect of the forgetful salam.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Bukhara: each shaf' is independent; the forgetful salam exits the prayer for that unit, but later rak'ahs are valid. Samarkand: the salam was invalid (since it occurred in the middle of the shaf'), so the prayer never ended; the later rak'ahs were built on an invalid foundation.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference based on ta'lil (legal reasoning).
4
Apply the condition
If after the forgetful salam the imam did something that invalidates the prayer (e.g., eating, drinking, speaking), then only the first shaf' is repeated according to both groups. If no invalidating act occurred, the dispute remains.
The condition is cited from al-Dhakhira and al-Khulasa.
5
Determine the practical outcome
In practice, the imam's obligation depends on whether an invalidating act occurred. If yes, he repeats only the first shaf'. If no, the dominant practice (in later Hanafi works) leans toward the Bukhari view, but the Samarkand view is also considered.
No explicit tarjih is given in the passage, but the condition clarifies the borderline case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو سلم الإمام على رأس ركعة ساهياً في الشفع الأول ثم صلى ما بقي على وجهها قال مشايخ بخاري : يقضي الشفع الأول لا غير . وقال مشايخ سمرقند : عليه قضاء الكل. وهذا إذا لم يفعل بعد السلام المذكور شيئاً مما يفسد من أكل أو شرب أو كلام، أما إذا فعل شيئاً من ذلك فليس عليه إلا قضاء الشفع الأول لا غير كما في الذخيرة والخلاصة وغيرهما.
And if the imam said the taslim on the first rak'ah forgetfully in the first shaf', then he prayed what remained in its proper manner, the scholars of Bukhara said: he makes up only the first shaf', nothing else. The scholars of Samarkand said: he must make up all of it. This is if after the said taslim he did not do anything that invalidates, like eating, drinking, or speaking; but if he did something of that, then he is only required to make up the first shaf' only, as in al-Dhakhira, al-Khulasa, etc.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand regarding a situation where the imam leading Tarawih forgetfully gives the taslim after only one rak'ah of the first shaf' (first two-rak'ah unit), then realizes and continues the rest of the Tarawih correctly. The Bukhari scholars say he must only redo that first shaf' (i.e., the 2 rak'ahs he intended but cut short), because each shaf' is an independent unit. The Samarkand scholars say he must repeat the entire Tarawih (all 20 rak'ahs or whatever he had prayed so far) because his forgetful salam did not actually exit him from the prayer, but then his subsequent rak'ahs were built on an invalid foundation, rendering the whole congregation's prayer invalid. However, both views are conditioned on the imam not having done anything invalidating (like eating, drinking, or speaking) after the forgetful salam. If he did such an act, then his prayer is truly terminated, and he only needs to make up that first shaf'. The relied-upon position is not explicitly given here, but the text cites the views.

Key Terms
الشفع الأول (al-shaf' al-awwal): The first pair of rak'ahs in Tarawih.
ساهياً (sāhiyan): Forgetfully, inadvertently.
يقضي (yaqḍī): Makes up, repeats (the prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam forgetfully says salam after one rak'ah and then does something invalidating (like speaking), what must he repeat according to the text?
A) The entire Tarawih
B) Only the first shaf'
C) He does not need to repeat anything
D) He must repeat the last shaf' only

Key Takeaway
In Tarawih, an imam's forgetful salam after one rak'ah requires only the first shaf' to be repeated if an invalidating act occurs; otherwise, there are two valid opinions within the Hanafi school.

Ruling on Praying All Tarawih with One Taslim
Ruling with proof and discussion on validity and dislike of single taslim for all Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on praying all Tarawih with one taslim, distinguishing between validity and karahah, and identify the evidence and grounds for the different views.

Core Idea
Praying all Tarawih with one taslim is valid but disliked because it contradicts the transmitted practice and the principle of karahah for exceeding eight rak'ahs in night prayer.

The Tarawih prayer during Ramadan is a sunnah mu'akkadah, typically performed in pairs with a taslim after every two rak'ahs. However, some have raised the question: what if the imam prays all twenty rak'ahs with a single taslim at the end, while still sitting for tashahhud after every two? This lesson examines the Hanafi debate on the validity and desirability of such a practice, drawing from the commentary of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and other key sources.

Guided Path
1
State the two views
Identify the view of permissibility without karahah (from al-Muhit and Munyat al-Musalli) and the view of karahah (from al-Allama al-Halabi and the commentator).
Both views agree on validity; the dispute is over dislike.
2
Examine the proof for permissibility
Analyze the qiyas argument from al-Muhit: performing all rak'ahs with one taslim is more strenuous (ashaqq) and thus more deserving of permissibility, provided the pillars are complete and sitting occurs every two rak'ahs.
This is a qiyas based on the principle that hardship permits leniency.
3
Analyze the counter-proof for karahah
The commentator counters that the practice contradicts the transmitted practice (al-mutawarith) of the Salaf, and that the general rule for optional night prayer (qiyam al-layl) is that exceeding eight rak'ahs without taslim is disliked.
The transmitted practice is given priority over the qiyas.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., Munyat al-Musalli) assert no karahah, while others (e.g., al-Nisab, Khizanat al-Fatawa) support karahah. The commentator sides with karahah.
This is a legitimate difference within the school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Although al-Muhit's explicit position is permissibility without karahah, the commentator's argument for karahah is based on stronger evidence (mutawarith and general principle). The preferred view for fatwa is karahah tanzihiyyah.
The commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) is a later authority whose view is given weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : لو صلى التراويح كلها بتسليمة واحدة وقد قعد على رأس كل ركعتين فالأصح أنه يجوز عن الكل لأنه قد أكمل الصلاة ولم يخل بشيء من الأركان إلا أنه جمع المتفرق واستدام التحريمة فكان أولى بالجواز لأنه أشق وأتعب للبدن .انتهى وظاهره أنه لا يكره، وقد صرح بعدم الكراهة في منية المصلي، ولا يخفى ما فيه لمخالفته المتوارث مع تصريحهم بكراهة الزيادة على ثمان في مطلق التطوع ليلاً فلأن يكره هنا أولى، فلهذا نقل العلامة الحلبي أن في النصاب وخزانة الفتاوي شيبة متفق على ضعفه مع مخالفته للصحيح ا هـ . قلت : أما مخالفته للصحيح فقد يجاب عنها بأن ما في الصحيح مبني على ما هو الغالب من أحواله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم وهذا كان ليلتين فقط ثم تركه عليه الصلاة والسلام فلذا لم تذكره عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها. وأما تضعيف الحديث بمن ذكر فقد يقال : إنه اعتضد بما مر من نقل الإجماع على سنيتها من غير تفصيل مع قول الإمام رحمه الله أن ما فعله عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه لم يتخرجه من تلقاء نفسه ولم يكن فيه مبتدعاً ولم يأمر به إلا عن أصل لديه وعهد من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فتأمل منصفاً قوله : (ثم اختلفوا الخ) قال الرملي : أقول على القولين يجب سجود السهو فتأمل ا.هـ. قلت: هذا في السهو، أما العمد فسيأتي أن انجباره بالسجود ضعيف قوله : (والصحيح الخ) قال الرملي : إنما كان كذلك لكراهة الإمامة في النفل في غير التراويح فلما احتمل أنها عشرة وهذه زائدة عليها كان الأفضل كونها فرادى قوله : (ثم صلى ما بقي على وجهها) أي قبل أن يعيد ذلك الشفع قوله : (يقضي الشفع الأول لا غير) أي لأن كل شفع صلاة على حدة وقد خرج من الشفع الأول بشروعه في الشفع الثاني فلا يفسد ما بعد الشفع الأول فلا يلزمه إلا قضاؤه قوله : (عليه قضاء الكل) أي كل التراويح لفسادها كلها لأن ذلك السلام لا يخرجه من حرمة الصلاة لكونه سهواً فإذا قام إلى الشفع الثاني صح شروعه فيه وكان قعوده فيه على الثالثة ، فإذا سلم كان سلامه سهواً بناء على السهو الأول فلم يخرج من ا الصلاة ولا يصح شروعه في الشفع الثالث وحصل قعوده وسلامه فيه على الخامسة سهواً وهكذا إلى آخره الأشفاع فقد ترك القعدة على الركعتين في الأشفاع كلها فتفسد بأسرها. وقيد بالسلام أنه ساهياً لأنه لو سلم عمداً لا يلزمه إلا قضاء الشفع الأول إجماعاً، وفهم من التوجيه المذكور أن الحكم مقيد بما إذا لم يتذكر أنه سلم في الأول على رأس الركعة إلى أن أتم التراويح حتى لو علم أنه سها وسلم على ركعة واحدة صح ما صلاه بعد العلم سوى ركعتين لكون سلامه بعدهما عمداً لا سهواً فكان مخرجاً له عن التحريمة وإن كان على وتر فليتأمل كذا في شرح المنية للشيخ ابراهيم الحلبي .
In al-Muhit: If one prayed all the Tarawih with one taslim and sat at the end of every two rak'ahs, the most sound view is that it suffices for all, because he completed the prayer and omitted nothing of the pillars, except that he combined the separate (units) and continued the state of consecration (tahrima), so it is more appropriate for permissibility because it is more strenuous and wearying for the body. End. Its apparent meaning is that it is not disliked (makruh), and (some) explicitly stated there is no dislike in Munyat al-Musalli. But what it contains is not hidden due to its opposition to the transmitted practice (al-mutawarith) along with their explicit statement of karahah for exceeding eight (rak'ahs) in absolute optional prayer at night, so it is more appropriate that it be disliked here. For this reason, al-Allama al-Halabi reported that in al-Nisab and Khizanat al-Fatawa, Shayba is unanimously weak (the hadith) along with its opposition to the authentic (hadith). End. I (the commentator) say: As for its opposition to the authentic, it can be answered by saying that what is in the authentic is based on the predominant of his (the Prophet's) states, and this was only for two nights, then he left it, so 'Aisha did not mention it. As for the weakening of the hadith by the one mentioned, it can be said that it is supported by what has passed of transmission of consensus on its sunnah without detail, along with the statement of the Imam (Abu Hanifa) that what Umar did was not innovated by himself nor was he an innovator, and he only commanded it based on a root with him and a covenant from the Messenger of Allah. Then consider fairly. His statement: 'Then they differed...' al-Ramli said: I say according to the two opinions, prostration of forgetfulness is required. End. I say: This is regarding forgetfulness; as for intentional, it will come that its compensation by prostration is weak. His statement: 'And the correct...' al-Ramli said: It is only so due to the dislike of leading in optional prayer other than Tarawih, so when it is probable that it is ten and this is extra upon it, the preferred is that they be individual. His statement: 'Then he prayed what remained in its proper manner' meaning before repeating that shaf'. His statement: 'He makes up only the first shaf' no more' meaning because each shaf' is a separate prayer, and he exited the first shaf' by starting the second, so what is after the first shaf' is not invalidated, so he is only required to make it up. His statement: 'He must make up all' meaning all the Tarawih because all are invalidated because that taslim does not take him out of the sanctity of the prayer due to being forgetfulness, so when he stands for the second shaf', his starting in it is valid and his sitting in it is on the third, then when he says taslim, his taslim is forgetfulness based on the first forgetfulness, so he does not exit the prayer, and his starting the third shaf' is not valid, and his sitting and taslim in it are on the fifth forgetfully, and so on to the rest of the shaf's, so he left the sitting after two rak'ahs in all the shaf's, so all are invalidated. He conditioned it by the taslim being forgetful because if he did it intentionally, he is only required to make up the first shaf' by consensus. It is understood from the mentioned explanation that the ruling is conditioned on him not having remembered that he had said taslim on the first (rak'ah) until he completed the Tarawih, meaning even if he knew that he erred and said taslim on one rak'ah, that which he prayed after knowing (the error) is valid except two rak'ahs, because his taslim after them is intentional, not forgetful, so it takes him out of the tahrima. And if he is on a witr, let him reflect. Thus in Sharh al-Munya by Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Muhit: if one prays all twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih with a single taslim at the end, but sits after every two rak'ahs (for tashahhud), the most correct view is that it suffices for the entire Tarawih. The reasoning: the worshipper has completed the prayer, not omitted any pillar; he merely combined the separate units and maintained the initial takbir (tahrima). This is actually more strenuous and thus more deserving of permissibility. The apparent meaning is that it is not disliked (makruh), and some explicitly state no karahah. However, the commentator (author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) notes that this contradicts the transmitted practice (al-mutawarith) — the practice of the Companions and early Muslims was to pray Tarawih in separate pairs (shaf'). Moreover, the scholars have stated karahah for exceeding eight rak'ahs in any optional night prayer (qiyam al-layl) without taslim between them. Therefore, it is more appropriate to consider this action disliked. The commentator then discusses a hadith used to support the practice of twenty rak'ahs, noting some weakness but defending it with arguments from consensus and the practice of Umar. The passage then reverts to clarifying earlier points: the need for sajdat al-sahw in some cases, the karahah of leading optional prayer individually, and the detailed reasoning behind the earlier dispute (Bukhari vs. Samarkand) about forgetful salam. The commentator emphasizes that the imam's forgetful salam does not exit the prayer; thus subsequent rak'ahs are performed within the same prayer, leading to missing the sitting after every two rak'ahs in all shaf's, invalidating the whole. Conversely, if he remembered his error later and then continued, his subsequent actions are intentional and he exits the prayer properly. The entire discussion is a critical refinement of the multiple rulings concerning Tarawih arrangement.

Key Terms
التوارث (al-tawāruth): The transmitted practice (of the Salaf), i.e., the continuous practice of the early Muslims.
التحريمة (al-taḥrīmah): The state of consecration initiated by the opening takbir; the ongoing sanctity of the prayer.
الأشفاع (al-ashfā'): Plural of shaf'; pairs of rak'ahs.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs; in Tarawih, each two rak'ahs form a unit (shaf').
متوارث (mutawarith): That which is transmitted from generation to generation; the established practice of the Muslims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, why is praying all Tarawih with one taslim considered disliked?
A) It is invalid
B) It opposes the transmitted practice and the ruling of karahah for exceeding eight rak'ahs in night prayer
C) It is too difficult for the congregation
D) It increases the time of the prayer

Key Takeaway
Praying all Tarawih with a single taslim is valid but disliked (makruh tanzih) because it opposes the transmitted practice and the general ruling on night prayer.

Time for Tarawih and Its Practical Consequences
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on the time for Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on the time for Tarawih, identify the preferred (mufta bihi) view, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to resolve priority conflicts between missed Tarawih units and Witr.

Core Idea
Tarawih's time is disputed within the Hanafi school — the practical consequence affects whether you can pray it after Witr and how to prioritize missed units.

In this lesson, we explore a passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that examines the time for Tarawih prayer. The commentary clarifies three opinions within the Hanafi school, their supporting proofs, and the practical consequences that follow from each view. Understanding this dispute helps you navigate real-life scenarios, such as when to pray missed Tarawih units if Witr is about to begin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions on Tarawih time
Read the passage carefully and list the three views: (1) all night after Isha, (2) between Isha and Witr, (3) after Isha only. Note the scholars who held each view.
The first opinion is attributed to Isma'il al-Zahidi and a group from Bukhara; the second to most Bukhari scholars; the third to the author of Kanz and the majority.
2
Examine the proof (dalil) for each opinion
For each opinion, find the textual evidence cited: (1) because Tarawih is qiyam al-layl; (2) due to the hadith of Ubayy ibn Ka'b; (3) because they were instituted after Isha prayer.
The second opinion's proof is explicitly mentioned as a hadith; the other proofs are more general.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The passage gives specific scenarios: praying Tarawih before Isha, after Witr, and what to do when missing units before Witr. Note how the ruling changes based on the opinion.
The consequence is not just theoretical; it affects daily practice during Ramadan.
4
Apply the preferred opinion to a scenario
According to the mufta bihi (third opinion, after Isha only), determine if Tarawih prayed after Witr counts as Tarawih. Then decide the priority when a person misses a tarwiha and fears missing Witr in congregation.
The third opinion treats the scenario of praying after Witr as valid, so one could make up missed Tarawih after Witr.
5
Recognize the intra-Hanafi nature and the authority of the opinions
Note that all three opinions are within the Hanafi school. The third opinion is considered mufta bihi because it is authenticated in later authoritative works like al-Hidaya and al-Muhit.
This shows how later Hanafi scholars resolved an earlier difference.

Source Text

وقوله بعد العشاء قبل الوتر وبعده» بيان لوقتها وفيه ثلاثة أقوال : الأولى ما اختاره اسمعيل الزاهدي وجماعة من بخاري أن الليل كله وقت لها قبل العشاء وبعده وقبل الوتر وبعده لأنها قيام الليل ولم أر من صححه . الثاني ما قاله عامة مشايخ بخاري : وقتها ما بين العشاء إلى الوتر . وصححه في الخلاصة ورجحه في غاية البيان بأن الحديث ورد . كذلك، وكان أبي رضي الله عنه : يصلي بهم التراويح كذلك. الثالث ما اختاره المصنف وعزاه في الكافي إلى الجمهور وصححه في الهداية والخانية والمحيط لأنها نوافل سنت بعد العشاء. وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر فيما لو صلاها قبل العشاء، فعلى القول الأول هي صلاة التراويح، وعلى الأخيرين لا . وفيما إذا صلاها بعد الوتر فعلى الثاني لا، وعلى الثالث نعم هي صلاة التراويح، وتظهر فيما إذا فاتته ترويحة أو ترويحتان ولو اشتغل بها يفوته الوتر بالجماعة، فعلى الأولى يشتغل بالوتر ثم يصلي ما فاته من التراويح، وعلى الثاني يشتغل بالترويحة الفائتة لأنه لا يمكنه الإتيان بعد الوتر . كذا في الخلاصة. وينبغي أن يكون الثالث كالثاني كما لا يخفى ولو فاتته ترويحة وخاف لو اشتغل بها تفوته متابعة الإمام فمتابعة الإمام أولى . وقد اختلفوا فيما لو تذكر تسليمة بعد الوتر، فقيل لا يصلون بجماعة ، وقيل يصلون بها كما في منية المصلي . وينبغي أن يكون مفرعاً على القول الثاني والثالث. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان ويستحب تأخير التراويح إلى ثلث الليل والأفضل استيعاب أكثر الليل بالتراويح، فإن أخروها إلى ما بعد نصف الليل فالصحيح أم لا بأس به. وإذا ماتت التراويح لا تقضى بجماعة والأصح أنها لا تقضى أصلاً، فإن قضاها وحده كان نفلاً مستحباً لا تروايح كسنة المغرب والعشاء . قوله : (كالثاني) صوابه كالأول كما رأيته في بعض النسخ مصلحاً وما بحثه هو ظاهر قوله في شرح المنية ويبتني على أنها تجوز بعد الوتر أم لا أنه إن فاتته الخ ثم هذا مبني على أن المراد بالحكم المذكور اللزوم كما هو مقتضى التفريع وهو ظاهر قوله لأنه لا يمكنه الإتيان بعد الوتر، أما إن أريد الأولوية فإنه يأتي فيه الخلاف الآتي في أن الأفضل الإتيان بالوتر بالجماعة أم في المنزل كما أشار إليه في شرح المنية، ولكن قد علمت مبني الكلام على اللزوم فهو يؤكد أن الصواب في العبارة ما قلنا لأنه لا لزوم على الأول والثالث قوله : ( وينبغي أن يكون مفرعاً) أي ينبغي أن يكون هذا الخلاف مفرعاً على الخلاف مفرعاً على الخلاف في وقتها فمن قال لا يصلون بجماعة يكون قد بناه على القول الثاني، ومن قال يصلون بها يكون قد بناه على الثالث واستظهر الثاني في شرح المنية قال : لأنه
His statement: 'after Isha, before Witr, and after it' is an explanation of its time, and regarding it there are three statements: The first is what Isma'il al-Zahidi and a group from Bukhara chose: all night is time for it, before Isha and after it, and before Witr and after it, because it is qiyam al-layl; and I have not seen anyone who authenticated this. The second is what most scholars of Bukhara said: its time is between Isha and Witr. And it was authenticated in al-Khulasa and preferred in Ghayat al-Bayan because the hadith came likewise, and Ubayy (ibn Ka'b) used to pray Tarawih with them likewise. The third is what the author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) chose and attributed in al-Kafi to the majority and authenticated in al-Hidaya, al-Khaniya, and al-Muhit, because they are optional prayers that were instituted after Isha. The consequence of the difference appears if one prays it before Isha: according to the first statement it is Tarawih, according to the latter two it is not. And if one prays it after Witr: according to the second it is not, according to the third it is Tarawih. It also appears if one misses one or two tarwihas (units), and if he occupies himself with them he will miss Witr in congregation: according to the first, he should occupy himself with Witr then pray what he missed of Tarawih; according to the second, he should occupy himself with the missed tarwiha because he cannot perform it after Witr. Thus in al-Khulasa. And the third should be like the second as is not hidden. If one misses a tarwiha and fears that if he occupies himself with it he will miss following the imam, then following the imam takes priority. And they differed regarding one who remembers a taslim after Witr: some said they do not pray (it) in congregation; some said they pray it (in congregation) as in Munyat al-Musalli. And it should be derived from the second and third opinions. In Fatawa Qadikhan, it is recommended to delay Tarawih to the third of the night, and the best is to occupy most of the night with Tarawih. If they delay it to after midnight, the correct view is that it is fine. And if Tarawih is missed, it is not performed in congregation, and the most correct view is that it is not performed at all (as qada). If he prays it alone, it is a recommended optional prayer, not Tarawih, like the sunna of Maghrib and Isha. His statement: 'like the second' should be 'like the first' as I saw it corrected in some manuscripts. And his research is apparent from his statement in Sharh al-Munya, and it is based on whether it is permissible after Witr or not, that if he missed it, etc. Then this is based on the meaning of the mentioned ruling being necessity (luzum) as required by the subdivision, and it is apparent from his statement 'because he cannot perform it after Witr.' But if what is intended is priority (awlawiyya), then there comes the following difference: whether it is better to perform Witr in congregation or at home, as indicated in Sharh al-Munya. But you have understood the basis of the speech on necessity, so it confirms that the correct in the expression is what we said, because there is no necessity according to the first and third. His statement: 'and it should be derived' i.e., this difference should be derived from the difference in its time. So the one who says they do not pray it in congregation bases it on the second opinion, and the one who says they pray it bases it on the third. And al-Ramli preferred the second in Sharh al-Munya.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage discusses the time for performing the Tarawih prayer. The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states: 'after Isha, before Witr and after it.' The commentator explains that there are three opinions on the matter: (1) Isma'il al-Zahidi and some Bukhari scholars hold that all night (after Isha prayer) is the time, even before Isha? Actually, 'before Isha' is confusing; but the text says 'all night is time for it, before Isha and after it, and before Witr and after it.' This seems to mean the entire night from after Isha? There is ambiguity. (2) The majority of Bukhari scholars say the time is between Isha and Witr. This is authenticated in al-Khulasa and preferred in Ghayat al-Bayan because the hadith mentions that Ubayy ibn Ka'b led the Tarawih in that time. (3) The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq and the majority (as attributed in al-Kafi) say the time is after Isha (only) because it is a set of optional prayers instituted after Isha. This is authenticated in al-Hidaya, al-Khaniya, and al-Muhit. The practical consequences (thamarah) are then outlined: If one prays Tarawih before Isha (i.e., before the Isha prayer itself?), according to the first opinion it counts as Tarawih, according to the other two it does not. If one prays after Witr, according to the second opinion it does not count, according to the third it does. Additionally, if a person misses some units (tarwiha) and fears that catching up will cause him to miss Witr in congregation, then on the first opinion he should pray Witr first, then make up the missed Tarawih. On the second opinion, he should pray the missed Tarawih immediately because he cannot do so after Witr (since that time is not considered Tarawih time according to the second). The third opinion is treated like the second in this context. The text also covers a scenario where a person remembers a missed taslim (unit) after Witr: some say he should not pray it in congregation; others say he may. This difference is derived from the dispute over the time: those who hold the second opinion (time only between Isha and Witr) would say he cannot pray it after Witr in congregation; those who hold the third opinion (time after Isha including after Witr) would allow it. The passage then cites Fatawa Qadikhan on the recommended time: delay to the third of the night, and it is best to occupy most of the night. It is fine if delayed to after midnight. Finally, regarding qada (making up missed Tarawih): It is not performed in congregation, and the most correct view is that it is not performed at all as qada. If one prays it alone, it counts as a general recommended optional prayer (nafl), not as Tarawih, similar to the sunna of Maghrib and Isha which are not repeated if missed. The commentary ends with a textual correction: the phrase 'like the second' should be 'like the first', and an explanation of the basis for the difference.

Key Terms
التراويح (al-tarāwīḥ): The optional night prayers performed in Ramadan, usually 20 rak'ahs.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamaratu al-khilāf): The practical consequence of a legal difference.
ترويحة (tarwīḥah): A set of four rak'ahs (or two, depending on context) in Tarawih; often used for a pause between units.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All night after Isha
B) Between Isha and Witr
C) After Isha only
D) Before Isha

Key Takeaway
The time for Tarawih is contested within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi is that it should be performed after Isha only, not before or after Witr.

Three Hanafi Opinions on the Time of Tarawih
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tarawih time with practical consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on the time of tarawih, identify the mufta bihi, and apply the thamarah to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
The time of tarawih is disputed; the preferred view restricts it to after isha until witr.

The time for tarawih prayer is not universally agreed upon within the Hanafi school. This lesson from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three distinct positions and explores their practical consequences (thamarat al-ikhtilaf). Understanding these nuances ensures that the prayer is performed correctly and that rulings on missed or conflicting prayers are properly applied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core issue is the time window during which tarawih prayer is validly performed. This affects whether praying before isha or after witr counts as tarawih.
The hukm of tarawih itself (sunnah muakkadah) is not disputed.
2
List the three opinions
Opinion 1 (Ismail al-Zahidi): entire night before and after both isha and witr. Opinion 2 (general mashayikh of Bukhara): between isha and witr. Opinion 3 (author and majority): after isha (and before witr). Note the authentication status of each.
The author notes that the first opinion is not authenticated, while the second and third have support.
3
Examine the thamarah
Analyze practical consequences: (a) praying before isha counts only per opinion 1; (b) praying after witr counts only per opinion 3; (c) if one misses a tarwiha and may miss witr congregation, opinion 1 prioritizes witr, opinion 2 prioritizes the missed tarawih.
The author equates opinion 3 with opinion 2 in this prioritization.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred view is opinion 3, authenticated in al-Hidayah, al-Khaniyya, and al-Muhit, and supported by the majority of later Hanafi authorities.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
5
Apply to a conflict scenario
If a person misses a tarwiha and fears missing witr with the congregation, the mufta bihi (opinion 3) likened to opinion 2 advises prioritizing the missed tarawih (since it cannot be done after witr), but following the imam is superior if the congregation is at risk.
The text also notes that a missed taslima after witr is treated differently by the second and third opinions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله بعد العشاء قبل الوتر وبعده» بيان لوقتها وفيه ثلاثة أقوال : الأولى ما اختاره اسمعيل الزاهدي وجماعة من بخاري أن الليل كله وقت لها قبل العشاء وبعده وقبل الوتر وبعده لأنها قيام الليل ولم أر من صححه . الثاني ما قاله عامة مشايخ بخاري : وقتها ما بين العشاء إلى الوتر . وصححه في الخلاصة ورجحه في غاية البيان بأن الحديث ورد . كذلك، وكان أبي رضي الله عنه : يصلي بهم التراويح كذلك. الثالث ما اختاره المصنف وعزاه في الكافي إلى الجمهور وصححه في الهداية والخانية والمحيط لأنها نوافل سنت بعد العشاء. وثمرة الاختلاف تظهر فيما لو صلاها قبل العشاء، فعلى القول الأول هي صلاة التراويح، وعلى الأخيرين لا . وفيما إذا صلاها بعد الوتر فعلى الثاني لا، وعلى الثالث نعم هي صلاة التراويح، وتظهر فيما إذا فاتته ترويحة أو ترويحتان ولو اشتغل بها يفوته الوتر بالجماعة، فعلى الأولى يشتغل بالوتر ثم يصلي ما فاته من التراويح، وعلى الثاني يشتغل بالترويحة الفائتة لأنه لا يمكنه الإتيان بعد الوتر . كذا في الخلاصة. وينبغي أن يكون الثالث كالثاني كما لا يخفى ولو فاتته ترويحة وخاف لو اشتغل بها تفوته متابعة الإمام فمتابعة الإمام أولى . وقد اختلفوا فيما لو تذكر تسليمة بعد الوتر، فقيل لا يصلون بجماعة ، وقيل يصلون بها كما في منية المصلي . وينبغي أن يكون مفرعاً على القول الثاني والثالث. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان ويستحب تأخير التراويح إلى ثلث الليل والأفضل استيعاب أكثر الليل بالتراويح، فإن أخروها إلى ما بعد نصف الليل فالصحيح أم لا بأس به. وإذا ماتت التراويح لا تقضى بجماعة والأصح أنها لا تقضى أصلاً، فإن قضاها وحده كان نفلاً مستحباً لا تروايح كسنة المغرب والعشاء .
His statement: 'after isha, before witr and after witr' is an explanation of its time. There are three opinions: The first is what Isma'il al-Zahidi and a group from Bukhara chose: the entire night is its time, before isha and after it, and before witr and after it, because it is the night prayer, and I have not seen anyone who authenticated it. The second is what the general mashayikh of Bukhara said: its time is between isha and witr. And it was authenticated in al-Khulasa and preferred in Ghayat al-Bayan because the hadith came similarly, and my father (may Allah be pleased with him) would lead them in tarawih similarly. The third is what the author chose and attributed in al-Kafi to the majority, and authenticated in al-Hidaya, al-Khaniyya, and al-Muhit, because they are supererogatory prayers instituted after isha. The fruit of the difference appears in the case where one prays them before isha: according to the first opinion, they are tarawih prayer; according to the latter two, no. And in the case where one prays them after witr: according to the second, no; according to the third, yes they are tarawih prayer. And it appears in the case where one misses one or two tarwihas, and if he occupies himself with them, he misses witr with the congregation: according to the first, he occupies himself with witr then prays what he missed of tarawih; according to the second, he occupies himself with the missed tarwiha because he cannot perform it after witr. Thus in al-Khulasa. And it is appropriate that the third be like the second, as is not hidden. And if he misses a tarwiha and fears that if he occupies himself with it, he will miss following the imam, then following the imam is more appropriate. And they differed concerning the case where he remembers a salutation after witr: it was said they do not pray in congregation, and it was said they pray it as in Munyat al-Musalli. It is appropriate that this be a branch of the second and third opinions. And in Fatawa Qadikhan: it is recommended to delay tarawih to the last third of the night, and the best is to cover most of the night with tarawih. If they delay it to after midnight, the correct view is that there is no harm. And when the time of tarawih passes, it is not made up in congregation, and the most correct is that it is not made up at all; if he makes it up alone, it becomes a recommended supererogatory prayer, not tarawih, like the sunna of maghrib and isha.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing the time for tarawih prayer. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute presenting three opinions. The first opinion (Ismail al-Zahidi) states the entire night is valid but the author notes no one authenticated it. The second (general mashayikh of Bukhara) limits time to between isha and witr, authenticated by some. The third (author and majority) holds it is after isha (before witr). The practical consequences (thamarah) are then shown: praying before isha counts only per first opinion; after witr counts only per third. The passage also addresses secondary issues: if one misses a tarwiha and might miss witr with congregation, the first opinion prioritizes witr, the second prioritizes the missed tarawih (as it cannot be done after witr). The third is likened to the second. Following the imam takes precedence over a missed tarwiha if congregation is at risk. Differences about praying a missed taslima after witr are tied to the time opinions. Qadikhan's fatwa recommends delaying tarawih to the last third of night. The final ruling: missed tarawih is not made up in congregation; if one prays alone, it is a regular nafl, not tarawih.

Key Terms
ثمرة الاختلاف (thamarat al-ikhtilaf): Practical legal consequences arising from differing scholarly opinions on a ruling.
تراويح (tarawih): The night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs (in the Hanafi school).
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after isha, wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (the third opinion), if a person prays tarawih after witr, what is the ruling?
A) It counts as tarawih prayer.
B) It does not count as tarawih prayer.
C) It counts only if he intended tarawih.
D) It is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi for tarawih time is after isha (and before witr), and this difference yields distinct practical guidelines for prioritization and validity.

Congregation in Tarawih: Three Hanafi Opinions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tarawih congregation ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on tarawih congregation, explain their proofs, and apply the sunnah kifaya ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
Tarawih congregation is sunnah kifaya: if some pray in congregation, others may pray alone without sin.

This lesson unpacks a key intra-Hanafi dispute: is tarawih congregation an individual sunnah (sunnat al-ayn) or a collective sunnah (sunnat al-kifaya)? The answer determines whether praying individually is blameworthy. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents three views, their evidence, and the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the first opinion
Identify the first opinion: congregation is sunnat al-ayn. What is its ruling and evidence?
The author of Kanz and Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani held this view based on the Prophet's practice.
2
State the second opinion
Identify the second opinion (al-Tahawi, Abu Yusuf): praying at home is recommended except for leading scholars. What is its evidence?
Based on the hadith 'The best prayer is in one's home except the obligatory.'
3
State the third opinion
Identify the third opinion (majority, al-Hidayah): congregation is sunnat al-kifaya. What is its ruling?
If some perform congregation, others are not blameworthy; only if all abandon it do they sin.
4
Analyze the response to the second opinion
How does the passage respond to al-Tahawi's hadith? What is the exemption?
Qiyam Ramadan is exempted from the hadith due to the Prophet's and Caliphs' practice.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the opinions? Which is mufta bihi?
The third opinion is preferred; the practical consequence: praying alone is not sinful if congregation exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله «بجماعة» متعلق بسن بيان لكون الجماعة سنة فيها وفيها ثلاثة أقوال : الأول ما اختاره المصنف أنه سنة على الأعيان حتى إن من صلى التراويح منفرداً فقد أساء لتركه السنة، وإن صليت في المساجد وبه كان يفتي ظهير الدين المرغيناني لصلاته عليه السلام إياها بالجماعة وبيان العذر في تركها الثاني ما اختاره الطحاوي في مختصره حيث قال : يستحب أن يصلي التراويح في بيته إلا أن يكون فقيهاً عظيماً يقتدي به فيكون في حضوره ترغيب لغيره وفي امتناعه تقليل الجماعة مستدلاً بحديث أفضل صلاة المرء في بيته إلا المكتوبة»(۱) وهو رواية عن أبي يوسف كما في الكافي. الثالث ما صححه في المحيط والخانية واختاره في الهداية وهو قول أكثر المشايخ على ما في الذخيرة وقول الجمهور على ما في الكافي أن إقامتها بالجماعة سنة على الكفاية حتى لو ترك أهل المسجد كلهم الجماعة فقد أساؤوا وأثموا. وإن أقيمت التراويح بالجماعة في المسجد وتخلف عنها أفراد الناس وصلى في بيته لم يكن مسيئاً لأن أفراد الصحابة يروى عنهم التخلف كابن عمر على ما رواه الطحاوي. والجواب عن دليل الطحاوي أن قيام رمضان مستثنى من الحديث لفعله إياه في المسجد ثم فعل الخلفاء الراشدين بعده إذ لا يختار المفضول ويجمعون عليه. وأما من تخلف من الصحابة فإما لعذر أو لأنه أفضل في اجتهاده وهو معارض بما هو أولى منه وهو اتفاق الجم الغفير على خلافه . فالحاصل أن القول الأول والثالث اتفقا على أفضليتها وإنما الكلام في الإساءة بالترك من البعض. وأطلق المصنف في الجماعة ولم يقيدها بالمسجد لما في الكافي والصحيح أن للجماعة في بيته فضيلة وللجماعة في المسجد فضيلة أخرى فهو حاز إحدى الفضيلتين وترك الفضيلة الأخرى انتهى. وفي الخلاصة : إذا صلى الترويحة الواحدة إمامان كل إمام ركعتين اختلف المشايخ والصحيح أنه لا يستحب ولكن كل ترويحة يؤديها إمام واحد إمام يصلي التراويح في مسجدين كل مسجد على وجه الكمال لا يجوز لأنه لا يتكرر، ولو اقتدى بالإمام في التراويح وهو قد صلى مرة لا بأس به ويكون هذا اقتداء المتطوع بمن يصلي السنة، ولو صلوا التراويح ثم أرادوا أن يصلوا ثانياً يصلون فرادى انتهى
His statement: 'in congregation' is attached to 'sunna' — an explanation that congregation in it is sunna. There are three opinions: The first is what the author chose: that it is sunna on individuals (ayn), such that whoever prays tarawih alone has acted wrongfully by leaving the sunna, even if it is prayed in the mosques. And this was the fatwa of Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani, because of his (peace be upon him) praying it in congregation and the explanation of the excuse for leaving it. The second is what al-Tahawi chose in his Mukhtasar, where he said: it is recommended to pray tarawih in one's home unless he is a great jurist who is followed, so his presence encourages others and his absence reduces the congregation, using as evidence the hadith 'The best prayer of a person is in his home except the obligatory prayer.' And this is a narration from Abu Yusuf as in al-Kafi. The third is what was authenticated in al-Muhit and al-Khaniyya and chosen in al-Hidaya, and it is the saying of most mashayikh according to al-Dhakhira and the saying of the majority according to al-Kafi: that performing it in congregation is sunna on sufficiency (kifaya), such that if all the people of the mosque leave the congregation, they have acted wrongfully and sinned. And if tarawih is performed in congregation in the mosque and some individuals stay behind and pray in their homes, they are not acting wrongfully because individuals among the Companions are narrated to have stayed behind, like Ibn Umar, as al-Tahawi narrated. The response to al-Tahawi's evidence is that qiyam Ramadan is exempted from the hadith because of his (peace be upon him) doing it in the mosque, and then the Rightly Guided Caliphs after him, for they do not choose the inferior and they agreed upon it. As for those Companions who stayed behind, it was either due to an excuse or because it was better in their ijtihad, and this is opposed by what is more appropriate: the agreement of the great multitude upon the opposite. So the conclusion is that the first and third opinions agree on its superiority; the discussion is only about wrongdoing by leaving it from some. And the author used the term 'congregation' without restricting it to the mosque, because in al-Kafi: the correct view is that congregation in one's home has a virtue and congregation in the mosque has another virtue, so he obtains one virtue and leaves the other virtue. End. And in al-Khulasa: If one tarwiha is led by two imams, each imam leading two rak'ahs, the mashayikh differed; the correct view is that it is not recommended. Rather, each tarwiha is performed by one imam. An imam leading tarawih in two mosques, each mosque in a complete manner, is not permissible because it does not repeat. And if one follows an imam in tarawih while he has already prayed once, there is no harm, and this is the following of a volunteer (mutatawwi') by one who prays the sunna. And if they pray tarawih and then want to pray a second time, they pray individually. End.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, focusing on whether tarawih should be prayed in congregation or individually. Three Hanafi opinions are detailed: First (author's choice): congregation is sunnah ayn, meaning it is an individual sunnah such that leaving it without excuse is blameworthy. This is supported by the Prophet's practice and the practice of the caliphs. Second (al-Tahawi, also a narration from Abu Yusuf): it is mustahabb (recommended) to pray at home, except for a leading scholar whose presence encourages others. The evidence is the hadith that the best prayer is at home except fard. Third (authenticated by al-Hidayah and others): congregation is sunnah kifaya (sufficient) — if all avoid it, they sin; but if some perform it, others may pray alone without blame. The author then discusses the response to al-Tahawi's hadith: qiyam Ramadan is an exception because the Prophet himself led it in the mosque. The passage also includes rulings: congregation at home or mosque both have virtue; one imam should lead all rak'ahs; following an imam after having prayed is allowed; repeating tarawih in congregation is not recommended.

Key Terms
سنة العين (sunnat al-ayn): A sunnah that is individually obligatory, such that leaving it without excuse is blameworthy.
سنة الكفاية (sunnat al-kifaya): A sunnah that is collectively obligatory; if some perform it, others are absolved of blame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the third and preferred opinion (sunnah kifaya), what is the ruling if some individuals pray tarawih at home while the congregation is established in the mosque?
A) They have sinned.
B) They are not sinful because the sunnah is fulfilled by the congregation.
C) Their prayer is invalid.
D) They must repeat it in congregation.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that tarawih congregation is sunnah kifaya: if it is established in the mosque, individuals may pray alone without sin.

Completing the Quran Once in Tarawih is Sunnah
States the sunnah of completing the Quran once during tarawih and the recommended night for completion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing the Quran in tarawih and identify the recommended night for completion.

Core Idea
Completing the Quran once during tarawih is sunnah, not obligatory; completion on the 27th night is recommended.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on reciting the Quran during tarawih prayers. While tarawih itself is sunnah muakkadah, the specific act of completing the entire Quran once over the month is also sunnah. There is a difference of opinion, but the majority of Hanafi scholars hold this view. Understanding this helps avoid the misconception that it is obligatory, and it provides guidance for those leading tarawih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses 'completing the Quran' (khatm) during tarawih. Identify that the ruling given is 'sunnah' (recommended) and not wajib or fard.
The author uses the term 'sunnah' explicitly.
2
Note the difference of opinion
The passage acknowledges ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) but states that the majority (جمهور) hold that completing once is sunnah. Recognize that this is the relied-upon view.
The commentator does not detail the opposing view, but it exists.
3
Understand the reason for not omitting
The passage says 'so it should not be omitted due to laziness of the people.' This implies that the sunnah is established and should be adhered to, even if some are negligent.
This emphasizes the importance of maintaining the practice.
4
Identify the recommended night
The passage recommends completing the khatm on the 27th night of Ramadan, due to the strong probability that it is Laylat al-Qadr (the Night of Decree).
This is a practical recommendation, not a requirement.
5
Recognize the virtue of doing more
The passage states that completing twice is a virtue (فضيلة), but it is not the sunnah. This shows that additional khatm is praiseworthy but not the ideal practice.
Once is the sunnah; more is extra reward.

And his statement: 'and completing [the Quran] once' is coordinated with 'twenty' — an explanation of the sunnah of recitation in it. And he completes it on the twenty-seventh night because of the many reports that it is Laylat al-Qadr. And twice is a virtue.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This brief passage addresses the recitation during tarawih. The author of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states that completing the Quran once during the month is sunnah. The commentator explains that there is difference, but the majority hold it sunnah to complete once. It should not be neglected due to people's laziness. It is recommended to complete on the 27th night, as it is most likely Laylat al-Qadr. Completing twice is considered a virtue but not required.

Key Terms
ختم (khatm): The act of reciting the entire Quran, typically over the month of Ramadan in tarawih prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is wajib.

D) It is optional with no preference.

Key Takeaway
Completing the Quran once in tarawih is sunnah; it is not obligatory and should not be neglected due to laziness. Completion on the 27th night is recommended.

Three Opinions on Tarawih Congregation
Explains three intra-Hanafi opinions on Tarawih congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi opinions on Tarawih congregation, explain the proof for each, and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
Tarawih congregation is sunnah kifayah; blame falls only if everyone abandons it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about whether praying Tarawih in congregation is sunnah 'ayn (individual), sunnah kifayah (communal), or merely recommended at home. Understanding these differences is crucial for knowing when one is blameworthy for praying alone. The majority view, adopted in authoritative texts like al-Hidayah, holds it as sunnah kifayah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position variants
Identify that there are three opinions within the Hanafi school on this issue. List them: sunnah 'ayn, recommended at home, and sunnah kifayah.
These variants show the range of ijtihad within a single madhhab.
2
Analyze the first opinion and its proof
Examine the opinion of the author of Kanz (sunnah 'ayn) and the evidence: the Prophet's practice of praying Tarawih in congregation. Note that this view makes praying alone sinful.
Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani gave fatwa on this view.
3
Analyze the second opinion and its proof
Examine al-Tahawi's opinion (recommended at home) and the hadith 'The best prayer is in one's home.' Also note this is narrated from Abu Yusuf.
This opinion prioritizes home prayer over congregational Tarawih.
4
Analyze the third opinion and its proof
Examine the majority opinion (sunnah kifayah) and its support: the Prophet's practice and the consensus of the caliphs. Understand that blame only falls if all abandon congregation.
This is the view adopted in al-Hidayah, al-Muhit, and al-Khaniyah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify that the relied-upon position is the third opinion (sunnah kifayah) because it is affirmed by the majority of mashayikh and aligns with the collective practice.
The author of Kanz may have intended the first, but the commentary clarifies the third is operative.

His statement 'in congregation' is attached to 'is sunnah' as an explanation that congregation is sunnah in it. There are three opinions: First: what the author chose, that it is sunnah 'ayn (individual sunnah), such that whoever prays Tarawih alone has done wrong by leaving the sunnah, even if it is prayed in the mosques. This was the fatwa of Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani, due to the Prophet's praying it in congregation and the excuse for leaving it. Second: what al-Tahawi chose in his Mukhtasar, where he said: It is recommended to pray Tarawih at home unless one is a great jurist followed by others, so his presence encourages others and his absence reduces the congregation, citing the hadith 'The best prayer of a person in his home is the obligatory prayer' (1) and it is a narration from Abu Yusuf as in al-Kafi. Third: what was declared correct in al-Muhit and al-Khaniyah, chosen by al-Hidayah, and it is the saying of the majority of the mashayikh as in al-Dhakhirah, and the saying of the general public as in al-Kafi: that performing it in congregation is sunnah kifayah (sufficiency sunnah), such that if all the people of the mosque abandon the congregation, they have done wrong and sinned. If Tarawih is established in congregation in the mosque and some individuals lag behind and pray at home, they are not wrong, because some Companions are reported to have lagged behind, like Ibn 'Umar as narrated by al-Tahawi. The response to al-Tahawi's evidence is that the night prayer of Ramadan is excepted from the hadith because the Prophet performed it in the mosque, and then the Rightly Guided Caliphs after him—since they do not choose the inferior and agreed upon it. As for those Companions who lagged behind, it was either due to an excuse or because they considered it better in their ijtihad, and it is opposed by what is more appropriate: the agreement of a large group against it. So the result is that the first and third opinions agree on its superiority, and the discussion is only about wrongdoing by some leaving. The author made 'congregation' absolute and did not restrict it to the mosque because in al-Kafi and Sahih, congregation at home has a virtue, and congregation in the mosque has another virtue. So he achieves one virtue and leaves the other virtue, end. In al-Khulasah: If one tarwihah is led by two imams, each leading two rak'ahs, the mashayikh differed, and the correct is that it is not recommended, rather each tarwihah should be led by one imam. An imam leading Tarawih in two mosques is not permissible because it does not repeat. If one follows an imam in Tarawih while having already prayed it once, there is no harm, and this is the following of a supererogatory prayer by one who prays the sunnah. If they pray Tarawih and then wish to pray a second time, they pray individually, end. (1) Narrated by al-Bukhari, al-Tirmidhi, al-Muwatta, Ahmad. Based on the chosen opinion regarding its time, and from this you know the point of his restricting to the third without also mentioning the first with it, due to what passed that no one corrected it. So apparently this opinion is based only on the third, even if its basis on the first is correct. Reflect on his statement: 'It is an apposition to twenty', meaning it is nominative, and the apparent is genitive as an apposition to 'congregation'.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is an expansion by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling of praying Tarawih in congregation. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that congregation is sunnah, and the commentary clarifies the disagreement within the Hanafi school. Three opinions are presented: (1) The first opinion, held by the author of Kanz, considers it sunnah 'ayn—an individual sunnah such that leaving it without excuse is blameworthy. (2) The second opinion, from al-Tahawi and narrated from Abu Yusuf, considers it better to pray at home except for leading scholars. (3) The third and relied-upon opinion, affirmed by al-Hidayah and the majority, holds it to be sunnah kifayah—a communal sunnah so that if sufficient people perform it, others are not blameworthy. The text then provides the proofs and responses, settling on the third opinion as the basis for the author's wording. Additional rulings include leading multiple mosques and following an imam after having prayed. The footnote gives the hadith source. The final remark explains why the author of Kanz only mentioned the third opinion, though the first could also be supported, but the third is the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
سنة على الأعيان (sunnah 'ala al-a'yan): An individual sunnah; leaving it is blameworthy without excuse. The first opinion considers Tarawih congregation as such.
سنة على الكفاية (sunnah 'ala al-kifayah): A communal sunnah; if sufficient people perform it, others are not blameworthy for leaving it. The relied-upon opinion for Tarawih congregation.
التراويح (al-tarawih): The night prayers of Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs, performed in congregation as sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) regarding Tarawih congregation according to al-Hidayah and the majority?
A) Sunnah 'ayn – every individual must pray in congregation.
B) Sunnah kifayah – enough people must pray in congregation to remove blame from others.
C) Mustahabb to pray at home, except for scholars.
D) Wajib – congregation is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih congregation is a communal sunnah (sunnah kifayah) according to the relied-upon Hanafi view, not an individual obligation.
