Completion (Khatm) of the Quran During Tarawih
Sunnah of khatm with practical exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on completing the Quran during Tarawih and identify when lighter recitation is preferred over completing the entire Quran.

Core Idea
Completing the Quran once is sunnah, but avoiding hardship for the congregation takes precedence.

In Tarawih prayers, the imam's recitation is meant to be spiritually uplifting. The majority of Hanafi scholars hold that completing the entire Quran once over Ramadan is the sunnah. However, if lengthy recitation causes people to leave or lose their focus, it is permissible to shorten the recitation. This lesson examines the evidence, the conditions, and the practical ruling followed by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is completing the entire Quran (khatm) during Tarawih prayers over the month of Ramadan. The Hanafi school rules this as sunnah (recommended), not wajib or fard.
The reward is great, but the imam is not sinning if he does not complete it due to practical reasons.
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
The primary evidence comes from reports that the Night of Qadr is often on the 27th, and that completing by that night is virtuous. Additionally, a logical argument (istidlal) is made: 600 rak'ahs of Tarawih over the month and 6000 verses of the Quran imply 10 verses per rak'ah to complete.
The sources cited are al-Hidayah, al-Muhit, and Mukhtarat al-Nawazil.
3
Understand the contravening consideration: tanfir (aversion)
Avoiding tanfir (making people dislike the prayer) is a key principle. If completing the Quran requires very long recitations that tire or annoy the congregation, the imam may shorten the recitation to keep the people engaged.
This is based on the principle that 'increasing the congregation is better than lengthening the recitation.'
4
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi) today
Later Hanafi authorities, given the condition of people in later times, chose the lightest option: reciting short surahs like al-Takathur and al-Ikhlas so that people do not become weary. The imam may also leave a mosque that insists on lengthy khatm.
This is reflected in the practice of many contemporary imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله والختم مرة» معطوف على «عشرون» بيان لسنة القراءة فيها وفيه اختلاف والجمهور على أن السنة الختم مرة فلا يترك لكسل القوم، ويختم في الليلة السابع والعشرين لكثرة الأخبار أنها ليلة القدر، ومرتين فضيلة، وثلاث مرات في كل عشر مرة أفضل كذا في الكافي. وذكر في المحيط والاختيار أن الأفضل أن يقرأ فيها مقدار ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفير القوم في زماننا لأن تكثير الجمع أفضل من تطويل القراءة. وفي المجتبي والمتأخرون كانوا يفتون في زماننا بثلاث آيات قصاراً وآية طويلة حتى لا يمل القوم ولا يلزم تعطيلها وهذا حسن، فإن الحسن روى عن أبي حنيفة أنه هذا إن قرأ في المكتوبة بعد الفاتحة ثلاث آيات فقد أحسن ولم يسيء في المكتوبة فما ظنك في غيرها اهـ. وفي التجنيس : ثم بعضهم اعتادوا قراءة «قل هو الله أحد» في كل ركعة وبعضهم اختاروا قراءة سورة الفيل إلى آخر القرآن وهذا حسن لأنه لا يشتبه عليه عدد الركعات ولا يشتغل قلبه بحفظها فيتفرغ للتدبر والتفكر ا.هـ. وصرح في الهداية بأن أكثر المشايخ على أن السنة فيها الختم . وفي مختارات النوازل أنه يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات وهو الصحيح لأن السنة فيها الختم لأن جميع عدد الركعات في جميع الشهر ستمائة ركعة وجيمع آيات القرآن ستة آلاف ا.هـ. ونص في الخانية على أنه الصحيح. وفي فتح القدير وغيره: وإذا كان إمام مسجد حيه لا يختم فله أن يترك إلى غيره. فالحاصل أن المصحح في المذهب أن الختم سنة لكن لا يلزم منه عدم تركه إذا لزم منه تنفير القوم وتعطيل كثير من المساجد خصوصاً في زماننا، فالظاهر اختيار الأخف على القوم كما تفعله الأئمة في زماننا من بداءتهم بقراءة سورة التكاثر في الركعة الأولى وبقراءتهم سورة الأخلاص في الثانية إلى أن تكون قراءتهم في الركعة التاسعة عشرة سورة «تبت» وفي العشرين سورة الأخلاص وليس فيه كراهة في الشفع الأولى من الترويحة الأخيرة بسبب الفصل بين الركعتين بسورة واحدة لأنه خاص بالفرائض كما هو ظاهر الخلاصة وغيرها إلا أنه قد زاد بعض الأئمة من فعلها على هذا الوجه منكرات من هذرمة القراءة وعدم الطمأنينة في الركوع والسجود وفيما بينهما وفيما بين السجدتين اشتمالها على ترك الثناء والتعوذ والبسملة في أول كل شفع وترك مع الاستراحة فيما بين كل ترويحتين . وفي الخلاصة : والأفضل التعديل في القراءة بين التسليمات كذا روي عن أبي حنيفة، فإن فضل البعض على البعض في القراءة لا بأس به. أما التسليمة الواحدة إن فضل الثانية على الأولى لا شك أنه لا يستحب، وإن فضل الأولى على الثانية على الخلاف في الفرض . الإمام إذا فرغ من التشهد في التراويح إن علم أن الزيادة على قدر التشهد لا تثفل يأتي بالدعوات، وإن علم أنها تثقل يقتصر على الصلاة لأن الصلاة فرض عند الشافي فيحتاط وعلله في فتح القدير بأن الصلاة فرض أو سنة ولا تترك السنن للجماعات اهـ. ليكون نصاً في سنية الختم في الصلاة قوله : (وليس فيه كراهة الشفع الأول من الترويحة الأخيرة) قال الرملي : لقراءته في الركعة الأولى منه النصر وفي الثانية منه بالإخلاص وفيه فصل بسورة «تبت»
His statement 'and completing once' is an apposition to 'twenty', an explanation of the sunnah of recitation in it. There is disagreement, and the majority are of the view that the sunnah is to complete once, and it should not be abandoned due to the laziness of the people. Completion is done on the 27th night due to many reports that it is the Night of Qadr. Twice is a virtue, and three times is better, once every ten nights, as stated in al-Kafi. It is mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar that the best is to recite an amount that does not cause aversion (tanfir) among the people in our time, because increasing the congregation is better than lengthening the recitation. In al-Mujtaba and al-Muta'akhkhirun, they used to give fatwa in our time for three short verses and one long verse so that the people do not tire and that it is not necessary to abandon it. This is good, because al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that if one recites three verses after al-Fatiha in the obligatory prayer, he has done well and not done wrong—so what do you think in other than it? End. In al-Tajnis: Some people are accustomed to reciting 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' in every rak'ah, and some choose to recite Surat al-Fil to the end of the Quran, and this is good because the number of rak'ahs is not confused and his heart is not occupied with memorizing it, so he is free for contemplation and reflection, end. It is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah that most of the mashayikh hold that the sunnah is to complete the Quran. In Mukhtarat al-Nawazil: He recites ten verses in every rak'ah, and this is the correct view because the sunnah is to complete, because the total number of rak'ahs in the whole month is six hundred, and the total verses of the Quran are six thousand, end. It is stated in al-Khaniyah that it is correct. In Fath al-Qadir and others: If the imam of his neighborhood does not complete the Quran, he may leave to another. So the result is that the relied-upon view in the madhhab is that completing is sunnah, but does not necessitate not leaving it if it causes aversion to the people and disabling many mosques, especially in our time. So the apparent is to choose the lighter option for the people, as the imams in our time do, starting with reciting Surat al-Takathur in the first rak'ah and Surat al-Ikhlas in the second, until their recitation in the nineteenth rak'ah is Surat al-Tabbat wa tawalla, and in the twentieth Surat al-Ikhlas. There is no dislike (karahah) in the first shaf' of the last tarwihah due to the separation between the two rak'ahs with one surah, because that is specific to obligatory prayers as is apparent from al-Khulasah and others. However, some imams have added abominable things in doing so: hasty recitation, lack of tranquility (tuma'ninah) in bowing and prostration and between them, omission of thana', ta'awwudh, and basmalah at the beginning of every shaf', and omission of the rest between every two tarwihahs. In al-Khulasah: The best is to balance recitation between the taslims; thus it was narrated from Abu Hanifa. If one prefers some over others in recitation, there is no harm. As for a single taslim, if the second is preferred over the first, there is no doubt that it is not recommended. If the first is preferred over the second, it is like the difference in obligatory prayer. If the imam finishes the tashahhud in Tarawih, if he knows that the increase beyond the amount of tashahhud does not weigh heavily on the people, he says the supplications. If he knows it will weigh heavily, he restricts to salawat (sending blessings on the Prophet) because salah is fard according to al-Shafi'i, so he takes precaution. Fath al-Qadir explains: Salah is fard or sunnah, and sunnahs are not abandoned for the congregation, end. So that it be a textual proof on the sunniyyah (sunnah status) of completing the Quran in prayer. His statement: (There is no dislike in the first shaf' of the last tarwihah). Al-Ramli said: Because he recites in its first rak'ah al-Nasr, and in the second al-Ikhlas, and there is separation with Surah al-Tabbat.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of completing the Quran (khatm) during Tarawih prayers. The majority hold that the sunnah is to complete the Quran once, preferably by the 27th night. Completing twice or three times is considered virtuous. However, practical considerations are emphasized: the imam should not cause aversion (tanfir) among the congregation, especially in later times. Contemporary practice, as noted, often involves shorter recitations to keep the congregation engaged. The text also provides specific rulings on recitation patterns, avoidance of disliked acts, and the imam's actions after tashahhud. The final note clarifies that there is no dislike in the first shaf' of the last tarwihah when separating with a surah, as this restriction applies only to obligatory prayers.

Key Terms
الختم (al-khatm): Completion of the entire Quran; in this context, reciting the whole Quran over the month of Ramadan during Tarawih prayers.
التنفير (al-tanfir): Causing aversion or annoyance to the congregation by excessively long recitation.
التسليمة (al-taslimah): One unit of Tarawih prayer, typically consisting of four rak'ahs with one taslim (salam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) No completion is required; any recitation is fine.

Key Takeaway
Completing the Quran once during Tarawih is sunnah, but avoiding tanfir (aversion) by shorter recitation takes precedence in the later Hanafi position.

Recitation in Tarawih: Quantity and Quality to Avoid Repelling the People
Ruling on preferred recitation amount and repetition of surahs in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on preferred recitation in Tarawih and apply the principle of avoiding tanfir (repelling the congregation) to determine appropriate recitation length.

Core Idea
Longer recitation is not always better; avoiding tanfir takes precedence over prolonging qira'ah.

The Hanafi school holds that Tarawih recitation should be moderate, prioritizing the congregation's comfort over lengthy recitation. This lesson examines the preferred number of verses per rak'ah and the permissibility of repeating the same surah, based on the principle that gathering many people (takthir al-jam') is better than lengthening the recitation (tatwil al-qira'ah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the preferred recitation quantity from al-Kafi
The passage begins by stating that reciting three verses per rak'ah (or three times in every ten) is better, as cited from al-Kafi. Identify this as one position.
The exact meaning of 'three times in every ten' is interpreted as three verses per rak'ah by some scholars.
2
Understand the principle of tanfir
From al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar, the preferred amount is that which does not cause tanfir (repelling) of the people. Recognize that this principle overrides a fixed number: the imam must gauge the congregation's capacity.
This is a manifestation of istihsan and ra'y in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Note the later scholars' (mutakhkhirin) fatwa
The later scholars gave fatwa for three short verses and one long verse per rak'ah to avoid weariness and abandonment of tarawih. This became the mufta bihi position for later times.
This shows how fatwa can adapt to circumstances while remaining within the school's principles.
4
Analyze the proof from Abu Hanifa
Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that reciting three verses after al-Fatiha in the obligatory prayer is sufficient and good; this is used as a qiyas (analogy) for tarawih: if in fard, then in nafl even more so.
The proof is a qawl sahabi of Abu Hanifa (though not a marfu' hadith), which is a valid source in Hanafi usul.
5
Consider the option of reciting the same surah repeatedly
From al-Tajnisi, some recite Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad in every rak'ah, while others recite from al-Fil to the end. This is deemed good because it aids in counting rak'ahs and allows for concentration.
Repetition is permissible and even recommended for focus, not a defect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثلاث مرات في كل عشر مرة أفضل كذا في الكافي. وذكر في المحيط والاختيار أن الأفضل أن يقرأ فيها مقدار ما لا يؤدي إلى تنفير القوم في زماننا لأن تكثير الجمع أفضل من تطويل القراءة. وفي المجتبي والمتأخرون كانوا يفتون في زماننا بثلاث آيات قصاراً وآية طويلة حتى لا يمل القوم ولا يلزم تعطيلها وهذا حسن، فإن الحسن روى عن أبي حنيفة أنه هذا إن قرأ في المكتوبة بعد الفاتحة ثلاث آيات فقد أحسن ولم يسيء في المكتوبة فما ظنك في غيرها اهـ. وفي التجنيس : ثم بعضهم اعتادوا قراءة «قل هو الله أحد» في كل ركعة وبعضهم اختاروا قراءة سورة الفيل إلى آخر القرآن وهذا حسن لأنه لا يشتبه عليه عدد الركعات ولا يشتغل قلبه بحفظها فيتفرغ للتدبر والتفكر ا.هـ.
And three times in every ten times is better, as stated in al-Kafi. And it is mentioned in al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar that the best is to recite as much as does not cause the people to be repelled in our time, because increasing the congregation is better than lengthening the recitation. And in al-Mujtaba: the later scholars used to give fatwa in our time for three short verses and one long verse so that the people do not become weary and its abandonment is not necessary, and this is good. Indeed, al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said: 'If one recited in the obligatory prayer after al-Fatiha three verses, he has done well and not done wrong in the obligatory prayer, so what do you think about other than it?'. And in al-Tajnisi: Some of them are accustomed to reciting 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' in every rak'ah, and some choose to recite Surah al-Fil to the end of the Quran, and this is good because it does not confuse him regarding the number of rak'ahs, nor does his heart become occupied with memorizing it, so he is free to reflect and contemplate.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the quantity and quality of recitation in tarawih. The author quotes multiple Hanafi sources. First, from al-Kafi: reciting three times in every ten times (i.e., reciting three verses per rak'ah?) is better. Then from al-Muhit and al-Ikhtiyar: the preferred amount is that which does not cause the congregation to be repelled, as gathering many people is better than lengthening the recitation. This shows the Hanafi concern for the people's capacity. The later scholars (mutakhkhirin) gave fatwa for three short verses and one long verse to avoid weariness. This is supported by a narration from Abu Hanifa: if one recites three verses after al-Fatiha in the obligatory prayer, he has done well, so how much more in nafl? Then from al-Tajnisi: some recite Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad every rak'ah, others recite from al-Fil to the end; this is good because it helps count rak'ahs and allows for concentration.

Key Terms
تراويح (tarawih): The night prayers during Ramadan performed in congregation after Isha, consisting of 20 rak'ahs in the Hanafi school.
تنفير (tanfir): Causing the congregation to become averse or repelled due to excessive length.

The Sunnah of Completing the Quran in Tarawih and Current Practice
Ruling on khatm in tarawih and its practical concession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on khatm in tarawih (sunnah muakkadah), explain the proof using the rak'ah/verse calculation, and identify when it may be abandoned to avoid hardship.

Core Idea
Khatm in tarawih is sunnah, but the imam may choose a lighter recitation to keep the congregation engaged.

Completing the entire Quran during Tarawih is a beloved practice, but is it obligatory? This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that khatm is a confirmed sunnah, not a wajib. The proof is clever: the total six hundred rak'ahs of the month can accommodate the six thousand verses of the Quran at ten verses per rak'ah. Yet, the late Hanafi masters recognized that insisting on khatm could drive people away, especially in our times. Thus, imams are permitted to recite shorter surahs, as seen in current practice. However, this concession does not permit rushing or abandoning tranquility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on khatm
State that the established position (mufta bihi) is that completing the Quran in tarawih is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Not wajib or fard.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
Note the calculation: 600 rak'ahs in the month ÷ 6000 verses = 10 verses per rak'ah, making khatm feasible. This is cited as evidence that khatm is the sunnah.
The proof is a form of qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) based on possibility.
3
Recognize the exception for hardship
Understand that khatm can be abandoned if it leads to repelling people (tanfir) or closing mosques. The lighter recitation is then chosen.
This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to preserve the practice of tarawih.
4
Describe the current practice
Learn that imams often recite from Surah al-Takathur to Surah al-Ikhlas across the month, ending with two rak'ahs of al-Ikhlas. There is no karahah in repeating a surah in nafl (unlike fard).
The rest between tarawih cycles (istiraha) is also part of the practice.
5
Identify objectionable additions
Be aware that some imams introduce harmful practices: hurried recitation (hadhramah), lack of tranquility in ruku' and sujud, and omitting sunnan like thana', ta'awwudh, basmalah.
These are makruh and should be avoided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصرح في الهداية بأن أكثر المشايخ على أن السنة فيها الختم. وفي مختارات النوازل أنه يقرأ في كل ركعة عشر آيات وهو الصحيح لأن السنة فيها الختم لأن جميع عدد الركعات في جميع الشهر ستمائة ركعة وجميع آيات القرآن ستة آلاف ا.هـ. ونص في الخانية على أنه الصحيح. وفي فتح القدير وغيره: وإذا كان إمام مسجد حيه لا يختم فله أن يترك إلى غيره. فالحاصل أن المصحح في المذهب أن الختم سنة لكن لا يلزم منه عدم تركه إذا لزم منه تنفير القوم وتعطيل كثير من المساجد خصوصاً في زماننا، فالظاهر اختيار الأخف على القوم كما تفعله الأئمة في زماننا من بداءتهم بقراءة سورة التكاثر في الركعة الأولى وبقراءتهم سورة الأخلاص في الثانية إلى أن تكون قراءتهم في الركعة التاسعة عشرة سورة «تبت» وفي العشرين سورة الأخلاص وليس فيه كراهة في الشفع الأولى من الترويحة الأخيرة بسبب الفصل بين الركعتين بسورة واحدة لأنه خاص بالفرائض كما هو ظاهر الخلاصة وغيرها إلا أنه قد زاد بعض الأئمة من فعلها على هذا الوجه منكرات من هذرمة القراءة وعدم الطمأنينة في الركوع والسجود وفيما بينهما وفيما بين السجدتين اشتمالها على ترك الثناء والتعوذ والبسملة في أول كل شفع وترك مع الاستراحة فيما بين كل ترويحتين.
And it is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah that most shaykhs are of the opinion that completing the Quran (khatm) is sunnah in it (tarawih). And in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil: He recites in every rak'ah ten verses, and that is the correct opinion, because the sunnah is to complete the Quran, because the total number of rak'ahs in the entire month is six hundred, and all the verses of the Quran are six thousand. And it is stated in al-Khaniyya that this is the correct opinion. And in Fath al-Qadir and others: If the imam of a mosque in his quarter does not complete the Quran, he may leave to another. So the gist is that the established position in the madhhab is that khatm is sunnah, but its abandonment is not necessarily required if it leads to repelling the people and causing many mosques to be closed, especially in our time. So it appears that choosing the lighter (recitation) for the people is preferred, as the imams do in our time, starting with Surah al-Takathur in the first rak'ah and reciting Surah al-Ikhlas in the second, until their recitation in the nineteenth rak'ah is Surah Tabbat and in the twentieth Surah al-Ikhlas. And there is no karahah in the first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih because of the separation between the two rak'ahs by one surah, for that is specific to the obligatory prayers, as is apparent from al-Khulasa and others. However, some imams have added to this practice objectionable things such as hurried recitation, lack of tranquility in bowing and prostration and in between them, and including the abandonment of the opening supplication, ta'awwudh, and basmalah at the beginning of each pair, and abandoning the rest between every two tarawih cycles.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the sunnah of completing the Quran in tarawih. The author cites al-Hidayah that most Hanafi shaykhs consider khatm sunnah. Mukhtarat al-Nawazil provides a proof: total rak'ahs (600) and total verses (6000) allow for 10 verses per rak'ah, so khatm is possible. Al-Khaniyya confirms this as the correct view. Fath al-Qadir adds an exception: if the imam cannot complete the khatm, he may leave to another imam who can. The conclusion: khatm is sunnah but can be abandoned if it causes hardship. The author then describes the current practice of imams reciting from Surah al-Takathur to al-Ikhlas, and clarifies that there is no karahah in the first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih for repeating the same surah because the rule against repetition applies to fard, not nafl. However, some imams introduce bad practices like rushing, lack of tranquility, and omitting sunnan acts.

Key Terms
ختم (khatm): Completing the recitation of the entire Quran in tarawih over the month of Ramadan.
هذرمة (hadhramah): Hurried, slurred recitation without proper articulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is khatm in tarawih considered sunnah?
A) Because the Prophet always did it
B) Because the number of rak'ahs matches the number of verses
C) Because it is mentioned in the Quran
D) Because it was the practice of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Khatm in tarawih is a confirmed sunnah that may be abandoned to avoid hardship, but rushing and omitting tranquility are not permitted.

Rest Between Tarawih Cycles: Mustahabb or Disliked?
Commentary on the matn regarding no karahah in the first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih and the ruling on rest between cycles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rest (istiraha) in tarawih and identify when it is recommended or disliked.

Core Idea
Rest after every four rak'ahs in tarawih is mustahabb, not sunnah; sitting on five taslimats is disliked.

In the previous lesson, we learned about the structure of tarawih prayer. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies a subtle dispute: is there a disliked sitting (karahah) in the first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih? More importantly, when is rest (istiraha) between cycles recommended? The commentator refines a common misunderstanding, distinguishing between mustahabb and sunnah, and between the majority view and a minority opinion that rest on five taslimats is good.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize that the passage discusses two issues: (1) no karahah in the first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih, and (2) the ruling on sitting (jalsa) between cycles. The main dispute is about the timing and desirability of rest.
The first issue is straightforward: the imam recites distinct surahs, so no repetition causing karahah.
2
State the two views on rest
The majority (including al-Hidayah) hold that rest is mustahabb after each complete tarawih (4 rak'ahs). Some scholars (like al-Halabi) consider rest on five taslimats (2 rak'ahs each) as good, but al-Kafi says this is disliked.
Al-Halabi extended dislike to omitting rest entirely, but the author criticizes this.
3
Trace the evidence
The dalil is the practice of the people of Makkah and Madinah (the two sanctuaries). Rest on five taslimats opposes that practice, hence disliked.
The evidence is urf (custom) of the pious predecessors.
4
Analyze the refinement
Imam Husam al-Din clarifies that rest on five taslimats is not recommended; the correct view is that rest is only recommended at the completion of each tarawih (i.e., after every 4 rak'ahs). The practice of imams includes some rest, so it is not disliked a fortiori.
This is a critical refinement: al-Halabi's argument is based on a faulty premise (that rest occurs on five taslimats when it does not).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and follower etiquette
The relied-upon position: rest is mustahabb after each tarawih (4 rak'ahs). Additionally, it is disliked for a follower to sit when the imam is about to bow, as that shows laziness.
From al-Khaniyya: the follower must stand when the imam stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وليس فيه كراهة الشفع الأول من الترويحة الأخيرة) قال الرملي : لقراءته في الركعة الأولى منه النصر وفي الثانية منه بالإخلاص وفيه فصل بسورة «تبت» اهـ. كالتسبيحات ا هـ. وقوله بجلسة» متعلق بسن بيان لكونه سنة فيها، وتعقبه الشارح بأنه مستحب لا سنة. وصرح في الهداية باستحبابه بين الترويحتين وبين الخامسة وبين الوتر العادة أهل الحرمين واستحسن البعض الاستراحة على خمس تسليمات وليس بصحيح . وفي الكافي والاستراحة على خمس تسليمات تكره عند الجمهور لأنه خلاف عمل أهل الحرمين وذكر العلامة الحلبي : ويعرف من هذا كراهة ترك الاستراحة مقدار ترويحة على رأس سائر الأشفاع كما هو شأن أكثر أئمة أهل زماننا في البلاد الشامية والمصرية بطريق أولى ا هـ . ولا يخفى ما فيه لأن الاستراحة لم توجد أصلاً في مسألة الكافي إلا على خمس تسليمات مع أنها ليست محل الاستراحة، ولهذا قال الإمام حسام الدين في تأليف له خاص بالتراويح : الاستراحة على خمس تسليمات لا تستحب على قول الأكثر وهذا هو الصحيح فإن الصحيح أنه لا يستحب إلا عند تمام كل ترويحة وهي خمس ترويحات ا.هـ. بخلاف فعل الأئمة فإن الاستراحة قد وجدت وإن لم تكن تامة فكيف تكون مكروهة بالأولى وقد قالوا: إنهم مخيرون حالة الجلوس إن شاؤا سبحوا وإن شاؤا قرؤا القرآن وإن شاؤا صلوا أربع ركعات فرادى وإن شاؤا قعدوا ساكتين وأهل مكة يطوفون أسبوعاً ويصلون ركعتين، وأهل المدينة يصلون أربع ركعات فرادى. وبهذا علم أنه لو قال بانتظار بعد كل ترويحة» بدل قوله «بجلسة» لكان أولى. وفي الخانية : يكره للمقتدي أن يقعد في التراويح فإذا أراد الإمام أن يركع يقوم لأن فيه إظهار التكاسل في الصلاة والتشبه بالمنافقين قال تعالى وإذا قاموا إلى الصلاة قاموا كسالى ﴾ [النساء : ١٤٢]١ هـ.
His statement: 'And there is no karahah in the first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih.' Al-Ramli said: Because of his recitation in the first rak'ah of it of al-Nasr and in the second of al-Ikhlas, and there is a separation with Surah Tabbat. End. Like the tasbihat. End. And his statement 'with a sitting' is related to 'sunnah' indicating that it is sunnah therein, but the commentator objected that it is mustahabb, not sunnah. And it is stated in al-Hidayah that it is mustahabb between two tarawih cycles and between the fifth and between the witr according to the practice of the people of the two sanctuaries. And some considered rest on five taslimats as good, but it is not correct. And in al-Kafi: Rest on five taslimats is disliked according to the majority because it opposes the practice of the people of the two sanctuaries. And al-Allama al-Halabi mentioned: From this is known the dislike of omitting the rest for the duration of a tarawih at the head of other cycles, as is the case of most imams of our time in the Syrian and Egyptian lands, by a greater reason. End of quote. And it is not hidden what is in it because rest did not exist originally in the issue of al-Kafi except on five taslimats, while they are not a place of rest. Hence Imam Husam al-Din said in his treatise on tarawih: Rest on five taslimats is not recommended according to most, and this is correct, for the correct view is that it is not recommended except at the completion of every tarawih, which is five tarawihs. End. Contrary to the practice of the imams, for rest has occurred even if not complete, so how could it be disliked a fortiori? And they said: They are free during the sitting state: if they wish, they glorify; if they wish, they recite Quran; if they wish, they pray four rak'ahs individually; if they wish, they sit silently. And the people of Makkah circumambulate one week and pray two rak'ahs, and the people of Madinah pray four rak'ahs individually. By this it is known that if he had said 'waiting after every tarawih' instead of 'a sitting', it would be better. And in al-Khaniyya: It is disliked for the follower to sit in tarawih; when the imam wants to bow, he should stand, because it shows laziness in prayer and resemblance to the hypocrites. Allah said: 'And when they stand up for prayer, they stand up lazily' [al-Nisa: 142].
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn statement that there is no karahah in the first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih. Al-Ramli explains that the imam recites al-Nasr and al-Ikhlas, separated by Tabbat, so there is no repetition causing karahah. The commentator then discusses the ruling on sitting (jalsa) between tarawih cycles. The matn may have said 'sitting' as a sunnah, but the commentator (sharh) objects that it is mustahabb, not sunnah. Al-Hidayah says it is mustahabb according to the practice of the people of Makkah and Madinah. Some considered rest on five taslimats (pairs of rak'ahs) as good, but al-Kafi states this is disliked according to the majority because it opposes the practice of the people of the two sanctuaries. Al-Halabi extends the dislike to omitting the rest entirely. However, the author criticizes this because rest on five taslimats is not the actual practice; rather, rest is after every tarawih (set of four rak'ahs). Imam Husam al-Din clarifies that rest is only recommended after each complete tarawih (five tarawihs). The imams' actual practice includes rest, so it is not disliked. The passage ends with a ruling from al-Khaniyya that it is disliked for a follower to sit while the imam is about to bow, as it shows laziness.

Key Terms
الشفع الأول من الترويحة الأخيرة (al-shaf' al-awwal min al-tarwiha al-akhirah): The first two rak'ahs of the last tarawih (the final set of 4 rak'ahs in the 20-rak'ah tarawih).
الاستراحة (al-istiraha): A brief rest between tarawih cycles, typically after each set of 4 rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After every two rak'ahs
B) After every four rak'ahs (tarawih)
C) After every five taslimats
D) After every eight rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Rest in tarawih is mustahabb after each complete set of four rak'ahs, and the follower must stand when the imam bows.

Witr in Congregation in Ramadan: Recommendation and Evidence
Ruling on Witr in congregation in Ramadan with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on Witr in congregation in Ramadan and identify its proof from the practice of 'Umar.

Core Idea
Witr in congregation in Ramadan is recommended, not obligatory.

The Hanafi school teaches that Witr in congregation is limited to Ramadan. This lesson examines the ruling, its basis in consensus, and the preferred view that congregational Witr is better, as demonstrated by the practice of Caliph 'Umar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on Witr in congregation
Note the matn statement: 'And he performs Witr in congregation in Ramadan only.' Recognize that the ruling is istihbab (recommendation), not obligation.
The word 'only' restricts the congregation to Ramadan.
2
Establish the consensus
Al-Hidayah reports ijma' (consensus) that it is legislated. This is the basis for the ruling.
Ijmā' makes the ruling certain (qat'i) in principle.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on preference
Some scholars debated whether congregation is better than praying alone. Al-Khaniyya supports congregation as better, citing 'Umar's practice.
The proof is a precedent from a rightly guided caliph.
4
State the mufta bihi
The operative position (mufta bihi) is that Witr in congregation in Ramadan is mustahabb and better than praying alone.
This is the relied-upon view in the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ويوتر بجماعة في رمضان فقط) أي على وجه الاستحباب وعليه إجماع المسلمين كما في الهداية. واختلفوا في الأفضل ففي الخانية الصحيح أن أداء الوتر بجماعة في رمضان أفضل لأن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يؤمهم في الوتر. وفي قوله : (وتعقبه الشارح بأنه مستحب لا سنة قال في النهر : وهو ظاهر في ندبها على رأس الخامسة لكن في الخلاصة أكثرهم على عدم الاستحباب وهو الصحيح ا هـ . قلت : إن أراد . الخامسة من التسليمة الخامسة وهي المسألة الآتية عن الكافى فما ادعاه من الظهور ممنوع إذ لا تعرض له في كلام الشارح أصلاً، وإن أراد منها الترويحة الخامسة فكلام الخلاصة ليس فيها لأن نص عبارة الخلاصة هكذا والاستراحة على خمس تسليمات اختلف المشايخ فيه، وأكثرهم على أنه لا يستحب وهو الصحيح .. قوله : (ولا يخفي ما فيه الخ أقول أظن أن لفظة ترك» في عبارة الحلبي زائدة من بعض النساخ ألحقها استبعاداً لأن يكون شأن الأئمة ذلك إذ شأنهم المساهلة ولعل ذلك كان في زمانه، وإن ثبت ما قلنا يندفع الإيراد عن كلام هذا العلامة وإلا فهو كلام متهافت يبعد صدوره عن (وقد قالوا الخ) قال الرملي قال الحلبي ومن المكروه ما يفعله بعض الجهال من صلاة ركعتين منفرداً أمثاله قوله :
His statement: 'And he performs Witr in congregation in Ramadan only' i.e., on the basis of recommendation, and there is consensus of the Muslims on it as in al-Hidayah. And they differed on what is better. In al-Khaniyya, the correct view is that performing Witr in congregation in Ramadan is better, because 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him) used to lead them in Witr. And regarding his statement: 'And the commentator objected that it is mustahabb, not sunnah.' He said in al-Nahr: It is apparent regarding its recommendation at the head of the fifth, but in al-Khulasa, most are of the opinion that it is not recommended, and that is correct. End. I say: If he meant the fifth of the fifth taslimah, which is the issue coming from al-Kafi, then his claim of apparentness is denied, since the commentator did not address it at all. And if he meant the fifth tarawih, then the statement of al-Khulasa is not about it, because the text of al-Khulasa is: 'And rest on five taslimats is a matter in which the mashayikh differed, and most are of the opinion that it is not recommended, and that is correct.' End. His statement: 'And it is not hidden what is in it, etc.' I say: I think that the word 'ترك' (omission) in the statement of al-Halabi is an addition by some scribes, inserted out of improbability that the practice of the imams is like that, since their practice is leniency, and perhaps that was in his time. If what we said is established, the objection to the statement of this scholar is repelled; otherwise, it is incoherent speech unlikely to have come from him. And 'And they said, etc.' Al-Ramli said: al-Halabi said: Among the disliked things is what some ignorant people do, praying two rak'ahs individually, etc. His statement:

Commentary
This passage opens with a matn statement that Witr in congregation is only in Ramadan, meaning it is recommended (mustahabb) and there is consensus on its legislation. The best view is that it is better to pray Witr in congregation in Ramadan, as 'Umar did. Then the author addresses a comment from the commentator (sharh) who said that a certain sitting is mustahabb not sunnah. The author of al-Nahr says this sitting is recommended at the head of the fifth (tarawih?), but al-Khulasa says most do not consider it recommended. The author (of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) clarifies: if 'the fifth' refers to the fifth taslimah (pair of rak'ahs) from al-Kafi, then the commentator did not discuss it; if it refers to the fifth tarawih, then al-Khulasa is about rest on five taslimats, not about a sitting. The author then suggests that a word in al-Halabi's statement may be a scribal addition. The passage ends with al-Ramli quoting al-Halabi that it is disliked for ignorant people to pray two rak'ahs individually (during the rest period).

Key Terms
الوتر بجماعة (al-witr bi-jama'ah): Performing the Witr prayer in congregation, which is recommended only in Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is sunnah mu'akkadah

Key Takeaway
Witr in congregation in Ramadan is recommended (mustahabb) and better than alone, based on the precedent of 'Umar.

Refinement of the Rest Ruling: When Sitting Between Tarawih Rak'ahs Is Not Recommended
Critical refinement of the ruling on resting during tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the rest after every two rak'ahs (or five taslimats) during tarawih is not recommended, and identify the correct view among Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
The rest (sitting) after five taslimats is not recommended despite a commentator's claim otherwise.

The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refines a previous commentator's statement about the recommendation of a rest during tarawih. He shows that the correct view, according to most mashayikh, is that such a rest is not recommended (mustahabb). This lesson clarifies the reasoning and resolves the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target of refinement
The commentator (sharih) on al-Kanz claimed that a certain rest (sitting after every two rak'ahs?) is mustahabb, not sunnah. The author of al-Nahr said it is apparent that it is recommended 'on the head of the fifth'.
'The fifth' could mean the fifth taslimah (pair) or the fifth tarawih.
2
Examine the objection from al-Khulasa
Al-Khulasa states that most scholars hold that it is not recommended. The author of al-Bahr clarifies that al-Khulasa refers to a different issue: the rest after five taslimats (i.e., after 10 rak'ahs), not after every two rak'ahs.
This resolves the apparent disagreement.
3
Distinguish the two meanings of 'the fifth'
If 'the fifth' means the fifth taslimah (from al-Kafi), the commentator did not address it; if it means the fifth tarawih, then al-Khulasa is about rest on five taslimats, not relevant.
Thus the commentator's claim is not supported.
4
State the correct ruling
The rest (sitting) after praying two rak'ahs (or after five taslimats) is not recommended; it is permissible but not a sunnah or mustahabb act.
Some later scholars (al-Halabi) even considered praying two rak'ahs individually during the rest as makruh.

Source Text

Rest Between Tarawih Cycles (Istirahah)
Explaining the ruling on rest between tarawih sets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking rest during tarawih and identify the correct timing (after each tarawih of 4 rak'ahs) while distinguishing it from incorrect practices.

Core Idea
Rest during tarawih is mustahabb only after each complete tarawih (4 rak'ahs), not after every two.

During the long tarawih prayers in Ramadan, a brief rest is recommended between sets. This lesson clarifies when that rest is taken, explains the intra-Hanafi disagreement over its timing, and also addresses the ruling on a follower sitting while the imam stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on rest
Read the passage to find the basic ruling: the rest is mustahabb (recommended), not sunnah. The commentator corrects the matn's phrasing.
The distinction between sunnah and mustahabb is important for understanding the legal strength.
2
Determine the proper timing
The passage states the correct timing is after each complete tarawih (4 rak'ahs), not after every two or after five salam-givings. Locate the opinion of Imam Husam al-Din supporting this.
The phrase 'عند تمام كل ترويحة' is key.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some scholars favored rest after five salam-givings (10 rak'ahs). Identify their reasoning and why the majority rejected it.
The dispute is resolved by citing the practice of the people of the two sanctuaries.
4
Understand the ruling on sitting
The passage notes that it is makruh for a follower to sit while the imam stands during tarawih, based on the verse showing laziness.
This is a separate but related point.

الاستراحة على خمس تسليمات وليس بصحيح . وفي الكافي والاستراحة على خمس تسليمات تكره عند الجمهور لأنه خلاف عمل أهل الحرمين وذكر العلامة الحلبي : ويعرف من هذا كراهة ترك الاستراحة مقدار ترويحة على رأس سائر الأشفاع كما هو شأن أكثر أئمة أهل زماننا في البلاد الشامية والمصرية بطريق أولى ا هـ . ولا يخفى ما فيه لأن الاستراحة لم توجد أصلاً في مسألة الكافي إلا على خمس تسليمات مع أنها ليست محل الاستراحة، ولهذا يطوفون أسبوعاً ويصلون ركعتين، وأهل المدينة يصلون أربع ركعات فرادى. وبهذا علم أنه لو قال بانتظار بعد كل ترويحة» بدل قوله «بجلسة» لكان أولى. وفي الخانية : يكره للمقتدي أن يقعد في التراويح فإذا أراد الإمام أن يركع يقوم لأن فيه إظهار التكاسل في الصلاة والتشبه بالمنافقين قال تعالى وإذا قاموا إلى الصلاة قاموا كسالى﴾ [النساء : ١٤٢]١ هـ. قوله: (ويوتر بجماعة في رمضان فقط) أي على وجه الاستحباب وعليه إجماع المسلمين كما في الهداية. واختلفوا في الأفضل ففي الخانية الصحيح أن أداء الوتر بجماعة في رمضان أفضل لأن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يؤمهم في الوتر. وفي النهاية : اختار علماؤنا أن يوتر في منزله لا بجماعة لأن الصحابة لم يجتمعوا على الوتر بجماعة في رمضان كما اجتمعوا على التراويح لأن عمر كان يؤمهم فيه في رمضان وأبي بن اه. الأول في فتح القدير بأنه كان أوتر بهم ثم بين العذر يؤمهم ورجح في تأخره عن مثل ما صنع فيما مضى فالوتر كالتراويح، فكما أن الجماعة فيها سنة فكذلك في الوتر، ولو صلوا الوتر بجماعة في غير رمضان فهو صحيح مكروه كالتطوع في غير رمضان بجماعة، وقيده في الكافي بأن يكون على سبيل التداعي، أما لو اقتدى واحد بواحد أو اثنان بواحد لا يكره وإذا اقتدى ثلاثة بواحد اختلفوا فيه وإن اقتدى أربعة بواحد كره وفي القنية : صلى العشاء وحده فله أن يصلي التراويح مع الإمام، ولو تركوا الجماعة في الفرض ليس لهم أن يصلوا التراويح جماعة لأنها تبع للجماعة، ولو لم يصل التراويح جماعة مع الإمام فله أن يصلي الوتر معه . ثم ذكر بعده أنه لو صلى التراويح مع غيره له أن يصلي الوتر معه هو الصحيح ا هـ . ومن رام الزيادة على ما ذكرناه من أحكام التراويح فعليه بمؤلف خاص بها للإمام الأجلّ حسام الدين قد اطلعت عليه والله الموفق للصواب .
Like the tasbihat, etc. And his saying 'with a sitting' is attached to 'sunnah' to indicate that it is sunnah therein. The commentator objected that it is mustahabb, not sunnah. And it is stated in al-Hidayah that it is mustahabb between the two tarawihs and between the fifth and witr according to the practice of the people of the two sanctuaries. And some deemed it good to rest after every five salam-givings, but it is not correct. And in al-Kafi: 'Resting after every five salam-givings is makruh according to the majority because it contradicts the practice of the people of the two sanctuaries.' And al-Allama al-Halabi mentioned: 'From this one knows the dislike of abandoning rest to the extent of one tarawih at the head of the remaining sets, as is the way of most imams of our time in the Levantine and Egyptian lands, by a fortiori reasoning.' It is not hidden what is in it because the rest did not exist originally in the issue of al-Kafi except after five salam-givings, and it is not a place of rest. Hence Imam Husam al-Din said in his work specifically on tarawih: 'Rest after five salam-givings is not recommended according to the majority, and this is correct. The correct view is that it is only recommended upon completion of each tarawih, which is five tarawihs.' Unlike the action of the imams, for rest has occurred even if not complete; so how could it be considered disliked by priority? And they said: They have a choice while sitting: if they wish they make tasbih, if they wish they recite Quran, if they wish they pray four rak'ahs individually, or if they wish they sit silently. The people of Mecca perform tawaf and pray two rak'ahs, and the people of Medina pray four rak'ahs individually. By this it is known that if he had said 'after each tarawih' instead of his saying 'with a sitting', it would have been better. And in al-Khaniyah: It is makruh for the follower to sit in tarawih, so when the imam wants to bow he stands up, because it shows laziness in prayer and resemblance to hypocrites. Allah says: 'And when they stand up for prayer, they stand up lazily' (al-Nisa 4:142). His saying: 'And he performs witr in congregation in Ramadan only' i.e., on the basis of recommendation, and upon this is the consensus of the Muslims as in al-Hidayah. They differed on what is better. In al-Khaniyah, the correct view is that performing witr in congregation in Ramadan is better because Umar (RA) used to lead them in witr. And in al-Nihayah: Our scholars chose that one should pray witr at home, not in congregation, because the Companions did not gather for witr in congregation in Ramadan as they did for tarawih, because Umar used to lead them in it in Ramadan and Ubay [ibn Ka'b]. The first view in Fath al-Qadir is that he used to lead them in witr, then he gave an excuse, and the latter view preferred that he was delayed similarly to what was done in the past, so witr is like tarawih. Just as congregation in it is sunnah, so too in witr. And if they pray witr in congregation outside Ramadan, it is valid but disliked, like voluntary prayer in congregation outside Ramadan. And in al-Kafi it was restricted to when it is by mutual agreement. But if one followers one, or two follow one, it is not disliked. If three follow one, they differed. If four follow one, it is disliked. And in al-Qunyah: If one prayed 'isha alone, he may pray tarawih with the imam. And if they abandon congregation in the obligatory, they may not pray tarawih in congregation because it is subsidiary to congregation. And if he did not pray tarawih in congregation with the imam, he may pray witr with him. Then he mentioned after that that if he prayed tarawih with someone else, he may pray witr with him—this is the correct view. And whoever desires more than what we have mentioned of the rulings of tarawih should refer to the specific work on it by the great Imam Husam al-Din, which I have seen. And Allah guides to correctness.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of tarawih and witr, specifically addressing the issue of 'rest' (استراحة) between sets of tarawih and the ruling on praying witr in congregation during Ramadan. The author, Ibn al-Humam, cites various earlier authorities. First, the text discusses whether the rest after every five salam-givings (i.e., after 10 rak'ahs) is recommended or not. The commentator (likely al-Haskafi) objects that it is mustahabb, not sunnah. Al-Hidayah states that a short rest after each tarawih (4 rak'ahs) and before witr is mustahabb. Some advocated resting after five salam-givings, but this is criticized as incorrect. Imām Ḥusām al-Dīn’s work on tarawih clarifies that rest is only recommended after completing a full tarawih (four rak'ahs), and there are five such tarawihs in the night. The practice of the people of Madinah and Makkah is mentioned. Then the ruling on a follower sitting during tarawih while the imam stands is given: it is makruh because it resembles laziness. Second, the passage covers witr in congregation in Ramadan. The matn says 'he performs witr in congregation in Ramadan only' meaning it is recommended. There is consensus on this. However, scholars differed on whether it is better to pray witr in congregation or alone. Some argue that since Umar (RA) led the Companions in witr, congregation is better. Others argue that the Companions did not gather for witr as they did for tarawih, so praying at home is better. The author notes that the first view in Fath al-Qadir reconciles Umar's action with the second view, and says witr is like tarawih—congregation is sunnah. The passage then clarifies that praying witr in congregation outside Ramadan is valid but disliked, similar to voluntary prayers in congregation. Conditions for dislike are discussed: if done by mutual agreement? If the number of followers is three or four? Finally, practical points: one may pray tarawih with the imam even if one prayed 'isha alone; if the congregation for obligatory prayer is abandoned, tarawih congregation cannot be held because it is subsidiary; if one missed tarawih with the imam, he may still pray witr with him.

Key Terms
الاستراحة (al-istirāḥah): A brief pause or rest between sets (tarawih) of the night prayer in Ramadan, during which the congregation may engage in tasbih, Quran recitation, silence, or optional prayer.
الترويحة (al-tarwīḥah): A set of four rak'ahs in the tarawih prayer; the night typically has five tarawihs (20 rak'ahs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should the rest (istirāḥah) during tarawih prayer be taken?
A) After every two rak'ahs
B) After every four rak'ahs (after each tarawih)
C) After every five rak'ahs
D) No rest at all

Key Takeaway
Rest during tarawih is mustahabb only after each full tarawih (4 rak'ahs), following the practice of the Salaf.

Salah — Prayer

Witr in Congregation in Ramadan
Explaining the ruling of witr in congregation in Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on performing witr in congregation during Ramadan and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether congregation is better than praying individually.

Core Idea
Witr in congregation is recommended in Ramadan only, and the Hanafi school considers it similar to tarawih in this regard.

The witr prayer is wajib, but praying it in congregation is recommended specifically in Ramadan. This lesson covers the consensus on its recommendation, the dispute over whether congregation is better, and the ruling for outside Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
State the basic ruling
The matn says 'he performs witr in congregation in Ramadan only.' Understand that this is on the basis of recommendation (istihbab).
The passage says there is consensus (ijma') on this ruling.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some Hanafis (in al-Khaniyah) hold that congregation is better, citing Umar's practice. Others (in al-Nihayah) prefer praying at home, arguing the Companions did not gather for witr like they did for tarawih.
Note the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in what is considered afdal.
3
Analyze the reconciliation in Fath al-Qadir
The author (Ibn al-Humam) in Fath al-Qadir reconciles the views, suggesting witr is like tarawih, and congregation is sunnah. Understand the reasoning.
This strengthens the recommendation of congregation.
4
Examine the ruling outside Ramadan
Praying witr in congregation outside Ramadan is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi) like any voluntary congregation. The passage details conditions when it is not disliked.
The dislike is when done by mutual agreement (tada'i) with three or more followers.

Finally, practical points: one may pray tarawih with the imam even if one prayed 'isha alone; if the congregation for obligatory prayer is abandoned, tarawih congregation cannot be held because it is subsidiary; if one missed tarawih with the imam, he may still pray witr with him.

Key Terms
الوتر بجماعة (al-watr bi-jamāʿah): Performing the witr prayer (odd-numbered prayer ending the night) in congregation; in Ramadan it is recommended, outside Ramadan it is makruh tanzihan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, ruling on performing witr in congregation during Ramadan is:
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah muakkadah
C) Mustahabb (recommended)
D) Makruh tanzihi

Key Takeaway
Witr in congregation is recommended only in Ramadan, and the relied-upon view holds that it is better than praying alone.

Joining the Congregation After Starting Prayer Alone
Ruling statement on joining congregation after started prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person has prayed one or three rak'ahs of an obligatory prayer and the iqamah is given, and explain the reasoning behind converting the begun prayer to nafl.

Core Idea
A begun obligatory prayer is not broken; it is completed as nafl to join the congregation.

Imagine you start praying Zuhr alone and after one rak'ah you hear the iqamah for the congregational Zuhr. What do you do? According to the Hanafi school, you do not abandon your prayer – you complete it as a voluntary prayer and then join the congregation. This ruling preserves both your started worship and the virtue of congregation. In this lesson, we unpack the exact ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and understand the legal logic behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial prayer and its status
The person has begun an obligatory prayer (e.g., Zuhr) and has completed one or three rak'ahs. The prayer is in progress, and the iqamah for the same obligatory prayer is called.
The prayer must be the same obligatory prayer for which the congregation is formed.
2
Determine the action upon hearing the iqamah
According to the matn, if one rak'ah has been prayed, he adds one rak'ah to make it two (shaf'an), thereby converting it to a nafl prayer. If three rak'ahs have been prayed, he adds one rak'ah to complete four, then follows the imam as a volunteer (mutatawwi'an).
In both cases, the original obligatory prayer is not invalidated; it becomes a voluntary prayer.
3
Recognize the legal transformation
The prayer is intentionally changed from obligatory to nafl by completing an even number (for one rak'ah) or completing the full count (for three rak'ahs). This is allowed because the virtue of congregation outweighs the specific obligation of continuing alone.
The underlying principle: you do not abandon an obligatory act without excuse, but you can upgrade to a more virtuous act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلى ركعة من الظهر فأقيم يتم شفعاً ويقتدي ولو صلى ثلاثاً يتم ويقتدي متطوعاً
If he prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr and the iqamah is given, he completes it as two (i.e., he makes it an even number) and then follows (the imam); and if he prayed three rak'ahs, he completes it and then follows as a volunteer.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of Bab Idrak al-Faridah (Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer). It presents a ruling from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The scenario: a person starts praying the obligatory Zuhr prayer alone, and after one rak'ah the iqamah for the congregational Zuhr prayer is called. The ruling: He should complete that rak'ah by adding one more rak'ah, thereby turning his prayer into a two-rak'ah voluntary prayer (nafl), and then he joins the congregation's prayer. If he has already prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr, he should complete it to four rak'ahs (i.e., add one more rak'ah) and then join the congregation as a voluntary prayer after finishing his own. The underlying principle is that one should not break an obligatory prayer without a valid excuse, but here the congregational obligation can be fulfilled after making the started prayer a nafl. The commentary that follows (not fully shown) discusses the rationale: because the original obligation is not abandoned without reason, but rather the prayer is converted to a voluntary act so that he may join the more virtuous congregation.

Key Terms
إدراك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): Catching the obligatory prayer; the chapter deals with situations where a person has partially performed a prayer and then the congregation is established, and how to join without invalidating the first prayer.
شفعاً (shafʿan): Making it an even number; i.e., if he has prayed one rak'ah, he adds another to make two rak'ahs (as a voluntary prayer).
يقتدي (yaqtadī): He follows; i.e., he joins the congregational prayer as a follower of the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Complete four rak'ahs (add three more) and then join
D) Continue his prayer alone and not join the congregation

Key Takeaway
When iqamah is called while praying alone, one may convert the commenced obligatory prayer to nafl by completing an even number and then join the congregation.

Catching the Obligatory Prayer After One Rak'ah
Commentary on the ruling for one who has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr when iqamah is given.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for a person who has prayed one rak'ah of an obligatory prayer when the congregation starts, and state the Quranic proof and the condition for adding a second rak'ah.

Core Idea
Add a second rak'ah to make a pair, then join the congregation—do not invalidate your prayer.

This passage addresses a common scenario: a person begins an obligatory prayer individually, completes one rak'ah, and then hears the iqamah for congregation. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling that balances the prohibition against invalidating worship with the virtue of congregational prayer. By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling, its proof from the Quran, and the principle of 'invalidation for completion'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the initial ruling
Read that if a person prays one rak'ah of Zuhr and iqamah is given, he should complete it as a pair (two rak'ahs) and then join the congregation. Recognize that this is a specific application of a general principle.
The matn is from Kanz al-Daqa'iq; the commentary expands on it.
2
State the general principle: intentionally invalidating worship is haram
The Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (47:33) prohibits invalidating acts of worship without excuse. This is a foundational rule.
This shows the authority of the proof.
3
Explain the exception: invalidation for completion (ikmal ma'nan) is allowed
Invalidation is permitted if it is for a meaningful completion, such as demolishing a mosque for repair or canceling Zuhr for Jumu'ah. Here, adding a rak'ah to make a pair and joining the congregation is a meaningful completion.
The superiority of congregation is established by hadith.
4
Apply the exception to the scenario
The person adds a second rak'ah to his single rak'ah, turns his prayer into nafl (since supererogatory prayers are in pairs), then says salam and joins the congregation. This safeguards both the prayer (from invalidity) and the congregation.
If the first rak'ah was not completed with prostration, he cuts and joins without adding.
5
Address the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad
Abu Hanifa holds that invalidation of the description (wajibat) does not invalidate the essence; so the prayer becomes nafl. Muhammad holds that it does invalidate the essence, but this is restricted to cases where proceeding is impossible (e.g., adding a fifth rak'ah). The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
Understand why the text says 'invalidation of description only'.

قوله : (حقيقة هذا الباب مسائل شتى تتعلق بالفرائض في الأداء الكامل وكله مسائل الجامع) ا هـ .
صلى ركعة من الظهر فأقيم شفعا ويقتدي لأن الأصل أن نقض العبادة قصداً بلا عذر حرام لقوله تعالى {ولا تبطلوا أعمالكم} [محمد: 33] ولإفضائه إلى السفه خصوصاً إذا كانت فرضاً، وأن النقض للإكمال إكمال معنى فيجوز مع إحراز النفل بإضافة ركعة أخرى إليها إذ التطوع شرع شفعاً لا وتراً، ومتى أمكن إدراك العبادتين لا يصار إلى إبطال أحدهما، وقد صرح الكل هنا بأنه إنما يضم ركعة أخرى صيانة للمؤدى عن البطلان وهو صريح فيمن وقول مع محمد بطلان الوصف يستلزم بطلان الأصل هو فيما إذا لم يتمكن من إخراج نفسه عن العهدة بالمضي كما إذا قيد خامسة الظهر بسجدة ولم يكن قعد الأخيرة، أما إذا كان متمكناً من المضي لكن أذن له الشرع في عدمه فلا يبطل أصلها بل تبقى نفلاً إذا ضم الثانية أراد بالظهر الفرض الرباعي وأراد بالإقامة شروع الإمام في موضع هو فيه لا إقامة المؤذن لأنه لا يقطع صلاته إذا أقام المؤذن وإن لم يقيد بالسجدة بل يتمها ركعتين الفراغ من بيان إدراك الفرائض والواجبات والنوافل . قال في النهر وهذا أولى ا هـ .
Chapter: Catching the Obligatory Prayer. His statement: The reality of this chapter is various issues related to obligatory prayers in complete performance, and all are issues of al-Jami'. He said: He prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr and then iqamah is given; he completes it as an even number (two rak'ahs) and then joins the congregation, because the principle is that intentionally invalidating an act of worship without excuse is forbidden due to His statement {Do not invalidate your deeds} [Muhammad:33] and because it leads to frivolity especially if it is an obligatory prayer. And that invalidation for completion is a completion in meaning, so it is permitted, like demolishing a mosque for repair, and like canceling Zuhr for Jumu'ah, and like someone who has a thorn on his forehead in prostration, then lifts then places, it does not count as two prostrations. And the congregation has superiority over prayer alone by hadith, so invalidating the individual prayer is permitted to attain the congregation. But this is when the semblance of completion of his individual prayer is not established; if its semblance is established, he does not invalidate it because the act of worship after it is finished cannot be nullified except by apostasy. So we say: If he prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr, he adds another to it, then says salam and enters with the people, because he can attain the congregation while attaining nafl by adding another rak'ah, since supererogatory prayer is legislated as pairs, not as odd. And whenever it is possible to attain both acts of worship, one should not resort to invalidating one of them. And all have explicitly stated here that he only adds another rak'ah to safeguard the performed prayer from invalidity, and it is explicit that whoever prayed only one rak'ah, it is invalid, not that it is valid but disliked, as some of our later Hanafis have imagined. If it is said: If he adds, he misses the opening takbir, we say: That is easier than invalidating the deed, because safeguarding it from invalidation is obligatory, and attaining the opening takbir is a virtue, and invalidation is permitted for the sake of what is sunnah because it is completion in meaning as we have presented, and meanings are more worthy of consideration than forms, like one who remembers a surah in ruku', he abandons it for its sake even though it is obligatory and ruku' is obligatory, because in his abandonment he is establishing it in the most complete manner, so it becomes good. That is invalidation of the description only. And the statement of Muhammad that invalidation of description necessitates invalidation of the essence is when he is not able to exit from the obligation by proceeding, as when he binds a fifth rak'ah of Zuhr with a prostration and did not sit for the last tashahhud. But if he is able to proceed but the Law permits him not to, then its essence is not invalidated; rather it remains nafl when he adds the second. By Zuhr he means the four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, and by iqamah he means the imam's start in a place where he is, not the mu'adhdhin's iqamah, because he does not cut his prayer when the mu'adhdhin recites iqamah. And even if he did not bind with the prostration, rather he completes it as two rak'ahs as in Ghayat al-Bayan and others. And if iqamah is given in the mosque while he is at home, or if he is in a mosque and iqamah is given in another mosque, he does not cut it at all, as mentioned by the commentator and others. And he restricted by the rak'ah that is completed with prostration because if the first was not completed with prostration, he does cut and starts with the imam, and that is the correct view because he is in a place of abandoning and cutting for completion. Thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Ashbah. And he restricted by obligatory because if he was in nafl, he does not cut at all; rather he completes it. The complete performance is the performance in congregation after finishing explaining the catching of obligatory prayers, obligatory acts, and supererogatory acts. He said in al-Nahr: This is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter 'Catching the Obligatory Prayer' from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It begins by defining the chapter as covering various issues related to complete performance of obligatory prayers. The core matn states that if a person has performed one rak'ah of Zuhr and then the iqamah is given, he should complete it as an even number (i.e., two rak'ahs) and then join the congregation. The commentary explains the underlying principle: intentionally invalidating an act of worship without excuse is forbidden (haram), based on the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (Surah Muhammad, 47:33). However, invalidation for the purpose of completion is considered a meaningful completion, similar to demolishing a mosque for repair or canceling Zuhr to join Jumu'ah. The superiority of congregational prayer over individual prayer, established by hadith, permits one to invalidate the individual prayer to attain the congregation—but only if the individual prayer has not already been completed. If there is a semblance of completion (e.g., one rak'ah already performed without intention to continue?), then one does not invalidate. The commentary further explains that if a person has prayed one rak'ah, he should add another rak'ah to make it two (pair), then say salam, and then join the congregation. This allows him to attain both the congregation and a supererogatory prayer, since supererogatory prayers are legislated in pairs (shaf'), not odd (witr). If it is possible to achieve both, one does not nullify either. The commentator emphasizes that the one rak'ah alone is invalid (batil), not valid but disliked, as some later Hanafis mistakenly held. An objection is raised: adding a rak'ah causes missing the opening takbir of the congregation. The response is that safeguarding the prayer from invalidation (which is obligatory) outweighs the virtue of the opening takbir. Invalidation is permitted for the sake of a sunnah (the congregation) because it is completion in meaning. An analogy is drawn: if one remembers a surah while in ruku', he should abandon the ruku' for the surah even though ruku' is obligatory, because it places the prayer in its most complete form. The passage then discusses that this invalidation is only of the description, not the essence, following the position of Abu Hanifa. Muhammad's view that description invalidation entails essence invalidation is restricted to cases where one cannot exit the obligation by proceeding (e.g., adding a fifth rak'ah to Zuhr without the final tashahhud). If one can proceed but the Law permits otherwise, the essence remains (as nafl) after adding the second rak'ah. The commentator clarifies that 'iqamah' here means the congregation's start, not the mu'adhdhin's call, as the latter does not necessitate cutting. Additional scenarios are covered: if iqamah is given while the person is at home or in a different mosque, he does not cut his prayer at all. If the first rak'ah was not completed with prostration (i.e., still in the early part), then he does cut and join, as per al-Hidayah. The passage also notes that these rulings apply only to obligatory prayers; if one is performing a supererogatory prayer, he does not cut but completes it. The final lines refer back to the chapter's purpose: complete performance means prayer in congregation, and this commentary is part of explaining the catching of obligatory, wajib, and supererogatory prayers.

Key Terms
إدراك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): Catching the obligatory prayer by joining the congregation after having started individually.
البتيراء (al-batīrā'): A prayer consisting of a single rak'ah (odd), which is prohibited and invalid in the Hanafi school for obligatory prayers.
شفعًا (shaf'an): In pairs; making the prayer an even number of rak'ahs (e.g., two) by adding one to the single rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He should stop praying immediately and join the congregation.
B) He should complete the remaining three rak'ahs and then join.
C) He should add one more rak'ah to make it two, say salam, then join the congregation.
D) He should ignore the congregation and finish his four rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
One rak'ah of an obligatory prayer alone is invalid; add a second rak'ah to preserve the prayer as nafl, then join the congregation.
