Cutting Your Prayer to Join the Congregation: The Hanafi Ruling
Explains when cutting a prayer to join congregation is permissible or prohibited

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on cutting an obligatory prayer to join the congregation, explain the istihsan exception of adding a rak'ah, and apply it to different scenarios.

Core Idea
Cutting a valid fard prayer is haram, but if you have completed only one rak'ah, add another to make it nafl, then join the congregation.

Imagine you are in the middle of praying Zuhr alone when the iqamah for congregation begins. What should you do? This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on cutting one's prayer to join the jama'ah. The scholars derive a general prohibition from the Quran, but through istihsan (juristic preference) they permit a specific method that preserves the value of your prayer while earning the superior reward of congregation. We will unpack the proof, the exception, and the conditions that apply.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling and Its Proof
The text opens by declaring that cutting an obligatory prayer is haram, citing the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' (Surah Muhammad 47:33). Understand that this general rule applies to deliberate invalidation without valid reason.
The proof is a Quranic imperative, which in Hanafi usul indicates prohibition unless overridden by a stronger consideration.
2
Understand the Istihsan Exception: Adding a Rak'ah
If you have prayed only one rak'ah of a fard prayer and the congregation begins, you may add a second rak'ah to make it a voluntary prayer (nafl), then say salam and join the imam. This is called 'annulment for completion' (naqd li al-ikmal). The text emphasizes that praying a single rak'ah without a pair is invalid (batil), not just disliked.
The principle is that voluntary prayers are pairs; a single rak'ah is prohibited (al-bitiraa).
3
Apply the Rule to Different Contexts
The passage distinguishes: if you are in a voluntary prayer, you do not cut but complete it as two rak'ahs. For the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, the preferred view (according to the shuyukh) is to complete four rak'ahs rather than cutting after two, because cutting would invalidate the sunnah description.
There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: some scholars (e.g., in Fath al-Qadir) allow cutting after two, but the majority opinion is to complete four.
4
Recognize Exceptions for Necessity
If cutting is due to a genuine need—such as saving a drowning person, extinguishing a fire, or responding to a parent's cry for help—it becomes permissible or even obligatory. The text gives examples: a woman whose pot is boiling, a traveler whose mount runs away, or fear of losing property.
Necessity overrides the general prohibition because preserving life takes priority.
5
Note Cross-Madhhab Differences
The Hanafi school requires adding a rak'ah to preserve the original prayer; the Shafi'i school permits cutting an obligatory prayer for the congregation without adding a rak'ah, considering the congregational reward sufficient. This illustrates how different usul principles lead to different rulings.
Both positions are legitimate; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi for Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرام لقوله تعالى ولا تبطلوا أعمالكم ﴾ [محمد : ۳۳] ولإفضائه إلى السفه خصوصاً إذا كانت فرضاً، وأن النقض للإكمال إكمال معنى فيجوز كنقض المسجد للإصلاح، وكنقض الظهر للجمعة، وكمن أصاب جبهته شوك في سجوده فرفع ثم وضع لم يجعل سجدتين، وللجماعة مزية على الصلاة منفرداً بالحديث فجاز نقض الصلاة منفرداً لإحراز الجماعة، ولكن هذا إذا لم تثبت شبهة الفراغ من صلاته منفرداً وإن ثبتت شبهته لا ينقضها لأن العبادة بعد ما فرغ منها لا تقبل البطلان إلا بالردة فنقول : إن صلى ركعة من الظهر يضم إليها أخرى ثم يسلم ويدخل مع القوم لأنه يمكنه إحراز الجماعة مع إحراز النفل بإضافة ركعة أخرى إليها إذ التطوع شرع شفعاً لا وتراً، ومتى أمكن إدراك العبادتين لا يصار إلى إبطال أحدهما، وقد صرح الكل هنا بأنه إنما يضم ركعة أخرى صيانة للمؤدى عن البطلان وهو صريح فيمن صلى ركعة فقط فهي باطلة لا أنها صحيحة مكروهة كما توهمه بعض حنفية عصرنا. فإن قيل : لو ضم تفوته تكبيرة الافتتاح قلنا : ذلك أيسر من إبطال العمل إذ صيانته عن البطلان واجبة وادراكها فضيلة وجاز الإبطال لما هو سنة لأنه إكمال معنى كما قدمناه والمعاني أحق بالاعتبار من الصور كمن تذكر في الركوع السورة فإنه يرفضه لأجلها مع أنها واجبة وهو فرض لأن في رفضه إقامته على أكمل الوجوه فصار حسناً . أنه إبطال للوصف فقط، وقول مع محمد بطلان الوصف يستلزم بطلان الأصل هو فيما إذا لم يتمكن من إخراج نفسه عن العهدة بالمضي كما إذا قيد خامسة الظهر بسجدة ولم يكن قعد الأخيرة، أما إذا كان متمكناً من المضي لكن أذن له الشرع في عدمه فلا يبطل أصلها بل تبقى نفلاً إذا ضم الثانية أراد بالظهر الفرض الرباعي وأراد بالإقامة شروع الإمام في موضع هو فيه لا إقامة المؤذن لأنه لا يقطع صلاته إذا أقام المؤذن وإن لم يقيد بالسجدة بل يتمها ركعتين كما في غاية البيان وغيره. ولو أقيمت في المسجد وهو في البيت أو كان في مسجد فأقيمت في مسجد آخر لا يقطعها مطلقاً كما ذكره الشارح وغيره. وقيد بالركعة التي تتم بالسجدة لأنه لو لم يقيد الأولى بالسجدة فإنه يقطع ويشرع مع الإمام وهو الصحيح لأنه بمحل الرفض والقطع للإكمال. كذا في الهداية. وفي الأشبه. وقيد بالفرض لأنه لو كان في النفل لا يقطع مطلقاً وإنما يتمه ركعتين. واختلفوا في السنة قبل الظهر أو الجمعة إذا أقيمت أو خطب الإمام فالصحيح أنه يتمها أربعاً كما صرح به الولوالجي وصاحب المبتغى والمحيط ثم الشمني لأنها صلاة واحدة وليس القطع للإكمال بل للإبطال صورة ومعنى. وقيل يقطع على رأس الركعتين، ورجحه في فتح القدير بحثاً بأنه يتمكن من قضائها بعد الفرض ولا إبطال في التسليم على الركعتين فلا يفوت فرض الاستماع والأداء على الوجه الأكمل بلا سبب اهـ. والظاهر ما صححه المشايخ لأنه لا شك أن في التسليم على رأس الركعتين إبطال وصف السنية لا لإكمالها، وتقدم أنه لا يجوز ويشهد لهم إثبات أحكام الصلاة الواحدة للأربع من عدم الاستفتاح والتعوذ في الشفع الثاني إلى غير ذلك كما قدمناه وأراد من الظهر الظهر المؤدى لأنه لو شرع في قضاء الفوائت ثم أقيمت لا يقطع كالنفل والمنذورة كالفائتة كذا في الخلاصة، وقيدنا يكون الإبطال حراماً لغير عذر لأنه لو كان لعذر فإنه جائز كالمرأة إذا فار قدرها والمسافر إذا ندت دابته أو خاف فوت درهم من ماله بل قد يكون واجباً كالقطع لإنجاء غريق. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي : المصلي إذا دعاه أحد أبويه فلا يجيبه ما لم يفرغ من صلاته إلا أن يستغيث به لأن قطع الصلاة لا يجوز إلا لضرورة، وكذلك الأجنبي إذا خاف أن يسقط من سطح أو تحرقه النار أو يغرقه الماء وجب عليه أن يقطع الصلاة هذا إذا كان في الفرض، فأما في النوافل إذا ناداه أحد أبويه إن علم أنه في الصلاة وناداه لا بأس به أن لا يجيبه، وإن لم يعلم يجيبه ا هـ . ومن العذر ما إذا شرع في نفل فحضرت جنازة خاف إن لم يقطعها تفوته فإنه
It is forbidden due to His statement: 'And do not invalidate your deeds' [Muhammad: 33], and because it leads to foolishness, especially if it is obligatory. And that annulment for completion is a completion of meaning, so it is permissible like the annulment of a mosque for repair, and like the annulment of Zuhr for Jumu'ah, and like the case of one whose forehead is pricked by a thorn in his prostration, so he raises it then places it, it is not considered two prostrations. And the congregation has superiority over praying alone according to the hadith, so annulment of praying alone is permissible to achieve the congregation. But this is when the semblance of completion of one's prayer alone is not established; if its semblance is established, he does not annul it, because the worship after it is completed is not subject to invalidation except by apostasy. So we say: If he prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr, he adds another to it, then says salam and enters with the people, because he can achieve the congregation while achieving the nafl by adding another rak'ah to it, since supererogatory prayer is legislated in pairs, not single. And whenever it is possible to achieve both acts of worship, one should not resort to invalidating one of them. And everyone here stated that he only adds another rak'ah to protect the performed act from invalidity, and it is clear regarding one who prayed only one rak'ah that it is invalid, not that it is valid but disliked, as some of our contemporary Hanafis imagined. If it is said: If he adds, he misses the opening takbir. We say: That is easier than invalidating the deed, because protecting it from invalidity is obligatory, and achieving it is a virtue. And invalidation is permissible for what is a sunnah, because it is a completion of meaning as we have mentioned, and meanings are more worthy of consideration than forms, like the one who remembers during ruku' that he omitted the surah, so he abandons it for its sake, even though it is obligatory and he is in a fard act, because in abandoning it he establishes it in the most complete manner, so it becomes good. It is only an invalidation of the description. And the statement of Muhammad that the invalidation of the description necessitates the invalidation of the original applies when he is unable to discharge himself by proceeding, such as if he tied a fifth rak'ah of Zuhr with a prostration and did not sit for the last sitting. But if he is able to proceed but the Law permits him not to, then its original is not invalidated; rather it remains as nafl when he adds the second. He meant by Zuhr the four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, and by iqamah he meant the imam's starting in the place where he is, not the muezzin's iqamah, because he does not cut his prayer when the muezzin makes iqamah, even if he did not tie it with the prostration; rather he completes it as two rak'ahs, as in Ghayat al-Bayan and others. And if iqamah is made in the mosque while he is in the house, or he is in a mosque and iqamah is made in another mosque, he does not cut it at all, as the commentator and others mentioned. And he restricted it to the rak'ah that is completed with prostration, because if he did not tie the first with prostration, he cuts and starts with the imam, and that is the correct view, because he is in a place of abandonment and cutting for completion. This is in al-Hidayah. And in al-Ashbah. And he restricted it to the obligatory, because if he was in a voluntary prayer, he does not cut at all; rather he completes it as two rak'ahs. And they differed regarding the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah when iqamah is made or the imam delivers the sermon; the correct view is that he completes it as four, as stated by al-Walwaliji, the author of al-Mubtagha, al-Muhit, and then al-Shamni, because it is one prayer, and cutting is not for completion but for invalidation in form and meaning. And it is said he cuts at the end of two rak'ahs, and this was preferred in Fath al-Qadir by research, because he is able to make it up after the obligatory prayer, and there is no invalidation in saying salam after two rak'ahs, so he does not miss the obligation of listening and performing in the most complete manner without cause. The apparent view is what the shuyukh corrected, because there is no doubt that in saying salam at the end of two rak'ahs there is an invalidation of the description of being sunnah, not for its completion, and it has been stated that it is not permissible. And what supports them is the establishment of the rulings of one prayer for four, such as not reciting opening supplication and seeking refuge in the second pair, etc., as we have mentioned. And he meant by Zuhr the performed Zuhr, because if he started making up missed prayers and then iqamah was made, he does not cut, like a voluntary prayer and a vowed prayer like a missed one, as in al-Khulasah. And we have restricted that invalidation is forbidden without an excuse, because if it is due to an excuse, then it is permissible, like a woman when her pot is boiling, or a traveler when his mount runs away, or he fears losing a dirham of his wealth; indeed it may be obligatory, like cutting to save a drowning person. In the Fatawa of al-Walwaliji: The praying person, if one of his parents calls him, he does not respond until he finishes his prayer, unless he cries for help, because cutting the prayer is not permissible except for necessity. Similarly, if a stranger fears that someone will fall from a roof, or be burned by fire, or drowned by water, it is obligatory for him to cut the prayer. This is when it is an obligatory prayer. As for voluntary prayers, if one of his parents calls him, if he knows that he is in prayer and calls him, it is fine if he does not answer; but if he does not know, he answers. And among the excuses is when he starts a voluntary prayer and then a funeral prayer is present, and he fears that if he does not cut it he will miss it, then he
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a detailed commentary on the chapter of catching the obligatory prayer (Idrak al-Faridah). It opens by establishing the general principle: cutting one's prayer to join the congregation is haram (forbidden), based on the Quranic verse 'Do not invalidate your deeds' and because it leads to foolishness, especially for obligatory prayers. However, the Hanafi school allows an exception through istihsan: if one has only prayed one rak'ah of an obligatory prayer and then the congregation begins, he may add another rak'ah to make it a voluntary prayer (nafl), then say salam and join the imam. This preserves the value of his prayer while allowing him to attain the reward of congregation. The author refutes the misunderstanding that such a single rak'ah is valid but disliked; it is actually invalid (batil) because praying a single rak'ah without a pair is prohibited (the 'bitiraa' is forbidden). The text then addresses objections: missing the opening takbir is a lesser loss than invalidating the entire prayer. Further rules are discussed: if one is in a voluntary prayer, he does not cut but completes it as two rak'ahs; the iqamah refers to the imam's starting, not the muezzin's call; if one is in a different location, he does not cut. For the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, the preferred view among the shuyukh is to complete it as four rak'ahs, as cutting would invalidate its sunnah quality. Exceptions for necessity include saving a drowning person, a parent's distress call, or avoiding harm. This passage shows the Hanafi method of balancing textual proofs with istihsan (juristic preference) to achieve maslahah.

Key Terms
البتيراء (al-bitiraa): A prayer that consists of only one rak'ah without a second, considered invalid because it goes against the nature of voluntary prayers being in pairs.
النقض للإكمال (al-naqd li al-ikmal): Annulment (of a prayer) for the purpose of completing it in a better manner, e.g., by joining the congregation; permissible when it leads to a more perfect worship.
إدراك الجماعة (idrak al-jama'ah): Catching the congregational prayer, which has a higher reward than praying alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if he has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr and then the congregation for Zuhr begins?
A) He must cut his prayer immediately and join the imam, not completing the first rak'ah.
B) He should add another rak'ah to make it two, say salam, and then join the congregation.
C) He should complete his prayer as four rak'ahs alone, ignoring the congregation.
D) His single rak'ah is valid and he can join after saying salam.

Key Takeaway
Cutting a fard prayer is generally haram, but if you are at one rak'ah, add a second to make it nafl before joining the congregation, thus preserving the prayer's validity and earning the reward of jama'ah.

Dispute on Completing Sunna of Zuhr/Jumu'ah When Iqama Is Called
Intra-Hanafi dispute on completing four vs. cutting two

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on whether to complete four rak'ahs or cut after two when the iqama is called for Zuhr or Jumu'ah, and explain the reasoning based on the integrity of the single prayer.

Core Idea
The four rak'ahs of sunna before Zuhr/Jumu'ah are one prayer; cutting early invalidates its sunniyya.

When the iqama is called during the sunna prayer before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, a Hanafi musalli faces a dilemma: should he complete all four rak'ahs or cut short at two? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue, where the majority of mashayikh uphold completing four as the correct view, while some scholars allow cutting. Understanding the reasoning behind the preferred position is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and triggering condition
What is the specific act? The sunna mu'akkada before Zuhr or Jumu'ah. What triggers the dilemma? The iqama being called or the khatib ascending.
The sunna here is four rak'ahs according to the Hanafi school.
2
State the two positions
Position 1: Complete the four rak'ahs as one prayer. Position 2: Cut after two rak'ahs and then join the congregation.
The author of Fath al-Qadir preferred the second position.
3
Examine the majority's proof
The four rak'ahs are a single prayer, evidenced by rulings like absence of istiftah and ta'awwudh in the second pair. Cutting at two invalidates the sunniyya (supererogatory nature).
Ibtal of sunna is prohibited without valid excuse.
4
Examine the opposing view's reasoning
Opponents argue that the sunna can be made up after the fard, and ending early does not invalidate anything; it allows one to join the congregation on time.
They do not consider the four as an indivisible unit.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and tarjih
The mashayikh (earlier authorities) corrected the view that completing four is correct. This is the relied-upon position because cutting invalidates the sunniyya, which is not allowed.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ركعتين. واختلفوا في السنة قبل الظهر أو الجمعة إذا أقيمت أو خطب الإمام فالصحيح أنه يتمها أربعاً كما صرح به الولوالجي وصاحب المبتغى والمحيط ثم الشمني لأنها صلاة واحدة وليس القطع للإكمال بل للإبطال صورة ومعنى. وقيل يقطع على رأس الركعتين، ورجحه في فتح القدير بحثاً بأنه يتمكن من قضائها بعد الفرض ولا إبطال في التسليم على الركعتين فلا يفوت فرض الاستماع والأداء على الوجه الأكمل بلا سبب اهـ. والظاهر ما صححه المشايخ لأنه لا شك أن في التسليم على رأس الركعتين إبطال وصف السنية لا لإكمالها، وتقدم أنه لا يجوز ويشهد لهم إثبات أحكام الصلاة الواحدة للأربع من عدم الاستفتاح والتعوذ في الشفع الثاني إلى غير ذلك كما قدمناه
Two rak'ahs. And they disagreed concerning the sunna before Zuhr or Jumu'ah when the iqama is given or the khatib ascends: the correct view is that he completes it as four, as stated by al-Walwaliji and the author of al-Mubtagha and al-Muhit and al-Shimni, because it is one prayer and cutting it is not for completion but for invalidation in form and meaning. And it was said that he cuts at the end of two rak'ahs, and it was preferred in Fath al-Qadir as an investigation because he can make it up after the fard and there is no invalidation in ending after two rak'ahs, so he does not miss the obligation of listening and performing in the most complete manner without cause. And what appears is what the mashayikh corrected because there is no doubt that ending after two rak'ahs invalidates the description of sunniyya and not for its completion, and it has preceded that it is not permissible; and their support is the establishment of the rulings of one prayer for the four, like the absence of istiftah and ta'awwudh in the second pair, and other things, as we have mentioned.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on completing the sunna of Zuhr or Jumu'ah when the iqama is called or the khatib ascends. The issue is whether one should complete four rak'ahs (the full sunna) or cut after two. The author cites that the correct view according to many Hanafi authorities is to complete four rak'ahs, as stated by al-Walwaliji and others. Their reasoning: the four rak'ahs of sunna are a single prayer in the Hanafi school, indicated by rulings such as not reciting istiftah and ta'awwudh in the second pair. Cutting at two would invalidate the prayer's sunniyya (its supererogatory nature). The opposing view, preferred by the author of Fath al-Qadir, says one may cut after two rak'ahs because the sunna can be made up after the fard, and ending early does not invalidate anything. The author then states that the relied-upon view (zahir) is what the mashayikh (earlier scholars) corrected: completing four. This is because ending at two rak'ahs invalidates the sunniyya of the prayer, which is not allowed. The passage also notes that this dispute is specific to the sunna before Zuhr or Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunna): Recommended prayer, here specifically the sunna mu'akkada before Zuhr or Jumu'ah.
الإبطال (al-ibtal): Invalidation of the supererogatory nature of the prayer by cutting before completion.
المشايخ (al-mashayikh): The early authoritative Hanafi scholars who corrected the relied-upon view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what should you do if you are praying the sunna of Zuhr and the iqama is called after you have completed two rak'ahs?
A) Cut the sunna and join the congregation.
B) Complete four rak'ahs, then join the congregation.
C) Continue until you finish four rak'ahs and then do not join.
D) Stop immediately and do not join.

Key Takeaway
The four rak'ahs of sunna before Zuhr/Jumu'ah are a single prayer; cutting early when iqama is called invalidates its sunniyya, so the relied-upon Hanafi view is to complete all four.

Cutting Salah for Emergencies: Permissibility and Obligation
Ruling on cutting salah for necessity with examples from fard and nafl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting salah during emergency and distinguish between permissible and obligatory cases.

Core Idea
Cutting salah is haram without excuse, but becomes permissible – even obligatory – to save life or property.

The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the nuanced rulings on cutting salah. While the default is that deliberately invalidating prayer is prohibited, the Shariah provides dispensations for genuine emergencies. This lesson will guide you through the scenarios that transform cutting from haram to permissible or wajib, and the specific application to fard and nafl prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The passage establishes that invalidating (ibṭāl) one's salah without a valid excuse is ḥarām or makrūh taḥrīmī.
This default sets the baseline: cutting is prohibited unless an excuse exists.
2
Recognize excusable cases
Examples include a woman whose pot boils over, a traveller whose mount bolts, or fear of losing money. These make cutting permissible (jāʾiz).
The common illa (cause) is imminent loss of property or harm.
3
Differentiate between fard and nafl
For fard, one should not respond to a parent's call unless the parent is seeking help (istighātha). For nafl, the ruling is more lenient: if the parent knows the child is praying, it is fine not to answer; otherwise, he may answer.
The difference stems from the binding nature of fard versus the lesser commitment of nafl.
4
Distinguish permissible from wajib
Cutting becomes wājib when necessary to save a life (e.g., drowning person) or prevent extreme harm. The passage explicitly states 'بل قد يكون واجباً كالقطع لإنجاء غريق'.
Saving life overrides the obligation of prayer; this is a higher priority.
5
Understand consequences of cutting
Cutting a nafl requires qaḍāʾ (making it up), whereas missing a funeral prayer without cutting is irrecoverable.
The text: 'وقطع النفل معقب للقضاء بخلاف الجنازة لو اختار تفويتها كان لا إلى خلف.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيدنا يكون الإبطال حراماً لغير عذر لأنه لو كان لعذر فإنه جائز كالمرأة إذا فار قدرها والمسافر إذا ندت دابته أو خاف فوت درهم من ماله بل قد يكون واجباً كالقطع لإنجاء غريق. وفي فتاوى الولوالجي : المصلي إذا دعاه أحد أبويه فلا يجيبه ما لم يفرغ من صلاته إلا أن يستغيث به لأن قطع الصلاة لا يجوز إلا لضرورة، وكذلك الأجنبي إذا خاف أن يسقط من سطح أو تحرقه النار أو يغرقه الماء وجب عليه أن يقطع الصلاة هذا إذا كان في الفرض، فأما في النوافل إذا ناداه أحد أبويه إن علم أنه في الصلاة وناداه لا بأس به أن لا يجيبه، وإن لم يعلم يجيبه ا هـ . ومن العذر ما إذا شرع في نفل فحضرت جنازة خاف إن لم يقطعها تفوته فإنه يقطعها ويصلي عليها لأنه لا يتمكن من المصلحتين معاً، وقطع النفل معقب للقضاء بخلاف الجنازة لو اختار تفويتها كان لا إلى خلف. كذا في فتح القدير
And we have restricted that invalidation is haram without an excuse because if there is an excuse then it is permissible, like a woman when her pot boils over, and a traveller when his mount bolts, or he fears losing a dirham from his wealth; indeed it may become obligatory, like cutting to save a drowning person. And in Fatawa al-Walwaliji: if one of a worshipper's parents calls him, he should not answer unless he has finished his prayer, unless the parent seeks his help, because cutting prayer is not permissible except for necessity. Similarly, if an outsider fears that [someone] might fall from a roof or be burned by fire or drowned by water, he must cut his prayer. This applies to fard. As for nafl prayers, if one of his parents calls him, if he knows that the parent is aware he is in prayer, it is fine not to answer; if not, he answers. And among the excuses is when someone starts a nafl and then a funeral arrives and he fears he will miss it, so he cuts the nafl and prays over it, because he cannot combine both benefits. And cutting a nafl is followed by qada, unlike the funeral if he chooses to miss it, it would be without recourse. Thus in Fath al-Qadir.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on cutting a prayer due to emergencies. The author first states that invalidating prayer (i.e., cutting it deliberately) is haram (or makruh tahrimi) without a valid excuse. However, with a valid excuse, it becomes permissible. Examples of permissible cutting: a woman whose cooking pot is boiling over, a traveller whose mount runs away, or if one fears losing money. In some cases, cutting becomes wajib, such as to save a drowning person. The passage then quotes from Fatawa al-Walwaliji: if a parent calls during fard, one should not respond unless the parent is calling for help (e.g., danger). For nafl, if the parent knows the child is praying, it is better not to answer; if the parent does not know, one may answer. Also, if one is praying nafl and a funeral prayer is about to be missed, he should cut his nafl to pray the funeral. This is because he cannot simultaneously attend to both the nafl and the funeral; and cutting nafl is compensated by making it up later, but missing the funeral is not recoverable.

Key Terms
الإبطال (al-ibtal): Cutting or invalidating a prayer deliberately.
الضرورة (al-darura): A situation of extreme necessity that permits cutting the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is cutting a fard prayer wajib according to the passage?
A) When a parent calls.
B) When a pot boils over.
C) To save a drowning person.
D) When fearing loss of a dirham.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, cutting salah is only excused for genuine necessity; saving life makes it wajib.

Completing a Fard Prayer When Congregation Starts: Three Rak'ahs Already Prayed
Ruling with proof for the case of three rak'ahs prayed alone before congregation begins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard when the iqama is given, and explain the proof from the hadith and the intra-madhhab difference.

Core Idea
If you have prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr alone, complete the fourth then join the congregation as a volunteer – do not cut.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: you begin a fard prayer alone, and after some rak'ahs the congregational prayer is announced. What should you do? The Hanafi school distinguishes between having prayed only one rak'ah and having prayed three. Here we focus on the latter: the ruling is to complete the fourth rak'ah, then join the congregation as a nafl prayer. We examine the evidence from hadith and the preferred view within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The text discusses a person who has prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard (like Zuhr). The Hanafi ruling is: he must complete the fourth rak'ah and then follow the imam with the intention of nafl (voluntary prayer).
Cutting the prayer without completing the fourth would be sinful.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told two men who had already prayed in their homes to join the congregation and make their prayer nafl. This indicates that a prayer already performed can be converted to nafl when joining the congregation.
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), so its thubut is zanni, but its meaning supports the ruling.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (reasoning)
The key principle: 'the majority has the ruling of the whole'. Having completed three out of four rak'ahs, the prayer is treated as if it were whole. Therefore, it cannot be annulled; instead, the fourth is completed to make it a valid four-rak'ah prayer, which then becomes nafl when joined with the congregation.
This is why the ruling differs from the one-rak'ah case, where the prayer can be cut.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some early Hanafi scholars (e.g., Fakhr al-Islam) held that the person should cut with a single salam after three rak'ahs and then join. They argued that the position after three is a 'place of rejection' (mahl al-rafd).
However, the majority (zahir al-riwayah) prefers completing the fourth.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon view for fatwa is to complete the fourth rak'ah and then join the congregation as a volunteer. This is the position of al-Hidayah, Ghayat al-Bayan, and is deemed wajib (obligatory).
One should not resort to legal stratagems (hiyal) to avoid completing, as finishing is obligatory.

Source Text

فإن صلى ركعة من الفجر أو المغرب فأقيم يقطع ويقتدي وكره خروجه من مسجد أذن يقطعها ويصلي عليها لأنه لا يتمكن من المصلحتين معاً، وقطع النفل معقب للقضاء بخلاف الجنازة لو اختار تفويتها كان لا إلى خلف. كذا في فتح القدير .
قوله : (ولو صلى ثلاثاً يتم ويقتدي متطوعاً لأن للأكثر حكم الكل فلا يحتمل النقض وإنما يقتدي متطوعاً لأن الفرض لا يتكرر في وقت واحد. وصرح في الحاوي القدسي أن ما يؤدي مع الإمام نافلة يدرك بها فضيلة الجماعة ولا يرد عليه العصر فإنه لا يقتدي بعدها لما علم من باب الأوقات المكروهة، ولهذا قيد بالظهر قيد بالثلاث لأنه لو كان في ولم يقيدها بالسجدة فإنه يقطعها لأنه بمحل الرفض ويتخيران شاء عاد وقعد وسلم وإن شاء كبر ينوي الدخول في صلاة الإمام. كذا في الهداية. وفي المحيط : الأصح أنه يقطع قائماً بتسليمة واحدة لأن القعود مشروط للتحلل وهذا قطع وليس بتحلل فإن التحلل عن الظهر لا يكون على رأس الركعتين وتكفيه تسليمة واحدة للقطع ا.هـ. وهكذا صححه في غاية البيان معزياً إلى فخر الإسلام واختلفوا فيما إذا عاد هل يعيد التشهد؟ قيل نعم لأن الأول لم يكن قعود ختم، وقيل يكفيه ذلك التشهد لأنه لما قعد ارتفض ذلك القيام فكأنه لم يقم وأورد على قوله «ويقتدي متطوعاً أن التطوع بجماعة مكروه خارج رمضان. وأجيب بنعم إذا كان الإمام والقوم متطوعين، أما إذا أدى الإمام الفرض والقوم النفل فلا لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام للرجلين : إذا صليتما في رحالكما ثم أتيتما صلاة قوم فصليا معهم واجعلا
يقطع فإن فيه إشارة إلى أنه لو أقيمت قبل شروعه يقدم الحاضرة والذي يظهر لي أرجحية هذا إذ في الابتداء بالفائتة والحالة هذه تفويت فضيلة الجماعة وليس في الابتداء بالحاضرة تفويت ذلك . تأمل وراجع فعسى تظفر بالمنقول. ثم نقل عن النووي أن الأفضل الترتيب للخلاف في وجوبه، وعن الأسنوي البداءة بالحاضرة جماعة ثم قال : فانظر كيف اختلف مثل هؤلاء الأجلاء في ترجيح أحد الوجهين وقواعدنا لا تأبى ذلك في سافط الترتيب فإن مذهبنا كمذهبهم فيه ا هـ ويظهر لي أرجحيته ما رجحه لأن الجماعة واجبة عندنا أو في حكم الواجب ومراعاة خلاف الإمام مالك مستحبة فلا ينبغي تفويت الواجب لأجل المستحب تأمل قول المصنف (ولو صلى ثلاثاً يتم) قال أي الرملي وجوباً فلو قطع واقتدي كان آثماً ا هـ . قلت : لكن في التاتارخانية : وإن أراد أن يكون فرضه ما يصلي مع الإمام فالحيلة أن لا يقعد في الرابعة من صلاته التي أداها وحده ويصلي ويصير ذلك نفلاً ويكون فرضه ما يصلي مع الإمام ثم نقل بعده أيضاً الحيلة أن يصلي الرابعة قاعداً فتنقلب هذه نقلاً عندهما خلافاً لمحمد ا هـ . فليتأمل، ثم رأيت في القهستاني ذكر أن في قوله «يتم» إشارة إلى أنه لا يشتغل بحيلة مثل أن لا يقعد على الرابعة ويصيرها ستاً كما في المحيط، ومثل أن يصلي الرابعة قاعداً لتنقلب نفلاً لأن الإتمام فرض كما في المنية ا هـ. قوله: (ولهذا قيد بالظهر) قال الرملي أقول : هذا يناقض ما تقدم قريباً من أن المراد بالظهر الرباعية تأمل
If he prays one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib and then the iqama is given, he cuts and follows [the imam], and it is disliked for him to leave the mosque after the adhan... He cuts it and prays over it because he cannot combine both benefits. And cutting a nafl is followed by qada, unlike the funeral if he chooses to miss it, it would be without recourse. Thus in Fath al-Qadir.
His statement: (And if he prays three rak'ahs, he completes and follows as a volunteer, because the majority has the ruling of the whole, so it does not bear annulment. He only follows as a volunteer because the fard does not repeat at one time. And it is stated in al-Hawi al-Qudsi that what he performs with the imam is nafl, he attains the virtue of congregation. And Asr is not objected to, for he does not follow after it, as known from the chapter on disliked times. For this reason, he restricted to Zuhr and restricted to three; because if he had not completed it with the sajda, he cuts it because it is at the place of rejection. And he has a choice: if he wishes, he returns, sits, and says salam; if he wishes, he says takbir intending to enter the imam's prayer. Thus in al-Hidayah. And in al-Muhit: the most correct is that he cuts standing with one salam, because sitting is a condition for tahlil, and this is a cut and not tahlil, for the tahlil of Zuhr is not at the end of two rak'ahs; one salam suffices for cutting. This is also corrected in Ghayat al-Bayan, attributed to Fakhr al-Islam. And they differed concerning if he returns: should he repeat the tashahhud? It was said yes, because the first was not a concluding sitting. And it was said that tashahhud suffices, because when he sat, that standing was abrogated, as if he had not stood. And an objection was raised against his saying 'and he follows as a volunteer' that performing a voluntary [with congregation] is disliked outside Ramadan. It was answered: yes, if the imam and people are volunteers. But if the imam performs fard and the people nafl, then no, because of his saying (peace be upon him) to the two men: 'When you have prayed in your homes, then come to a congregational prayer, pray with them and make it...'
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage addresses two scenarios when a person has started a fard prayer alone and then the congregational prayer is begun. First, if one has prayed one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib, he should cut his prayer and join the congregation. It is disliked to leave the mosque after the adhan. The reason is that he cannot attain both benefits (completing his own prayer and the congregation). Cutting a nafl requires qada, but missing the funeral (if that were the case) is irreversible. Second, if one has prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard (like Zuhr), he does not cut but completes the fourth rak'ah and then joins the congregation as a volunteer (nafl). The majority has the ruling of the whole, so he cannot annul the three rak'ahs. He prays the fourth and then follows the imam with the intention of nafl. The passage discusses various opinions: some say he should cut after three rak'ahs with a salam, but the preferred view is to complete and then join. There is also a discussion about whether to repeat tashahhud if he returns, and the dislike of volunteering in congregation outside Ramadan is addressed by distinguishing when the imam leads fard versus nafl. The author also mentions a hila (legal trick) from al-Tatarkhaniyya: if one wants his prayer to be nafl, he can avoid sitting for tashahhud in the fourth and instead stand for a fifth, making it a six-rak'ah nafl, or pray the fourth sitting to convert it to nafl. However, the relied-upon view is that completion is obligatory, so one should not resort to such hiyal. The passage ends with a warning that the restriction to Zuhr might contradict earlier statements about the sunna.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): Pair of rak'ahs; here refers to completing a pair of rak'ahs within a prayer.
الحيلة (al-hila): A legal stratagem to achieve a different ruling while staying within the law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what should a person do if he has prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr alone and then the iqama for Zuhr congregation is given?
A) Cut the prayer immediately with a salam and join the congregation.
B) Complete the fourth rak'ah, then join the congregation as a volunteer.
C) Complete the fourth rak'ah as fard and do not join.
D) Abandon the prayer entirely and start fresh with the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi ruling is to complete the fourth rak'ah as nafl and then join the congregation, based on the principle that the majority of the prayer is treated as the whole.

Cutting a Current Prayer to Join Congregation: Fajr and Maghrib Cases
Commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding cutting prayer to join congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has performed one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib and then the iqamah is called, and identify the condition that determines whether he must cut or complete his prayer.

Core Idea
Preserving the congregation is wajib, so cut your current prayer unless you have already prostrated the second rak'ah.

This lesson tackles a practical scenario: you start praying Fajr or Maghrib alone, and after the first rak'ah you hear the iqamah. What should you do? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the priority of congregation over completing an individual prayer. We will examine the ruling, its reasoning through the maxim 'the majority has the ruling of the whole', and the critical condition that changes the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
We are dealing with a person who has performed one rak'ah of a two-rak'ah (Fajr) or three-rak'ah (Maghrib) fard prayer individually, and then the iqamah for the congregational prayer is called.
The prayer is fard, but the individual is praying alone, not with the congregation.
2
State the primary ruling
The person must cut his current prayer (by giving one salam) and join the imam in congregation. This is wajib.
Cutting means exiting the prayer before its completion.
3
Understand the reasoning
If he were to add another rak'ah, he would either complete the prayer exactly when the congregation starts (Fajr) or reach a majority (Maghrib, where two out of three rak'ahs counts as the whole due to the maxim). This would cause him to miss the congregation entirely, which is given priority.
The maxim 'li'l-akthar hukm al-kull' (the majority has the ruling of the whole) is applied here.
4
Recognize the condition
The ruling applies only if the person has not yet performed the prostration (sajdah) of the second rak'ah. If he has already prostrated in the second rak'ah, he must complete his prayer and not join, because it is disliked to perform supererogatory (nafl) prayer after Fajr or Maghrib.
The prostration of the second rak'ah marks the point where the majority is considered done; cutting at that stage would be futile.
5
Note the authority
This ruling is found in the zahir al-riwayah and is supported by Fath al-Qadir and al-Kafi. The evidence is based on qiyas (analogy) that preserving the congregation takes precedence.
The weight of authority: zahir al-riwayah and later tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن صلى ركعة من الفجر أو المغرب فأقيم يقطع ويقتدي لأنه لو أضاف إليها أخرى لفاتته الجماعة لوجود الفراغ حقيقة في الفجر أو شبهه في المغرب لأن للأكثر حكم الكل. وقطع النفل معقب للقضاء بخلاف الجنازة لو اختار تفويتها كان لا إلى خلف. كذا في فتح القدير . قوله : (فإن صلى ركعة من الفجر أو المغرب فأقيم يقطع ويقتدي لأنه لو أضاف إليها أخرى لفاتته الجماعة لوجود الفراغ حقيقة في الفجر أو شبهه في المغرب لأن للأكثر حكم الكل. وشمل كلامه ما إذا قام إلى الثانية ولم يقيدها بالسجدة، وقيد بالركعة احترازاً عما إذا قيد الثانية بسجدة فإنه لا يقطعها ويتمها ولا يشرع مع الإمام لكراهة النفل بعد الفجر، وكذا بعد المغرب في ظاهر الرواية.
If he prays one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib, and the iqamah is called, he cuts (his prayer) and follows (the imam), because if he were to add another to it, the congregation would be lost, due to the presence of actual completion in Fajr or its likeness in Maghrib, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. Cutting the supererogatory is a follower to making up, unlike the funeral prayer; if he chose to miss it, it would be without consequence. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. His statement: (If he prays one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib and the iqamah is called, he cuts and follows, because if he were to add another to it, the congregation would be lost, due to the presence of actual completion in Fajr or its likeness in Maghrib, because the majority has the ruling of the whole.) And his speech includes the case when he stood for the second and did not tie it with a prostration, and he restricted it to the one rak'ah to avoid the case when he tied the second with a prostration, for then he does not cut it but completes it and does not join the imam, due to the dislike of supererogatory prayer after Fajr, and similarly after Maghrib in the apparent transmission.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school, explaining the case of a person who has prayed one rak'ah of a two-rak'ah or three-rak'ah obligatory prayer (Fajr or Maghrib) and then the iqamah for the congregational prayer is called. The ruling is that he must cut his individual prayer and join the congregation. The reasoning is that if he were to add another rak'ah to complete his prayer, he would miss the congregation entirely (for Fajr, completing two rak'ahs would mean finishing just as the congregation starts; for Maghrib, adding a third would make it three but delay him, so the majority opinion applies). Since the majority (three out of four rak'ahs) has the ruling of the whole, he cannot continue. The text clarifies that cutting a supererogatory prayer in this case is commendable for the sake of making up the fard later, unlike a funeral prayer where missing it has no compensation. A key condition is that this applies only if he has not performed the prostration of the second rak'ah. If he has already prostrated in the second rak'ah (i.e., he is close to finishing), he should complete his prayer and not join the congregation, because it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayer after Fajr or Maghrib. This ruling is based on the principle that preserving the congregation (which is wajib) takes precedence over completing a nafal that would cause delay.

Key Terms
يقطع (yaqta'): To cut the current prayer by giving one salam, exiting the prayer prematurely.
للأكثر حكم الكل (li'l-akthar hukm al-kull): The majority of the prayer has the same ruling as the complete prayer, so continuing after the majority is not allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a person prays one rak'ah of Fajr and then the iqamah is called, what should he do?
A) He should complete his two rak'ahs and then join the congregation.
B) He should cut his prayer with one salam and join the imam.
C) He should continue his prayer but delay joining until after finishing.
D) He should not cut and instead pray alone.

Key Takeaway
Preserving the congregation is prioritized over completing an individual prayer; if you have prayed one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib and iqamah is called before prostrating the second rak'ah, you must cut and join.

Cutting Optional Prayer at Iqamah for Fajr or Maghrib
Ruling on cutting one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib to join congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting the sunnah prayer of Fajr or Maghrib when iqamah is called, identify the condition that determines whether to cut or complete, and explain why the ruling is makruh tahrimi based on the hadith of al-Batira'.

Core Idea
Cut before the second prostration; after it, complete but do not join the congregation.

When the iqamah sounds while you are in the middle of the sunnah prayer of Fajr or Maghrib, a precise ruling applies depending on how far you have progressed. The Hanafi school distinguishes between cutting immediately and completing the prayer alone. This lesson unpacks the conditions, the evidence from the hadith of al-Batira', and the scholarly differences within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
The passage addresses a person who has prayed one rak'ah of the Fajr or Maghrib sunnah and the iqamah is called. The immediate ruling is to cut and join the congregation, because adding a second rak'ah would cause missing the congregation.
This applies when the second rak'ah has not yet reached prostration.
2
Find the exception condition
If the person has already prostrated in the second rak'ah, the ruling changes: he must complete the prayer and not join the congregation, due to the dislike (karahah) of performing sunnah after Fajr and Maghrib.
The key is whether the second prostration (sajdah) has occurred.
3
Analyze the evidence for the ruling
The scholars cite the hadith of al-Batira' — the Prophet forbade 'cutting off the tail' of prayer. This hadith, while zanni al-thubut, is qati al-dalalah, leading to the ruling of makruh tahrimi (prohibitive dislike) according to Hanafi usul.
The prohibition (nahy) indicates impermissibility; combined with the hadith's transmission, it yields makruh tahrimi, not haram.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi authorities (Qadi Khan) considered it haram, others bid'ah, but al-Hidayah and the majority hold it to be makruh tahrimi. The mufta bihi position is makruh tahrimi.
The text clarifies that 'karahah' in the apparent narration means prohibitive dislike.
5
Understand the consequence if one follows the Imam
If the person joins the congregation despite the prohibition, and the Imam mistakenly prays four rak'ahs in Maghrib, the follower's prayer becomes invalid because he obligated himself to four by following.
This is the chosen view from al-Khulasa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن صلى ركعة من الفجر أو المغرب فأقيم يقطع ويقتدي لأنه لو أضاف إليها أخرى لفاتته الجماعة لوجود الفراغ حقيقة في الفجر أو شبهه في المغرب لأن للأكثر حكم الكل. وشمل كلامه ما إذا قام إلى الثانية ولم يقيدها بالسجدة، وقيد بالركعة احترازاً عما إذا قيد الثانية بسجدة فإنه لا يقطعها ويتمها ولا يشرع مع الإمام لكراهة النفل بعد الفجر، وكذا بعد المغرب في ظاهر الرواية. علله في الكافي بأنه إن وافق إمامه خالف السنة بالتنفل بالثلاث وإن وافق السنة فجعلها أربعاً خالف إمامه وكل ذلك بدعة، فإن شرع أتمها أربعاً لأنه أحوط إذ فيه زيادة الركعة وموافقة السنة أحق لأن مخالفة الإمام مشروعة في الجملة كالمسبوق فيما يقضي والمقتدي إذا اقتدى بالمسافر ومخالفة السنة لم تشرع أصلاً. كذا في الكافي. وعلله في الهداية بأن التنفل بالثلاث مكروه، وفي غاية البيان أنه بدعة، وفي شرح الجامع الصغير لقاضيخان أنه حرام والظاهر ما في الهداية. ويراد بالكراهة التحريمية لأن المشايخ يستدلون بأنه عليه السلام نهى عن البتيراء كما في غاية البيان وهو من قبيل ظني الثبوت قطعي الدلالة فيفيد كراهة التحريم على أصولنا. ولو سلم مع الإمام فعن بشر لا يلزمه شيء، وقيل فسدت ويقضي أربعاً لأنه التزم بالاقتداء ثلاثاً فيلزمه أربع كما لو نذر ثلاثاً، وإذا أتمها أربعاً يصلي ركعة ويقعد لأن الأولى من الصلاة ثانية صلاته ولو تركها جازت في الاستحسان لا القياس ولو صلى الإمام أربعاً ساهياً بعد ما قعد على رأس الثلاث وقد اقتدى به الرجل متطوعاً قال ابن الفضل : تفسد صلاة المقتدي لأن الرابعة وجبت على المقتدي بالشروع، وعلى الإمام بالقيام إليها فصار كرجل أوجب على نفسه أربع ركعات بالنذر فاقتدي فيهن بغيره لا تجوز صلاة المقتدي. كذا هذا كذا في فتح القدير . في الخلاصة : المختار فساد صلاة المقتدي قعد الإمام على رأس الثالثة أو لم يقعد ا هـ .
For if he prayed one rak'ah of Fajr or Maghrib and the iqamah is called, he cuts and joins, because if he added another to it, he would miss the congregation due to actual completion in Fajr or its likeness in Maghrib, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. His words include the case when he stood for the second and did not tie it to the prostration, and he restricted it to [one] rak'ah as a precaution for when he tied the second to a prostration, for then he does not cut it but completes it and does not begin with the Imam due to dislike of supererogatory prayer after Fajr, and likewise after Maghrib in the apparent narration. He explained in al-Kafi that if he matches his Imam, he opposes the Sunnah by performing three rak'ahs supererogatorily, and if he matches the Sunnah and makes it four, he opposes his Imam, and all that is innovation. If he begins, he completes it as four because it is more cautious, as it involves an additional rak'ah and matching the Sunnah is more deserving because opposing the Imam is permissible generally, like the latecomer in what he makes up and the follower when following a traveler, but opposing the Sunnah is not permitted at all. So in al-Kafi. He explained in al-Hidayah that supererogatory prayer with three is disliked, and in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is innovation, and in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir by Qadi Khan that it is forbidden, and the apparent is what is in al-Hidayah. And by dislike, prohibitive dislike is meant because the scholars infer that he (peace be upon him) forbade al-Batira', as in Ghayat al-Bayan, and it is of the type of probable transmission but definite in meaning, so it indicates prohibitive dislike according to our principles. If he saluted with the Imam, according to Bishr nothing is incumbent upon him, and it is said that it is invalid and he prays four because he obligated himself by following to three, so four become incumbent as if he vowed three. If he completes it as four, he prays one rak'ah and sits because the first of the prayer is his second prayer, and if he leaves it, it is permitted by istihsan not qiyas. If the Imam prays four forgetfully after sitting at the end of three, and the man followed him as a volunteer, Ibn al-Fadl said: the follower's prayer is invalid because the fourth became obligatory on the follower by commencement, and on the Imam by standing to it, so it becomes like a man who obligated upon himself four rak'ahs by vow, then followed another in them – the follower's prayer is not valid. This is in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Khulasa: the chosen view is the invalidity of the follower's prayer whether the Imam sat at the end of the third or not.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on what to do when a person has prayed one rak'ah of the Fajr or Maghrib supererogatory prayer (sunnah) and the iqamah for the obligatory congregational prayer is called. The author explains that the person should cut his prayer and join the congregation, because if he were to add another rak'ah, he would miss the congregation. This applies whether he has stood for the second rak'ah or not, as long as he has not performed the prostration of the second rak'ah. If he has performed the prostration of the second rak'ah, he should complete it and not join the Imam, due to the dislike of supererogatory prayer after Fajr and Maghrib.

The discussion then addresses a scenario where a person begins the supererogatory prayer after Maghrib and, upon the iqamah, decides to join the congregation. If he joins, he must adjust his intention and complete four rak'ahs total (the two sunnah plus the two fard with the Imam? Actually, the text discusses a volunteer who follows the Imam after the iqamah). There is a difference of opinion on whether this is permissible. Some say it is makruh, some say bid'ah, some say haram. The preferred view in al-Hidayah is that it is makruh (disliked), and it is clarified that this is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) based on the hadith prohibiting 'al-Batira'' (cutting off the tail). The text also discusses if the person salutes with the Imam, and if the Imam makes a mistake and prays four rak'ahs instead of three (in Maghrib), the follower's prayer becomes invalid because he obligated himself to four by following the Imam who prayed four, even if the Imam did so forgetfully. This is the chosen view from al-Khulasa.

Key Terms
البتيراء (al-batira'): The act of cutting a prayer short by leaving it incomplete; specifically, a supererogatory prayer that is cut before completion.
الكراهة التحريمية (al-karahah al-tahrimiyyah): Prohibitive dislike, a ruling that is close to haram but not as severe; requires repentance but not invalidated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has prayed one rak'ah of the Fajr sunnah and the iqamah is called, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Complete his prayer and then join the congregation.
B) Cut his prayer immediately and join the congregation.
C) Continue his prayer and not join the congregation.
D) Pray another rak'ah to complete his sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Before the second prostration of the Fajr/Maghrib sunnah, cut and join; after it, complete alone – and joining after three rak'ahs is makruh tahrimi.

Leaving the Mosque After the Adhan: The Main Ruling and Its Proofs
Ruling on leaving mosque after adhan with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan and identify the two proofs (hadith and mawquf) that support it.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque after the adhan is makruh tanzihi based on a hadith and the statement of Abu Hurayra treated as marfu'.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that it is disliked to leave the mosque after the adhan until one prays. We will analyze the two proofs cited: a hadith from Ibn Majah and a statement from Abu Hurayra (radiallahu anhu) which the Hanafi school treats with the force of a prophetic statement. Understanding these proofs helps us grasp the precise level of dislike and the reasoning behind the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is leaving the mosque after the adhan has been called, before praying the congregational prayer. The ruling is 'makruh' (disliked). Note that the dislike is not absolute; exceptions exist.
The source text says 'ukriha khurujuhu' indicating dislike.
2
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith from Ibn Majah states that one who hears the adhan in the mosque then leaves without a need, intending to return, is a hypocrite. This indicates strong disapproval but does not necessarily imply prohibition.
The hadith is ahad, so its dalala is zanni.
3
Examine the mawquf proof
The statement of Abu Hurayra (radiallahu anhu) that the man who left after the adhan 'disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' is treated as marfu' because a Companion would not say such a thing based on personal opinion. This reinforces the disapproval.
The Hanafi principle 'al-mawquf ka al-marfu'' applies here.
4
Determine the level of dislike
The author explicitly states that these proofs do not indicate that the dislike is prohibitive (tahrimi). Therefore, the ruling is makruh tanzihi (non-prohibitive dislike) unless there is a valid need.
This distinction is important for understanding the severity of the act.

Source Text

قوله: (وكره خروجه من مسجد أذن فيه حتى يصلي وإن صلى لا إلا في الظهر والعشاء إن شرع في (الإقامة لحديث ابن ماجه من أدرك الأذان في المسجد ثم خرج لم يخرج لحاجة الا يريد الرجوع فهو منافق»(۱) وأحرج الجماعة إلا البخاري عن أبي الشعثاء قال : كنا مع أبي هريرة في المسجد فخرج رجل حين أذن المؤذن للعصر قال أبو هريرة: أما هذا فقد عصى أبا القاسم . والموقوف في مثله كالمرفوع، وهذا لا يدل على أن الكراهة تحريمية وهي المحمل عند إطلاقها كما قدمناه واستثنى المشايخ منها ما إذا كان ينتظم به أمر جماعة أخرى بأن كان مؤذناً أو إماماً في مسجد تتفرق الجماعة بغيبته فإنه يخرج بعد النداء لأنه ترك صورة تكميل معنى والعبرة أن الظاهر من الخروج من غير صلاة . الصلاة مع الجماعة، وسواء خرج أو كان ماكثاً في المسجد من غير صلاة كما نشاهده في زماننا من بعض الفسقة حتى لو كانت الجماعة يؤخرون لدخول الوقت المستحب كالصبح مثلاً فخرج إنسان من المسجد بعد دخول الوقت ثم رجع وصلى مع الجماعة ينبغي أن لا يكون مكروهاً، ولم أره كله منقولاً. وقوله «وإن صلى «لا أي وإن صلى الفرض وحده لا يكره خروجه قبل أن يصلي مع الجماعة لأنه قد أجاب داعي الله مرة فلا يجب عليه ثانياً. والظاهر أن مرادهم عدم كراهة الخروج لا عدمها مطلقاً لأن من صلى وحده فقد ارتكب المكروه وهو ترك الجماعة لأنها على الصحيح إما سنة مؤكدة أو واجبة ولم أر من نبه عليه واستثنى المصنف الظهر والعشاء عند الشروع في الإقامة فإنه يكره لمن صلى وحده أن يخرج قبل الصلاة الجماعة لأنه بمخالفة الجماعة عياناً والنفل بعد هاتين الصلاتين ليس بمكروه، وأما في الفجر والعصر فلا يكره له الخروج لكراهة التنفل بعدهما، وأما في المغرب فلما فيه من التنفل بالثلاث أو مخالفة الإمام إن أتمها أربعاً وكل منهما مكروه كما سبق. ولم يذكر المصنف حكم المكث في المسجد بلا صلاة، أما في موضع لا يكره التنفل فالكراهة ظاهرة، وأما في موضع يكره التنفل فذكر في المحيط أنه يتهم من الإضافة تأمل قوله : (كما أن الظاهر من الخروج (الخ) حمل في النهر الخروج على حقيقته وجعل المكث مفهوماً بالدلالة فقال : وإذا كان الخروج إعراضاً كان عدم الصلاة مع المكث حين الإقامة بالإعراض أولى، ثم اعترض على المؤلف بأن ما ذكره مما لا حاجة إليه وأن هذا المجاز لا قرينة عليه قوله : (لأن من صلى وحده فقد ارتكب المكروه) أي ومن ارتكب مكروهاً تحريماً تجب عليه إعادة الصلاة أو مكروهاً تنزيهاً تستحب كما سنذكره في الباب الآتي والراجح في المذهب وجوب صلاة الجماعة ومقتضاه أنه تجب إعادة من صلاها منفرداً بالجماعة أو تسن ليوافق القاعدة المذكورة لكن قول المصنف فيما مر ولو صلى ثلاثاً يتم ويقتدي متطوعاً ينافي ذلك فالأولى تأويل القاعدة بأن يراد بالواجب والسنة تعاد الصلاة بتركه ما كان من أجزاء الصلاة وماهيتها والجماعة وصف لها خارج عنها فلا تعاد الصلاة لتركه فليتأمل قوله : (إما) في موضع لا يكره التنفل) المراد بالموضع الوقت لا
His statement: (And it is disliked for him to leave the mosque in which the adhan was called until he prays, even if he prays [alone] - except in Dhuhr and Isha if the iqamah has started) due to the hadith of Ibn Majah: 'Whoever hears the adhan in the mosque then leaves without a need intending to return, is a hypocrite.' And the group narrated except al-Bukhari from Abu al-Sha'tha' who said: We were with Abu Hurayra in the mosque when a man left after the adhan for Asr. Abu Hurayra said: This one has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim. And the mawquf in such cases is like marfu'. This does not indicate that the dislike is prohibitive, and it is the interpretation when unrestricted as we have stated. The scholars excepted from this the case where an organized congregation would be maintained by his presence, such as if he is the mu'adhdhin or the imam in a mosque whose congregation would disperse without him; then he may leave after the call because he is leaving a form for the sake of the meaning, and consideration is given to the meaning. In al-Nihaya it adds: or if he leaves to pray in the mosque of his neighborhood with the congregation, then there is no harm absolutely, without restriction to imam or mu'adhdhin. It is not hidden that there is [problem] in this, because his leaving is prohibitively disliked and praying in his neighborhood mosque is recommended, so the disliked is not committed for the sake of the recommended, and there is no evidence to restrict it to what he mentioned. The author [al-Kanz] gave it unrestricted, so it includes the case where he was inside when the adhan was called or entered after the adhan. The apparent meaning of their saying 'in which the adhan was called' is that the time entered while he was inside, whether the adhan was in it or elsewhere, just as the apparent meaning of 'leaving without prayer' is not praying with the congregation. And whether he leaves or remains in the mosque without praying as we see in our time from some sinners. Even if the congregation delays [prayer] for the preferred time like Fajr, and a person leaves after the time enters then returns and prays with the congregation, it should not be disliked. I have not seen all this transmitted. And his statement 'even if he prays' means: if he prays the obligatory alone, his leaving before praying with the congregation is not disliked because he has answered the call of Allah once, so it is not required a second time. The apparent meaning is that they mean there is no dislike of leaving, not that there is no dislike at all, because the one who prays alone has committed a disliked act, which is leaving the congregation, because the correct view is that it is either a stressed sunnah or obligatory. And I have not seen anyone draw attention to this. The author excepted Dhuhr and Isha when the iqamah has started, for it is disliked for one who prayed alone to leave before the congregational prayer because it involves open opposition to the congregation, and supererogatory after these two prayers is not disliked. As for Fajr and Asr, it is not disliked for him to leave due to the dislike of supererogatory after them. As for Maghrib, due to the supererogatory of three or opposing the Imam if he completes it as four, both of which are disliked as above. The author did not mention the ruling of staying in the mosque without prayer. In a time when supererogatory is not disliked, the dislike is apparent; when supererogatory is disliked, it is mentioned in al-Muhit that he is accused of... Consider his statement: (Just as it is apparent that leaving...) In al-Nahr, 'leaving' is interpreted literally, and staying is understood by implication. He said: If leaving is turning away, then not praying while staying when the iqamah is given is even more a turning away. Then he objected to the author that what he mentioned is unnecessary and that this metaphor has no indication. His statement: (Because whoever prays alone has committed a disliked act) meaning: whoever commits a prohibitively disliked act must repeat the prayer, or if it is non-prohibitively disliked, it is recommended to repeat, as we will mention in the coming chapter. The preponderant view in the madhhab is the obligation of the congregational prayer, and its implication is that repeating [the prayer] with the congregation is obligatory or recommended to match the mentioned principle. But the author's statement earlier 'if he prayed three, he completes and follows as a volunteer' contradicts that. So it is better to interpret the principle to mean that obligatory and sunnah repeat the prayer upon its omission pertains to parts of the prayer and its essence, whereas congregation is an attribute external to it, so the prayer is not repeated for its omission. So ponder. His statement: (Either) in a time when supererogatory is not disliked) means by 'time' the prayer time, not...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of leaving the mosque after the adhan has been called. Citing a hadith from Ibn Majah and a statement from Abu Hurayra, the text establishes that it is disliked (makruh) to leave the mosque after the adhan without a valid intention to return. The scholars clarify that this is not necessarily prohibitive dislike (tahrimi), but rather tanzihi (non-prohibitive), unless there is evidence to the contrary.

Exceptions are made for the mu'adhdhin or imam of a mosque whose absence would disrupt the congregation, allowing them to leave after the adhan to preserve the congregation. An additional exception from al-Nihaya allows leaving to pray in another mosque with the congregation. However, the commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) criticizes this, arguing that leaving is prohibitively disliked, and a recommended act does not justify committing a disliked act.

The author of al-Kanz (the matn) mentions an exception for Dhuhr and Isha when the iqamah has started: if someone has already prayed alone, it is not disliked for him to leave before the congregational prayer? Actually, the text says it is disliked for him to leave before the congregation if he prayed alone, because it involves open opposition.

The passage also discusses the case of staying in the mosque without praying, and the difference between times when supererogatory prayer is permissible and when it is not. The discussion ends with a note that the preponderant view in the Hanafi school is that congregational prayer is obligatory (wajib), but this does not require repeating the prayer if one prays alone, because congregation is an attribute separate from the essence of the prayer. This is harmonized with earlier statements that seem to suggest otherwise.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike, a ruling that discourages an act without making it unlawful. The text distinguishes between tanzihi and tahrimi.
الموقوف كالمرفوع (al-mawquf ka al-marfu'): A statement or action of a Companion that is attributed to the Prophet in terms of authority, i.e., it has the legal force of a marfu' hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the proof from Abu Hurayra is classified as:
A) Marfu' hadith
B) Mawquf hadith treated as marfu'
C) Da'if hadith
D) Qudsi hadith

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after the adhan is makruh tanzihi based on a hadith and a Companion's statement; it is not haram.

intermediate

Exceptions to the Dislike: The Mu'adhdhin, Imam, and the Dispute with al-Nihaya
Exceptions to the ruling on leaving after adhan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the exceptions to the dislike of leaving after the adhan and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding leaving to pray in another mosque.

Core Idea
The mu'adhdhin and imam may leave if their absence would disrupt the congregation; but the claim that leaving for any other congregation is permissible is disputed.

In this lesson, we explore the exceptions to the general rule. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a concession for the mu'adhdhin and imam whose departure is needed to maintain another congregation. It then cites al-Nihaya's broader exception allowing anyone to leave to pray in their neighborhood mosque, which the author strongly criticizes. Understanding this intra-madhhab ikhtilaf is important for issuing correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first exception (mu'adhdhin/imam)
The scholars excepted the case where the mu'adhdhin or imam of a mosque must leave to preserve the congregation of another mosque. Here the dislike is lifted because the purpose (congregation) is considered more important than the form (staying in the mosque).
The principle: 'al-ibrah lil-ma'na la li al-surah' (consideration is for meaning, not form).
2
Understand the reasoning
The exception is based on necessity: if the mu'adhdhin/imam did not leave, the other congregation would disperse. The harm of losing the congregation outweighs the dislike of leaving.
This is a form of istihsan.
3
Identify the broader exception from al-Nihaya
Al-Nihaya adds that anyone may leave to pray in the mosque of his neighborhood with the congregation, without restriction to imam or mu'adhdhin. This includes people who are not responsible for a congregation.
This is a more permissive position.
4
Analyze the author's critique
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq objects strongly, arguing that leaving is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) according to some, and a recommended act (praying in neighborhood mosque) does not justify committing a disliked act. He finds no evidence for such a generalization.
The author maintains the original dislike unless there is a genuine need like preserving another congregation.

إلا البخاري عن أبي الشعثاء قال : كنا مع أبي هريرة في المسجد فخرج رجل حين أذن المؤذن للعصر قال أبو هريرة: أما هذا فقد عصى أبا القاسم . والموقوف في مثله كالمرفوع، وهذا لا يدل على أن الكراهة تحريمية وهي الله مرة فلا يجب عليه ثانياً. والظاهر أن مرادهم عدم كراهة الخروج لا عدمها مطلقاً لأن من صلى وحده فقد ارتكب المكروه وهو ترك الجماعة لأنها على الصحيح إما سنة مؤكدة أو واجبة ولم أر من نبه عليه واستثنى المصنف الظهر والعشاء عند الشروع في الإقامة فإنه يكره لمن صلى وحده أن يخرج قبل الصلاة الجماعة لأنه بمخالفة الجماعة عياناً والنفل بعد هاتين الصلاتين ليس بمكروه، وأما في الفجر والعصر فلا يكره له الخروج إعراضاً كان عدم الصلاة مع المكث حين الإقامة بالإعراض أولى، ثم اعترض على المؤلف بأن ما ذكره مما لا حاجة إليه وأن هذا المجاز لا قرينة عليه قوله : (لأن من صلى وحده فقد ارتكب المكروه) أي ومن ارتكب مكروهاً تحريماً تجب عليه إعادة الصلاة أو مكروهاً تنزيهاً تستحب كما سنذكره في الباب الآتي والراجح في المذهب وجوب صلاة الجماعة ومقتضاه أنه تجب إعادة من صلاها منفرداً بالجماعة أو تسن ليوافق القاعدة المذكورة لكن قول المصنف فيما مر ولو صلى ثلاثاً يتم ويقتدي متطوعاً ينافي ذلك فالأولى تأويل القاعدة بأن يراد بالواجب والسنة تعاد الصلاة بتركه ما كان من أجزاء الصلاة وماهيتها والجماعة وصف لها خارج عنها فلا تعاد الصلاة لتركه فليتأمل قوله : (إما) في موضع لا يكره التنفل) المراد بالموضع الوقت لا
His statement: (And it is disliked for him to leave the mosque in which the adhan was called until he prays, even if he prays [alone] - except in Dhuhr and Isha if the iqamah has started) due to the hadith of Ibn Majah: 'Whoever hears the adhan in the mosque then leaves without a need intending to return, is a hypocrite.' And the group narrated except al-Bukhari from Abu al-Sha'tha' who said: We were with Abu Hurayra in the mosque when a man left after the adhan for Asr. Abu Hurayra said: This one has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim. And the mawquf in such cases is like marfu'. This does not indicate that the dislike is prohibitive, and it is the interpretation when unrestricted as we have stated. The scholars excepted from this the case where an organized congregation would be maintained by his presence, such as if he is the mu'adhdhin or the imam in a mosque whose congregation would disperse without him; then he may leave after the call because he is leaving a form for the sake of the meaning, and consideration is given to the meaning. In al-Nihaya it adds: or if he leaves to pray in the mosque of his neighborhood with the congregation, then there is no harm absolutely, without restriction to imam or mu'adhdhin. It is not hidden that there is [problem] in this, because his leaving is prohibitively disliked and praying in his neighborhood mosque is recommended, so the disliked is not committed for the sake of the recommended, and there is no evidence to restrict it to what he mentioned. The author [al-Kanz] gave it unrestricted, so it includes the case where he was inside when the adhan was called or entered after the adhan. The apparent meaning of their saying 'in which the adhan was called' is that the time entered while he was inside, whether the adhan was in it or elsewhere, just as the apparent meaning of 'leaving without prayer' is not praying with the congregation. And whether he leaves or remains in the mosque without praying as we see in our time from some sinners. Even if the congregation delays [prayer] for the preferred time like Fajr, and a person leaves after the time enters then returns and prays with the congregation, it should not be disliked. I have not seen all this transmitted. And his statement 'even if he prays' means: if he prays the obligatory alone, his leaving before praying with the congregation is not disliked because he has answered the call of Allah once, so it is not required a second time. The apparent meaning is that they mean there is no dislike of leaving, not that there is no dislike at all, because the one who prays alone has committed a disliked act, which is leaving the congregation, because the correct view is that it is either a stressed sunnah or obligatory. And I have not seen anyone draw attention to this. The author excepted Dhuhr and Isha when the iqamah has started, for it is disliked for one who prayed alone to leave before the congregational prayer because it involves open opposition to the congregation, and supererogatory after these two prayers is not disliked. As for Fajr and Asr, it is not disliked for him to leave due to the dislike of supererogatory after them. As for Maghrib, due to the supererogatory of three or opposing the Imam if he completes it as four, both of which are disliked as above. The author did not mention the ruling of staying in the mosque without prayer. In a time when supererogatory is not disliked, the dislike is apparent; when supererogatory is disliked, it is mentioned in al-Muhit that he is accused of... Consider his statement: (Just as it is apparent that leaving...) In al-Nahr, 'leaving' is interpreted literally, and staying is understood by implication. He said: If leaving is turning away, then not praying while staying when the iqamah is given is even more a turning away. Then he objected to the author that what he mentioned is unnecessary and that this metaphor has no indication. His statement: (Because whoever prays alone has committed a disliked act) meaning: whoever commits a prohibitively disliked act must repeat the prayer, or if it is non-prohibitively disliked, it is recommended to repeat, as we will mention in the coming chapter. The preponderant view in the madhhab is the obligation of the congregational prayer, and its implication is that repeating [the prayer] with the congregation is obligatory or recommended to match the mentioned principle. But the author's statement earlier 'if he prayed three, he completes and follows as a volunteer' contradicts that. So it is better to interpret the principle to mean that obligatory and sunnah repeat the prayer upon its omission pertains to parts of the prayer and its essence, whereas congregation is an attribute external to it, so the prayer is not repeated for its omission. So ponder. His statement: (Either) in a time when supererogatory is not disliked) means by 'time' the prayer time, not...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of leaving the mosque after the adhan has been called. Citing a hadith from Ibn Majah and a statement from Abu Hurayra, the text establishes that it is disliked (makruh) to leave the mosque after the adhan without a valid intention to return. The scholars clarify that this is not necessarily prohibitive dislike (tahrimi), but rather tanzihi (non-prohibitive), unless there is evidence to the contrary.

Exceptions are made for the mu'adhdhin or imam of a mosque whose absence would disrupt the congregation, allowing them to leave after the adhan to preserve the congregation. An additional exception from al-Nihaya allows leaving to pray in another mosque with the congregation. However, the commentator (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) criticizes this, arguing that leaving is prohibitively disliked, and a recommended act does not justify committing a disliked act.

The author of al-Kanz (the matn) mentions an exception for Dhuhr and Isha when the iqamah has started: if someone has already prayed alone, it is not disliked for him to leave before the congregational prayer? Actually, the text says it is disliked for him to leave before the congregation if he prayed alone, because it involves open opposition.

The passage also discusses the case of staying in the mosque without praying, and the difference between times when supererogatory prayer is permissible and when it is not. The discussion ends with a note that the preponderant view in the Hanafi school is that congregational prayer is obligatory (wajib), but this does not require repeating the prayer if one prays alone, because congregation is an attribute separate from the essence of the prayer. This is harmonized with earlier statements that seem to suggest otherwise.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike, a ruling that discourages an act without making it unlawful. The text distinguishes between tanzihi and tahrimi.
العبرة للمعنى لا للصورة (al-ibrah lil-ma'na la li al-surah): Consideration is given to the meaning and purpose, not the outward form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, who may leave the mosque after the adhan without dislike?
A) Anyone who intends to pray in another mosque
B) Only the mu'adhdhin or imam whose absence would disrupt another congregation
C) Only the person who has already prayed alone
D) No one

Key Takeaway
Only the mu'adhdhin or imam may leave after the adhan to preserve another congregation; other exceptions are disputed and not mufta bihi.

Leaving After Praying Alone and Staying Without Prayer
Further details on leaving after adhan and staying without prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on leaving the mosque after praying alone and the ruling on staying in the mosque without praying after the adhan.

Core Idea
If one prays alone, leaving before the congregation is not disliked, except in Dhuhr and Isha when the iqamah has started; staying without prayer is also disliked when supererogatory is permissible.

In this lesson, we examine additional scenarios discussed in the passage: what if someone prays the obligatory prayer alone and then leaves? And what about staying in the mosque without praying at all? The text provides nuanced rulings based on the time and the availability of supererogatory prayer. These rulings complete the picture of the legal framework surrounding the adhan and congregation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the ruling for one who prays alone
If a person prays the obligatory prayer alone in the mosque, it is not disliked for him to leave before the congregational prayer because he has already responded to the call of Allah once.
This is based on the idea that the obligation of answering the adhan is fulfilled by prayer alone.
2
Identify the exception for Dhuhr and Isha
However, if the iqamah has started for Dhuhr or Isha, it is disliked for him to leave even if he prayed alone, because leaving at that point constitutes open opposition to the congregation, and supererogatory prayer after these two prayers is not disliked.
For Fajr and Asr, supererogatory prayer is disliked after the obligatory, so leaving is not disliked.
3
Analyze the ruling on staying without prayer
The text also discusses staying in the mosque without praying. At times when supererogatory prayer is not disliked (e.g., after Dhuhr and Isha), staying without prayer is disliked because it shows disregard. At times when supererogatory is disliked (e.g., after Fajr and Asr), staying might be less problematic, but the text notes that such a person is 'accused' of impropriety.
This distinction is subtle and based on the time of prayer.

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of leaving the mosque after the adhan has been called. الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer recited just before the obligatory prayer begins, signaling that the prayer is about to start.
