Leaving the Mosque After the Adhan: Ruling and Exceptions
Explains ruling on leaving mosque after adhan with exceptions and critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan, identify the exceptions for the imam and mu'adhdhin, and explain why the addition from al-Nihayah is considered problematic.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque after the adhan is makruh tahriman — a disliked act close to prohibition — unless one's presence is needed for another congregation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan. While the general rule is clear — it is makruh tahriman — the commentators carved out specific exceptions. The text also presents a more permissive view from al-Nihayah and subjects it to critical scrutiny, revealing key Hanafi principles about priority of obligations over recommendations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and its legal category
Locate the statement in the passage that leaving after the adhan is disliked. Note the term 'makrūh tahrīman' and understand that in Hanafi fiqh this means it is close to prohibition.
The ruling applies to a person who hears the adhan while inside the mosque and then leaves without praying.
2
Examine the first exception: imam or mu'adhdhin
Read the exception mentioned by the mashāyikh: it is permissible to leave if one is an imam or mu'adhdhin whose absence would cause another congregation to disperse. Understand the reasoning: form vs. meaning, and consideration of the greater good.
This exception is based on necessity for preserving congregational prayer.
3
Critique the second exception from al-Nihayah
Analyze the addition from al-Nihayah that permits leaving to pray in one's neighborhood mosque unconditionally. Then read the author's criticism: a makruh tahriman cannot be committed for a mandub act. Identify the legal principle at work.
This shows the Hanafi commitment to upholding the hierarchy of rulings: avoid what is close to prohibition even if it means missing a recommended act.
4
Clarify scope: 'adhan' and 'leaving'
Understand that 'adhan' here means the entry of prayer time, not necessarily the specific call. And 'leaving' means abandoning the congregational prayer, whether physically exiting or remaining in the mosque without praying. Consider the author's own observation about delaying congregations.
This clarification prevents misunderstanding: the ruling applies to avoiding the jama'ah, not just walking out.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب إدراك الفريضة عدم عند إطلاقها كما قدمناه واستثنى المشايخ منها ما إذا كان ينتظم به أمر جماعة أخرى بأن كان مؤذناً أو إماماً في مسجد تتفرق الجماعة بغيبته فإنه يخرج بعد النداء لأنه ترك صورة تكميل معنى والعبرة للمعنى. زاد في النهاية أو يكون خرج ليصلي في مسجد حيه مع الجماعة فلا بأس به مطلقاً من غير قيد بالإمام والمؤذن ا هـ . ولا يخفى ما فيه إذ خروجه مكروه تحريماً والصلاة في مسجد حيه مندوبة فلا يرتكب المكروه لأجل المندوب ولا دليل يدل على تقييدها بما ذكره وأطلقه المصنف فشمل ما أذن فيه وهو داخله أو دخل بعد الأذان، والظاهر أن مرادهم من الأذان فيه هو دخول الوقت وهو داخله، سواء أذن فيه أو في غيره كما أن الظاهر من الخروج من غير صلاة . الصلاة مع الجماعة، وسواء خرج أو كان ماكثاً في المسجد من غير صلاة كما نشاهده في زماننا من بعض الفسقة حتى لو كانت الجماعة يؤخرون لدخول الوقت المستحب كالصبح مثلاً فخرج إنسان من المسجد بعد دخول الوقت ثم رجع وصلى مع الجماعة ينبغي أن لا يكون مكروهاً، ولم أره كله منقولاً.
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer. [The ruling] of dislike [for leaving after the adhan] in its unrestricted form, as we have mentioned. The mashāyikh excepted from it the case where the person's [departure] is necessary for another congregation, such as if he is a mu'adhdhin or an imam in a mosque whose congregation would disperse in his absence; then he may leave after the adhan because he is abandoning the form for the sake of completing the meaning, and consideration is for the meaning. In al-Nihāyah it is added: Or if he leaves to pray in the mosque of his neighborhood with the congregation, then there is no harm absolutely, without the restriction of being an imam or mu'adhdhin – end. But it is not hidden what is in it, for his leaving is makrūh tahrīman, and praying in his neighborhood mosque is mandūb, so the makrūh is not committed for the sake of the mandūb. And there is no evidence to restrict it to what he mentioned; the author (al-Kanz) stated it absolutely, so it includes what is permitted: that he is inside [the mosque] or entered after the adhan. And the apparent [meaning of their words] is that 'the adhan in it' means the entry of time while he is inside, whether the adhan is called inside or elsewhere. Also, the apparent [meaning of] 'leaving' is [leaving] without prayer, [i.e.,] leaving the congregational prayer. And it is the same whether he leaves or remains in the mosque without prayer, as we observe in our time from some wicked people. Even if the congregation delays for the entry of the preferred time, like Fajr for example, and a man leaves the mosque after the entry of time and then returns and prays with the congregation, it should not be disliked. I have not seen all of this transmitted.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq discusses the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan. The base ruling is that it is disliked (makrūh tahrīman) to leave after the adhan without praying, unless one intends to join another congregation that depends on him. The mashāyikh (later Hanafi scholars) excepted two cases: (1) if the person is an imam or mu'adhdhin whose absence would cause the congregation to disperse; (2) if he leaves to pray in his neighborhood mosque (adding from al-Nihāyah). The commentary then critiques the addition from al-Nihāyah, arguing that a disliked action cannot be justified by a recommended one. It clarifies that 'leaving' here means leaving without praying, and stresses that remaining idly in the mosque without praying is also problematic. The author adds a modern observation: if someone leaves and returns when the congregation delays, it should not be disliked.

Key Terms
النداء (al-nidā'): The adhan, the call to prayer.
مكروه تحريماً (makrūh tahrīman): A disliked action that is close to prohibition; the Hanafi school treats it as a distinct category between makrūh tanzīhan and harām.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan without praying, if one is not an imam or mu'adhdhin?
A) Permissible (mubāḥ)
B) Recommended (mandūb)
C) Disliked near prohibition (makrūh tahrīman)
D) Forbidden (ḥarām)

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after the adhan is makruh tahriman; only necessary duties for another congregation justify it, not simple convenience or preference.

Leaving After Praying Alone: When It's Disliked and When It's Not
Clarifies that one who prays alone may leave before congregation, with exceptions for Dhuhr, 'Isha, and staying idle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on leaving the mosque after praying alone and identify the specific prayer times when leaving is disliked.

Core Idea
Praying alone is disliked; leaving after that is not disliked except at Dhuhr and 'Isha when iqāmah is called.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the rules for a person who has already performed their obligatory prayer alone. It addresses whether such a person may leave the mosque before the congregation begins, and examines the exceptions for different prayer times. Understanding these nuances helps you navigate fiqh rulings on congregational prayer and their application in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
Identify that the act of leaving after praying alone is not disliked. The commentator notes this is 'la yukrah' (not disliked).
This is the default position.
2
Understand the rationale
The reason given is that the person has already responded to the call of Allah once, so he is not obligated a second time. This justifies the absence of dislike.
This is a legal cause (sabab) based on the principle of sufficiency.
3
Identify the exceptions for Dhuhr and 'Isha
The author explicitly states that for Dhuhr and 'Isha, when the iqāmah has started, it is disliked to leave because it constitutes open defiance of the congregation.
These are the only two prayers with this heightened dislike.
4
Distinguish the rulings for other prayers
For Fajr and 'Asr, leaving is not disliked because voluntary prayer after them is disliked anyway. For Maghrib, leaving is also not clearly disliked due to inherent ambiguity in performing supererogatory prayer.
This shows the connection between the dislike of leaving and the dislike of voluntary prayer.
5
Apply the ruling on idle staying
The passage concludes with a ruling from al-Muhit: staying in the mosque without praying is disliked in times when voluntary prayer is disliked (after 'Asr, Maghrib, Fajr). This is because it resembles opposing the congregation.
This is an extension of the same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله «وإن صلى «لا أي وإن صلى الفرض وحده لا يكره خروجه قبل أن يصلي مع الجماعة لأنه قد أجاب داعي الله مرة فلا يجب عليه ثانياً. والظاهر أن مرادهم عدم كراهة الخروج لا عدمها مطلقاً لأن من صلى وحده فقد ارتكب المكروه وهو ترك الجماعة لأنها على الصحيح إما سنة مؤكدة أو واجبة ولم أر من نبه عليه واستثنى المصنف الظهر والعشاء عند الشروع في الإقامة فإنه يكره لمن صلى وحده أن يخرج قبل الصلاة الجماعة لأنه بمخالفة الجماعة عياناً والنفل بعد هاتين الصلاتين ليس بمكروه، وأما في الفجر والعصر فلا يكره له الخروج لكراهة التنفل بعدهما، وأما في المغرب فلما فيه من التنفل بالثلاث أو مخالفة الإمام إن أتمها أربعاً وكل منهما مكروه كما سبق. ولم يذكر المصنف حكم المكث في المسجد بلا صلاة، أما في موضع لا يكره التنفل فالكراهة ظاهرة، وأما في موضع يكره التنفل فذكر في المحيط أنه في العصر والمغرب والفجر يخرج لكراهة التطوع بعدها وإن مكث وإن لم يدخل معهم يكره لأن مخالفة الجماعة وزر عظيم ا هـ
And his statement 'And if he prays...' i.e., if he prays the obligatory prayer alone, his leaving before he prays with the congregation is not disliked, because he has responded to the call of Allah once, so it is not obligatory upon him a second time. But the apparent [meaning] is that they mean the absence of dislike for leaving, not absolute absence [of dislike], because one who prays alone has already committed a disliked act, i.e., abandoning the congregation, for it is, according to the correct view, either a stressed sunnah or obligatory. And I have not seen anyone who alerted to this. The author excepted Dhuhr and 'Isha at the start of the iqāmah: it is disliked for one who prayed alone to leave before the congregational prayer, because it is open defiance of the congregation, and the supererogatory prayer after these two prayers is not disliked. As for Fajr and 'Asr, it is not disliked for him to leave, due to the dislike of supererogatory prayer after them. As for Maghrib, because there is [the problem of] praying three as supererogatory or opposing the imam if he completes four, and each is disliked, as has preceded. The author did not mention the ruling on staying in the mosque without prayer. In a time when supererogatory prayer is not disliked, the dislike [of staying] is apparent. But in a time when supererogatory prayer is disliked, it is mentioned in al-Muhīt that in 'Asr, Maghrib, and Fajr, he should leave because of the dislike of voluntary prayer after them; if he stays and does not enter with them, it is disliked because opposing the congregation is a great burden – end.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on leaving the mosque. It first addresses the case of a person who has already prayed his obligatory prayer alone. The author states that it is not disliked for him to leave before joining the congregation for a second prayer, because he has already fulfilled the obligation once. However, the commentator (Ibn 'Abidin/author of al-Bahr) notes that this does not mean there is no dislike at all, because praying alone itself is disliked (either makrūh tanzīhan or tahrīman, since congregation is stressed). Then exceptions are mentioned: for Dhuhr and 'Isha, if the iqāmah has started, it is disliked to leave because it is open defiance. For Fajr and 'Asr, it is not disliked to leave because voluntary prayer after them is disliked anyway. For Maghrib, leaving is also not preferred because of confusion. Then the passage discusses the ruling on staying idly in the mosque without praying, citing al-Muhīt: during times when voluntary prayer is disliked (like after 'Asr, Maghrib, Fajr), one should leave; if he stays and does not join the congregation, it is disliked.

Key Terms
المكروه (al-makrūh): A disliked act; in this context, it ranges from tanzīhan (lightly disliked) to tahrīman (near prohibition) depending on the situation.
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): The second call to prayer signaling the immediate start of the congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
At which two prayer times is it disliked for a person who prayed alone to leave before the congregation, if the iqāmah has started?
A) Fajr and 'Asr
B) Dhuhr and 'Isha
C) Maghrib and 'Isha
D) Fajr and Maghrib

Key Takeaway
Leaving after praying alone is generally not disliked, but it becomes disliked at the start of iqāmah for Dhuhr and 'Isha, and staying idle during times when voluntary prayer is prohibited is also disliked.

Prioritizing Congregation over Sunnah of Fajr: Intra-Hanafi Analysis
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sunnah of Fajr vs congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi priority rule when sunnah of Fajr conflicts with congregation and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Congregation takes priority over sunnah of Fajr when feared to be missed.

This lesson examines a common scenario: a Muslim arrives at the mosque for Fajr but has not yet prayed the sunnah. Should he pray the sunnah first or join the congregation immediately? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on this, with the majority ruling that congregation takes precedence. We will analyze the proofs and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the conflict
Understand the situation: a person fears missing the Fajr congregation and has not yet performed the sunnah. The two acts conflict.
2
State the Hanafi default position
According to the apparent madhhab (zahir al-riwayah), congregation is prioritized because it carries promise and threat, while the sunnah has only promise.
The proof includes hadith on the virtue of congregation and the threat for abandoning it.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that if one can catch the tashahhud, he may perform the sunnah first, by analogy to catching a rak'ah in Jumu'ah.
Muhammad al-Shaybani (Imam Muhammad) appears to differ, though the text is ambiguous.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is to join the congregation immediately, following the majority of the Hanafi school, as supported by al-Khulāṣah, al-Jāmi' al-Saghīr, and al-Badā'i'.
The author of al-Bahr al-Rā'iq endorses the apparent madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن خاف فوت الفجر أن أدى سنته أيتم وتركها وإلا لا لأن الأصل إن سنة الفجر لها فضيلة عظيمة قال عليه الصلاة والسلام ركعتا الفجر خير من الدنيا وما فيها»(۱) وكذا ما قدمناه ، وكذا للجماعة بالأحاديث المتقدمة، فإذا تعارضا عمل بها بقدر الإمكان وإن لم يمكن بأن خشي فوت الركعتين أحرز أحقهما وهو الجماعة لورود الوعد والوعيد في الجماعات، والسنة وإن ورد الوعد فيها لم يرد الوعيد بتركها، ولأن ثواب الجماعة أعظم لأنها مكملة ذاتية والسنة مكملة خارجية والذاتية أقوى. وشمل كلامه ما إذا كان يرجوا إدراكه في التشهد فإنه يأتي بالسنة، وظاهر ما في الجامع الصغير حيث قال : إن خاف أن تفوته الركعتان دخل مع الإمام أن لا يأتي بالسنة وفي الخلاصة ظاهر المذهب أنه يدخل مع الإمام، ورجحه في البدائع بأن للأكثر حكم الكل فكأن الكل قد فاته فيقدم الجماعة. ونقل في الكافي والمحيط أنه يأتي بها عندهما خلافاً لمحمد لأن إدراك القعدة عندهما كإدراك ركعة في الجمعة خلافاً له، له، وقد جعل المصنف لسنة الفجر حكمين أما الفعل إن لم يخف فوت الجماعة وهو المراد بفوت الفجر بقرينة قوله أيتم وأما الترك إن خاف فوت الجماعة فاندفع ما ذكره الفقيه معهم
His statement: 'And whoever fears missing Fajr, if he performs his sunnah, he completes it and then joins [the congregation], otherwise not.' Because the origin is that the sunnah of Fajr has great virtue. He (peace be upon him) said: 'The two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and what is in it.' Likewise, what we have mentioned. And likewise for the congregation, due to the hadiths that have preceded. So if they conflict, one acts on them as much as possible. If not possible, i.e., he fears missing both rak'ahs, he secures the greater right, which is the congregation, because promise and threat have come regarding congregations. And the sunnah, even though promise has come regarding it, no threat has come for abandoning it. And because the reward of congregation is greater, for it is an intrinsic completion, while the sunnah is an external completion, and the intrinsic is stronger. His speech includes the case where he hopes to catch [the imam] in the tashahhud; then he performs the sunnah. The apparent [teaching] in al-Jāmi' al-Saghīr – where he said: if he fears missing both rak'ahs, he enters with the imam and does not perform the sunnah – [supports that]. And in al-Khulāṣah, the apparent madhhab is that he enters with the imam. And in al-Badā'i' it is preferred [as such] because the majority takes the ruling of the whole, so as if the whole has passed, so he gives precedence to the congregation. And it is narrated in al-Kāfī and al-Muhīt that he performs the sunnah according to them (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad?) contrary to Muhammad? Actually: 'according to the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad' – the text is ambiguous. Because catching the sitting (tashahhud) according to them is like catching a rak'ah in Jumu'ah, contrary to him. And the author (al-Kanz) made for the sunnah of Fajr two rulings: action if he does not fear missing the congregation (which is meant by missing Fajr, indicated by his saying 'he completes [the sunnah]'), and abandoning if he fears missing the congregation. Thus what the faqīh mentioned with them is refuted.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Rā'iq addresses the conflict between performing the sunnah of Fajr and joining the congregational Fajr prayer. The base rule: if one fears missing the congregation, he should join immediately; if not, he may perform the sunnah first. The proof: the hadith praising the two rak'ahs of Fajr, and the stronger evidence for congregation (promise and threat). The commentator then details an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to the apparent madhhab (as in al-Khulāṣah and al-Jāmi' al-Saghīr), one should enter with the imam even if it means missing the sunnah. However, in al-Kāfī and al-Muhīt, it is reported that according to Abū Yūsuf and Muhammad (the two companions), one should perform the sunnah if he hopes to catch the tashahhud, because catching the tashahhud is like catching a rak'ah in Jumu'ah. But Muhammad (al-Shaybānī) differs. The author of al-Kanz (the matn) reconciles by stating two rulings: perform the sunnah if no fear of missing congregation; otherwise abandon it. The commentator argues that this resolves the dispute.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of recommended prayer before the obligatory Fajr prayer, highly emphasized.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The sitting position in prayer where one recites the testimony of faith; here, catching the last sitting of the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent madhhab, what should a person do if he fears missing the Fajr congregation while he has not yet prayed the sunnah?
A) Perform the sunnah first, then join the congregation.
B) Join the congregation immediately and skip the sunnah.
C) Pray the sunnah and then join if the congregation is still ongoing.
D) Abandon both and pray alone.

Key Takeaway
When the sunnah of Fajr conflicts with congregation, the Hanafi mufta bihi is to join the congregation immediately.

Fajr Sunnah vs. Congregation: Prioritization and Dispute
Commentary on prioritizing congregation over Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing the Fajr sunnah when fearing missing the congregation and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
When congregation is at risk, skip the sunnah and join the imam.

The Fajr sunnah is a highly recommended prayer, but when it conflicts with the obligation of attending the Fajr congregation, a prioritization is needed. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and the commentary in al-Bahr al-Raiq, including a dispute within the school about whether the sunnah can be performed if only the tashahhud will be missed. By the end, you will understand the preferred view and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the main ruling: if one fears missing the entire Fajr congregation, he should skip the sunnah and join the imam immediately.
The source text emphasizes that congregation takes precedence because of the threat for missing it.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the dispute: Abu Hanifa says to skip the sunnah even if only the tashahhud will be missed; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow performing the sunnah if the tashahhud will be caught.
The Sahibayn consider catching the tashahhud equivalent to catching a rak'ah in Jumu'ah.
3
Examine the proofs
Understand the dalil for each view: congregation is backed by threats of punishment, while the sunnah is only praised. The Sahibayn use qiyas on Jumu'ah.
The hadith 'Rak'ata al-fajr khair min al-dunya wa ma fiha' shows virtue but not obligation.
4
Analyze the tarjih
Learn why Abu Hanifa's view is preferred: the majority is treated as the whole, so missing any part of the congregation is like missing it all. Also, congregation is a self-integral complement, while sunnah is external.
Al-Bada'i and others prefer Abu Hanifa's view as the apparent madhhab.
5
Apply the ruling with conditions
Consider additional conditions: if there is a separate place to pray sunnah without appearing to oppose, some allow it, but the best is to avoid.
The mashayikh differed on whether the entire mosque is one place or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ومن خاف فوت الفجر أن أدى سنته أيتم وتركها وإلا لا لأن الأصل إن سنة الفجر لها فضيلة عظيمة قال عليه الصلاة والسلام ركعتا الفجر خير من الدنيا وما فيها وكذا ما قدمناه ، وكذا للجماعة بالأحاديث المتقدمة، فإذا تعارضا عمل بها بقدر الإمكان وإن لم يمكن بأن خشي فوت الركعتين أحرز أحقهما وهو الجماعة لورود الوعد والوعيد في الجماعات، والسنة وإن ورد الوعد فيها لم يرد الوعيد بتركها، ولأن ثواب الجماعة أعظم لأنها مكملة ذاتية والسنة مكملة خارجية والذاتية أقوى. وشمل كلامه ما إذا كان يرجوا إدراكه في التشهد فإنه يأتي بالسنة، وظاهر ما في الجامع الصغير حيث قال : إن خاف أن تفوته الركعتان دخل مع الإمام أن لا يأتي بالسنة وفي الخلاصة ظاهر المذهب أنه يدخل مع الإمام، ورجحه في البدائع بأن للأكثر حكم الكل فكأن الكل قد فاته فيقدم الجماعة. ونقل في الكافي والمحيط أنه يأتي بها عندهما خلافاً لمحمد لأن إدراك القعدة عندهما كإدراك ركعة في الجمعة خلافاً له، له، وقد جعل المصنف لسنة الفجر حكمين أما الفعل إن لم يخف فوت الجماعة وهو المراد بفوت الفجر بقرينة قوله أيتم وأما الترك إن خاف فوت الجماعة فاندفع ما ذكره الفقيه إسماعيل الزاهد من أنه ينبغي أن يفتتح ركعتي الفجر ثم يقطعهما ويدخل مع الإمام حتى تلزمه بالشروع فيتمكن من القضاء بعد الفجر وهو مردود من وجهين: أحدهما ما ذكره الإمام السرخسي أن ما وجب بالشروع لا يكون أقوى مما وجب بالنذر وقد نص محمد أن المنذورة لا تؤدى بعد الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس. ثانيهما ما ذكره قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير أن المشايخ نكروا عليه ذلك لأن هذا أمر بافتتاح الصلاة على قصد أن يقطع ولا يتم وأنه غير مستحسن. ثم إن هنا قيداً تركه المصنف في قوله «وإلا لا» أن يجد مكاناً المسجد يصلي السنة فيه، فإن لم يجد فينبغي أن لا يصلي السنة لأن ترك المكروه مقدم على فعل السنة. كذا في فتح القدير وهو متفرع على أحد القولين لما في المحيط : ولو صلاهما في المسجد الخارج والإمام يصلي في المسجد الداخل قيل لا يكره لأنه لا يتصور بصورة المخالفة لاختلاف المكان حقيقة ، وقيل يكره لأن ذلك كله كمكان واحد فإذا اختلف المشايخ فيه كان الأفضل أن لا يفعل اهـ.
His saying: (And whoever fears missing Fajr, if he performs his sunnah, he completes it and leaves it, otherwise not) because the sunnah of Fajr has great virtue. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and what is in it.' And similarly what we have presented. And similarly for the congregation due to the previous hadiths. So when they conflict, one acts on both as much as possible. If not possible, as when he fears losing both rak'ahs, he secures the more deserving of the two, which is the congregation, because promise and threat are mentioned regarding congregations. As for the sunnah, although promise is mentioned regarding it, no threat is mentioned for leaving it. And because the reward of congregation is greater, for it is a self-integral complement, while the sunnah is an external complement, and the self-integral is stronger. His statement includes the case where he hopes to catch only the tashahhud: he performs the sunnah. The apparent position in al-Jami' al-Saghir is that if he fears losing both rak'ahs, he enters with the imam and does not perform the sunnah. In al-Khulasa, the apparent madhhab is that he enters with the imam. It is preferred in al-Bada'i that the majority has the ruling of the whole, so it is as if the whole has been missed, so he gives priority to the congregation. It is transmitted in al-Kafi and al-Muhit that he performs the sunnah according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) contrary to Muhammad (al-Shaybani), because catching the sitting (tashahhud) according to them is like catching a rak'ah in Jumu'ah, contrary to him. The author has made for the Fajr sunnah two rulings: the action if he does not fear missing the congregation (that is the meaning of 'fear of missing Fajr' as indicated by his saying 'he completes it'), and the abandonment if he fears missing the congregation. Thus what al-Faqih Isma'il al-Zahid mentioned is refuted: that he should begin the two rak'ahs of Fajr, then cut them off and enter with the imam so that they become obligatory by starting, enabling him to make them up after Fajr. This is rejected from two aspects: first, what Imam al-Sarakhsi mentioned that what becomes obligatory by starting is not stronger than what becomes obligatory by vow, and Muhammad has stated that the vowed prayer is not performed after Fajr before sunrise. Second, what Qadikhan mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that the mashayikh disapproved of this, because it is an order to begin prayer with the intention of cutting it and not completing it, which is not recommended. Then there is a condition that the author omitted in his saying 'otherwise not': that he finds a place in the mosque to pray the sunnah. If he does not find, then he should not pray the sunnah because avoiding the disliked takes precedence over performing the sunnah. Thus in Fath al-Qadir, and it is branched on one of two opinions. According to al-Muhit: If he prays them in the outer mosque while the imam prays in the inner mosque, it is said not disliked because he does not appear to be opposing due to the difference of place in reality; and it is said disliked because all of that is like one place. So when the mashayikh differed in it, the best is not to do it.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq about performing the Fajr sunnah when one fears missing the congregation. The commentator explains that normally the Fajr sunnah is highly recommended, but when it conflicts with the congregation, the latter takes precedence. The proof includes the hadith praising Fajr sunnah and the general evidence for congregation. The commentator then discusses a dispute among Hanafi scholars: if one hopes to catch only the tashahhud, should he still perform the sunnah? According to some sources, if he fears missing both rak'ahs, he should skip the sunnah. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that if he will catch at least the tashahhud, he should perform the sunnah, because catching the sitting is like catching a rak'ah in Jumu'ah. Abu Hanifa's position is preferred in al-Bada'i. The commentator also refutes the idea of starting the sunnah then cutting it off to join the congregation, as that would involve intending to cut off a prayer, which is not approved. Finally, a condition is added: if there is a separate place in the mosque to pray the sunnah without appearing to oppose the congregation, it may be permissible, but if not, one should avoid it to prevent dislike.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs before the Fajr obligatory prayer, highly recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah).
إدراك التشهد (idrak al-tashahhud): Catching the final sitting (tashahhud) with the imam, considered as catching a rak'ah by some scholars.
مخالفة الجماعة (mukhalafat al-jama'ah): Opposing or appearing to oppose the congregation by praying separately, which is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person fears that performing the Fajr sunnah will cause him to miss the entire Fajr congregation, what should he do according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Perform the sunnah quickly and then join the congregation
B) Skip the sunnah and join the congregation immediately
C) Perform the sunnah and then pray Fajr alone
D) Start the sunnah, then cut it off to join the congregation

Key Takeaway
When a conflict arises between performing the Fajr sunnah and joining the Fajr congregation, the congregation takes precedence; skip the sunnah and join the imam immediately.

Salah — Prayer

Supererogatory Prayer During Iqamah: Ruling and the Fajr Exception
Commentary on performing sunnah/nafl during iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing supererogatory prayers during iqamah, identify the proof, and explain the exception for the Fajr sunnah.

Core Idea
Praying nafl during iqamah is disliked, but the Fajr sunnah is excluded by Imam Muhammad's explicit text.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses an important timing nuance in salah: whether one may begin a voluntary prayer when the iqamah has started. The general rule is that it is disliked due to potential suspicion of avoiding congregation. However, Imam Muhammad made a specific exception for the Fajr sunnah, leading to an intra-madhhab debate on its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is beginning a supererogatory prayer (nafl or sunnah) during the iqamah. The initial ruling from the passage is that it is disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it may create suspicion that one is avoiding the congregation.
The ruling applies whether it is two rak'ahs of Fajr or any other voluntary prayer, unless an exception is proven.
2
Locate the primary proof
The proof cited is the hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not stand in places of suspicion' (related by Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). This hadith is used to argue that praying during iqamah could cause false suspicion.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and its dalala is also zanni, allowing for exceptions via Istihsan or other proofs.
3
Find the exception in the source
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani explicitly stated in Kitab al-Salat from al-Asl: 'Is it disliked to perform a voluntary prayer? He said: Yes, except the two rak'ahs of Fajr.' This exception is a clear text from a Zahir al-Riwayah source.
This exception is specific to the Fajr sunnah; other voluntary prayers remain disliked during iqamah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi difference
Some Hanafi mashayikh interpret the exception narrowly, applying it only when the person has missed the initial takbir of the congregational prayer. The majority (including Fakhr al-Kamal, al-Halabi, al-Maqdisi) take the exception absolutely, regardless of whether one catches the takbir or not.
The difference affects whether one should pray the Fajr sunnah if he enters before the imam starts or only if he arrives late.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the absolute exception: one may pray the Fajr sunnah during iqamah as long as it can be completed before the imam finishes the obligatory prayer. This is supported by Fakhr al-Kamal and adopted by later Hanafi scholars.
If finishing the sunnah before the imam ends is uncertain, it is better to skip it and join the congregation immediately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل أن حكم المصلي نافلة أو سنة لا يخلوا ما أن يكون قبل شروع الإمام في الفرض أو بعده، فإن كان الأول لا يخلوا ما أن يكون وقت إقامة المؤذن أو قبله، فإن كان قبل إقامة المؤذن فله أن يأتي بهما في أي موضع أراد من المسجد أو غيره إلا في الطريق كما قدمناه ، وإن كان وقت إقامة المؤذن ففي البدائع إذا دخل المسجد للصلاة وقد كان المؤذن أخذ في الإقامة يكره له التطوع، سواء كان ركعتي الفجر أو غيرهما، لأنه بأنه لا يرى صلاة الجماعة وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يقفن مواقف التهم ا اه. وبحث العلامة الحلبي بأن هذا الظن يزول عنه في ثاني الحال إذا شوهد شروعه فيها بعد فراغه من السنة، وقد نص محمد في كتاب الصلاة من الأصل في المؤذن يأخذ في الإقامة أيكره أن يتطوع ؟ قال : نعم إلا ركعتي الفجر . واختلف المشايخ في فهمه؛ فمنهم من قال موضعها فيما إذا انتهى إلى الإمام وقد سبقه بالتكبير فيأتي بركعتي الفجر وعامتهم على الإطلاق سواء وصل إلى الإمام بعد شروعه أو قبله في الإقامة كما ذكره فخر الكمال : وهذ يعكر على ما قيل فيمن يرجوا إدراك التشهد في الفجر لو اشتغل بركعتيه من أنه قول محمد لا اعتبار به فيترك ركعتي الفجر على قوله فالحق خلافه لنص محمد هنا على ما يناقضه اهـ. في كلام الشرنبلالية والحاصل أنه متابع للمحقق الكمال في ذلك والوجه معه وقد نقل الشيخ ابراهيم الحلبي كلام الكمال ،وأقره ، وكذا العلامة المقدسي في شرح النظم ومشى عليه في المنح فليتأمل مع ما مر قوله : (وهو مرود الخ قال في العناية أقوال : إن أراد الفقيه بقوله بعد الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس فالتزييف موجه وإن أراد بعده فلا والقصد للقطع نقض للإكمال فلا بأس به وفي الحواشي السعدية فيه بحث إذ لا إكمال فيها فإنها لا تؤدى بالجماعة، ألا ترى إلى ما مر من قوله بخلاف النفل لأنه ليس للإكمال وكان الصواب أن يقول ليؤديها مرة أخرى، وجوابه أن إبطال اهـ.
In summary, the ruling of one praying a voluntary or sunnah prayer is either before the imam starts the obligatory prayer or after. If before, it is either during the iqamah or before. If before the iqamah, he may perform them in any place he wishes in the mosque or elsewhere except on the road, as we previously mentioned. If it is during the iqamah, then in al-Bada'i: if he enters the mosque for prayer while the mu'adhdhin has begun the iqamah, it is disliked for him to perform a supererogatory prayer, whether it is the two rak'ahs of Fajr or other, because he would appear as not seeing the congregation, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not stand in places of suspicion.' (End). Al-Halabi discussed that this suspicion is removed if he is seen starting after finishing the sunnah. Muhammad has stated in Kitab al-Salat from al-Asl regarding the mu'adhdhin beginning the iqamah: 'Is it disliked to perform a voluntary prayer?' He said: 'Yes, except the two rak'ahs of Fajr.' The mashayikh differed in understanding this. Some said its place is when he reaches the imam and the imam has preceded him in takbir, so he performs the two rak'ahs of Fajr. But the majority said absolutely, whether he reaches the imam after starting or before in the iqamah, as mentioned by Fakhr al-Kamal. This contradicts what was said that the one hoping to catch the tashahhud in Fajr, if he occupies himself with his two rak'ahs, that is a statement of Muhammad not to be considered, so he leaves the two rak'ahs of Fajr according to his statement; the truth is contrary due to Muhammad's text here that contradicts it. (End). In the words of al-Shirnblali: The summary is that he follows al-Muhaqqiq al-Kamal in that, and the correct view is with him. Sheikh Ibrahim al-Halabi transmitted the words of al-Kamal and approved them, as did al-Maqdisi in Sharh al-Nuzum, and it is followed in al-Minh. So reflect on what has passed. His saying: (He is rejected, etc.) Al-‘Inaya said: There are sayings: If the faqih meant by his saying 'after Fajr before sunrise', then the rejection is valid; if he meant after, then no. The intention to cut is a breach of completion, so it is fine. In al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyya, there is a discussion: there is no completion in it because it is not performed with congregation. Do you not see what passed from his statement unlike nafl because it is not for completion? The correct thing would be to say 'to perform it another time.' The answer is that invalidation... (End).
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage summarizes the ruling on performing supererogatory prayers (nafl or sunnah) in relation to the iqamah. If before the iqamah, one may pray in the mosque or elsewhere except on a path. If the iqamah has started, it is disliked to begin any voluntary prayer, because it may create suspicion that one is avoiding the congregation. However, Imam Muhammad made an exception for the Fajr sunnah. The commentators debate the scope of this exception: some limit it to when one has missed the initial takbir, while others apply it generally. The author favors the view that the exception applies broadly, and that one should perform the Fajr sunnah even during iqamah if one can still catch the congregation. This contradicts an earlier suggestion that if one hopes only to catch the tashahhud, he should skip the sunnah. The correct view, according to al-Kamal and others, is that Muhammad's explicit text allows the Fajr sunnah during iqamah, so it should be followed. The passage also touches on the issue of cutting a prayer to join the congregation, which is generally disapproved except when necessary.

Key Terms
الإقامة (al-iqamah): The second call to prayer, signaling the start of the congregational prayer.
مواقف التهم (mawaqif al-tuham): Places or situations that cause suspicion or bad assumptions about a person's intentions.
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary prayer, including both sunnah and nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the ruling on performing the Fajr sunnah when the iqamah has begun?
A) It is disliked like any other voluntary prayer
B) It is permissible and not disliked
C) It is forbidden
D) It is only allowed if one has missed the takbir

Key Takeaway
The general ruling of makruh tahrimi for supererogatory prayers during iqamah is lifted for the Fajr sunnah based on Imam Muhammad's explicit text in al-Asl.

Ruling on Sunnah Prayers During Iqamah and the Exception for Fajr
Expansion of the ruling on Sunnah prayers during iqamah with emphasis on the Fajr exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing Sunnah prayers during iqamah, identify the exception for Fajr, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its scope.

Core Idea
Performing voluntary prayers during iqamah is disliked, but the two rak'ahs of Fajr are explicitly exempted.

Imagine you arrive at the mosque and the muadhdhin has begun the iqamah. You have not yet prayed the Sunnah of Fajr. Should you pray them or rush to join the congregation? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the text of Muhammad al-Shaybani, but later scholars debated the scope. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The performance of any voluntary prayer (Sunnah or nafl) during the iqamah. The hukm level is makruh tanzih, meaning it is disliked but not sinful.
The dislike stems from the suspicion of avoiding the congregation, not from any intrinsic impurity.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited in the text: the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him), 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not stand in places of suspicion.' This is the basis for the dislike.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but its meaning is clear in discouraging actions that create suspicion.
3
Note the exception
Despite the general dislike, Muhammad al-Shaybani explicitly exempts the two rak'ahs of Fajr. His text in al-Asl states that it is disliked to volunteer during iqamah 'except the two rak'ahs of Fajr.'
This exemption is a specific text (takhsis) from the general ruling.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Later scholars differed on whether the exception applies only when one reaches the imam after he has started, or generally. The majority (عامتهم) hold it is general, which is the mufta bihi.
Understanding this dispute helps in applying the ruling in different scenarios.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that one may pray the Fajr Sunnah during iqamah regardless of whether the imam has started. This is the view followed for fatwa.
The practical consequence: one should not skip the Fajr Sunnah out of concern for missing the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب إدراك الفريضة
وهو عند باب إسماعيل الزاهد من أنه ينبغي أن يفتتح ركعتي الفجر ثم يقطعهما ويدخل مع الإمام حتى تلزمه بالشروع فيتمكن من القضاء بعد الفجر وهو مردود من وجهين: أحدهما ما ذكره الإمام السرخسي أن ما وجب بالشروع لا يكون أقوى مما وجب بالنذر وقد نص محمد أن المنذورة لا تؤدى بعد الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس. ثانيهما ما ذكره قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير أن المشايخ نكروا عليه ذلك لأن هذا أمر بافتتاح الصلاة على قصد أن يقطع ولا يتم وأنه غير مستحسن. ثم إن هنا قيداً تركه المصنف في قوله «وإلا لا» أن يجد مكاناً المسجد يصلي السنة فيه، فإن لم يجد فينبغي أن لا يصلي السنة لأن ترك المكروه مقدم على فعل السنة. كذا في فتح القدير وهو متفرع على أحد القولين لما في المحيط : ولو صلاهما في المسجد الخارج والإمام يصلي في المسجد الداخل قيل لا يكره لأنه لا يتصور بصورة المخالفة لاختلاف المكان حقيقة ، وقيل يكره لأن ذلك كله كمكان واحد فإذا اختلف المشايخ فيه كان الأفضل أن لا يفعل اهـ. فالحاصل أن حكم المصلي نافلة أو سنة لا يخلوا ما أن يكون قبل شروع الإمام في الفرض أو بعده، فإن كان الأول لا يخلوا ما أن يكون وقت إقامة المؤذن أو قبله، فإن كان قبل إقامة المؤذن فله أن يأتي بهما في أي موضع أراد من المسجد أو غيره إلا في الطريق كما قدمناه ، وإن كان وقت إقامة المؤذن ففي البدائع إذا دخل المسجد للصلاة وقد كان المؤذن أخذ في الإقامة يكره له التطوع، سواء كان ركعتي الفجر أو غيرهما، لأنه بأنه لا يرى صلاة الجماعة وقد قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يقفن مواقف التهم ا اه. وبحث العلامة الحلبي بأن هذا الظن يزول عنه في ثاني الحال إذا شوهد شروعه فيها بعد فراغه من السنة، وقد نص محمد في كتاب الصلاة من الأصل في المؤذن يأخذ في الإقامة أيكره أن يتطوع ؟ قال : نعم إلا ركعتي الفجر . واختلف المشايخ في فهمه ؛ فمنهم من قال موضعها فيما إذا انتهى إلى الإمام وقد سبقه بالتكبير فيأتي بركعتي الفجر وعامتهم على الإطلاق سواء وصل إلى الإمام بعد شروعه أو قبله في الإقامة كما ذكره فخر الدين على الكمال : وهذ يعكر على ما قيل فيمن يرجوا إدراك التشهد في الفجر لو اشتغل بركعتيه من أنه قول محمد لا اعتبار به فيترك ركعتي الفجر على قوله فالحق خلافه لنص محمد هنا على ما يناقضه اهـ. في كلام الشرنبلالية والحاصل أنه متابع للمحقق الكمال في ذلك والوجه معه وقد نقل الشيخ ابراهيم الحلبي كلام الكمال ،وأقره ، وكذا العلامة المقدسي في شرح النظم ومشى عليه في المنح فليتأمل مع ما مر قوله : (وهو مرود الخ قال في العناية أقوال : إن أراد الفقيه بقوله بعد الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس فالتزييف موجه وإن أراد بعده فلا والقصد للقطع نقض للإكمال فلا بأس به وفي الحواشي السعدية فيه بحث إذ لا إكمال فيها فإنها لا تؤدى بالجماعة، ألا ترى إلى ما مر من قوله بخلاف النفل لأنه ليس للإكمال وكان الصواب أن يقول ليؤديها مرة أخرى، وجوابه أن إبطال الفجر إن أدى سنته أيتم وتركها وإلا لا ولم تقض إلا تبعاً وقضى التي قبل الظهر في الإسلام . ما في الحاوي القدسي والمحيط ولا يتطوع إذا أخذ المؤذن في الإقامة إلا ركعتي الفجر ا هـ . إلا أنه قد يقال : إن ما يوقع في التهمة لا يرتكب وإن ارتفعت بعده كما ورد عن علي : إياك وما يسبق إلى القلوب إنكاره وإن كان عندك اعتذاره. وإن كان الثاني فيكره له أن يشتغل بنفل أو سنة مؤكدة إلا سنة الفجر على التفصيل السابق . ثم السنة في السنن أن يأتي بها في بيته أو عند باب المسجد وإن لم يمكن ففي المسجد الخارج وإن كان المسجد واحداً فخلف الإسطوانة ونحو ذلك، أو في آخر المسجد بعيداً عن الصفوف في ناحية منه. وتكره في موضعين : الأول أن يصليها مخالطاً للصف مخالفاً للجماعة . الثاني أن يكون خلف الصف من غير حائل بينه وبين الصف والأول أشد كراهة من الثاني. وأما السنن التي بعد الفرائض فالأفضل فعلها في المنزل إلا إذا خاف الاشتغال عنها لو ذهب إلى البيت فيأتي بها في المسجد في أي مكان منه ولو في مكان صلى فيه فرضه والأولى أن يتنحى خطوة. ويكره للإمام أن يصلي مكان صلى فيه فرضه. كذا في الكافي وغيره .
يعني فما في البدائع من التعميم لركعتي الفجر ليس على قول العامة ويشهد له في قوله : (ولم تقض إلا تبعاً) أي لم تقض سنة الفجر إلا إذا فاتت مع الفرض فتقضي تبعاً للفرض سواء قضاها مع الجماعة أو وحده لأن الأصل في السنة أن لا تقضى لاختصاص القضاء بالواجب والحديث ورد في قضائها تبعاً للفرض في غداة ليلة التعريس فبقي ما وراءه على الأصل، فأفاد المصنف أنها لا تقضى قبل طلوع الشمس أصلاً ولا بعد الطلوع إذا كان قد أدى الفرض. وشمل كلامه ما إذا قضاهما بعد الزوال أو قبله ولا خلاف في الثاني . واختلف المشايخ في الأول على قولهما والصحيح كما في غاية البيان أنها لا تقضى تبعاً لأن العمل قصداً منهي ودرء المفسدة مقدم على جلب المصلحة ا هـ قوله : (يعني فما في البدائع من التعميم لركعتي الفجر ليس على قول العامة تخصيصه بأنه ليس على قول العامة محل نظر بل المفهوم من الكلام قبله أنه ليس على قول الجميع فليتأمل قوله : (ثم السنة في السنن الخ) أقول : المذكور في النهاية والعناية وشرح قاضيخان وغيرهما أن ما ذكرهم السنة هو في سنة الفجر، وأما غيرها ففي التبيين إن أمكنه أن يأتي بها قبل أن يركع الإمام أتى بها خارج المسجد ثم شرع في الفرض معه لأنه أمكنه إحراز الفضيلتين، وإن خاف فوت ركعة شرع معه بخلاف سنة الفجر على ما مر ا هـ . فالصواب أن يقول ثم السنة في السنة كما عبر به المقدسي في شرحه وقد رأيته كذلك في أصل بعض النسخ لكنه مصلح بالسنن، وهذا الإصلاح إفساد كما رأيت ثم هذا الحكم المذكور إذا كان بعد الشروع في الفريضة كما في المنية قال : وأما قبل شروعهم في الفريضة فيأتي بها في أي موضع شاء ا هـ. وقد علم هذا مما مر وبه يعلم أن الصواب ما قلناه لأن غير سنة الفجر ليس كذلك كما بينه المؤلف قوله : (لأن سائر السنن لا تقتضى) إلى آخر عبارته. قال في الهداية وأما سائر السنن سواها لا تقضى بعد
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. ... It is reported from Isma'il al-Zahid that one should begin the two rak'ahs of Fajr then cut them and enter with the Imam so that they become binding by starting, enabling him to make them up after Fajr. This is rejected on two grounds: first, what Imam al-Sarakhsi mentioned that what becomes obligatory by starting is not stronger than what becomes obligatory by vow, and Muhammad texted that a vowed prayer is not performed after Fajr before sunrise. Second, what Qadikhan mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that the scholars disapproved of it because it is an order to start a prayer with the intention to cut and not complete, which is not commendable. Then there is a condition the author left out in his statement 'otherwise no': that he finds a place in the mosque to pray the Sunnah; if he does not find, he should not pray the Sunnah because avoiding dislike is prioritized over performing the Sunnah. ... The summary: the ruling of one praying a supererogatory or Sunnah prayer is either before the Imam starts the obligatory or after. If before, it is either during the iqamah or before. If before the iqamah, he may perform them anywhere in the mosque or elsewhere except in the road. If during the iqamah, in al-Bada'i' it is disliked to volunteer, whether the two rak'ahs of Fajr or others, because it is thought he does not care for the congregation, and the Prophet said: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not stand in places of suspicion.' ...
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of performing Sunnah prayers when the congregation is about to begin. The author first critiques the view of Isma'il al-Zahid who suggested starting the Fajr Sunnah with the intention to cut them and join the Imam. This is rejected because it makes an act that becomes obligatory by starting (like a supererogatory prayer after beginning) similar to a vowed prayer, which cannot be performed after Fajr before sunrise. Also, it involves starting a prayer intending to break it, which is not commendable. The author then explains that if one cannot find a place to pray the Sunnah in the mosque (i.e., behind the rows), it is better not to pray to avoid the dislike of being in the suspect position of seeming to avoid the congregation. The main ruling: before the iqamah, one may pray Sunnah anywhere; during the iqamah, it is disliked to pray any voluntary prayer except the two rak'ahs of Fajr, based on the text of Muhammad in al-Asl. There is disagreement among later scholars about whether this exception applies only when one reaches the Imam after he has begun or generally; the majority hold it is general. The passage also covers where to pray Sunnah: best at home, then at the mosque door, then in the outer mosque, etc. It discusses the dislike of praying in specific places and the ruling on making up missed Sunnah of Fajr: it is only made up if the obligatory prayer was missed along with it, but not otherwise. Finally, the author clarifies that the general statement in al-Bada'i' that all voluntary prayers are disliked during iqamah is not the unanimous view; the exception for Fajr is well-established.

Key Terms
تطوع (tatawwu'): Voluntary acts of worship, including both supererogatory prayers (nawafil) and Sunnah prayers.
إقامة (iqamah): The second call to prayer given just before the obligatory prayer begins, signaling that the congregation is about to start.
سنن (sunan): Plural of Sunnah; here refers to the confirmed Sunnah prayers (rawatib) associated with the obligatory prayers, especially the two rak'ahs before Fajr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing the two rak'ahs of Fajr Sunnah when the mu'adhdhin is giving the iqamah?
A) It is disliked (makruh) because it creates suspicion.
B) It is permissible and not disliked, based on the exception in Muhammad's text.
C) It is forbidden (haram) because the iqamah is obligatory.
D) It is recommended (mustahabb) to do them to gain extra reward.

Key Takeaway
The general rule is that voluntary prayers during iqamah are disliked, but the two rak'ahs of Fajr are an explicit exception; the relied-upon view allows them without restriction.

Ruling on Making Up the Sunnah of Fajr
Explains that the Fajr sunnah is only made up along with the fard prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the Fajr sunnah and identify the condition under which it is permitted.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is only made up when the fard is also missed—not independently.

Many assume that missed sunnah prayers are simply lost with no possibility of recovery. However, the Hanafi school makes a specific exception for the Fajr sunnah based on a prophetic precedent. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and the underlying principle that distinguishes it from other sunnah prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? The sunnah of Fajr (two rak‘ahs before the fard). What is the ruling regarding making it up? It is not made up independently, only as a follower (taba‘an).
The ruling is specific to the Fajr sunnah; other sunnah prayers are generally not made up.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith of the night of al-Ta‘ris, when the Prophet ﷺ and his companions overslept and missed Fajr. Upon waking, they made up both the fard and the sunnah together.
This is an ahad hadith, zanni in transmission and indication, but sufficient for establishing a sunnah ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet’s action of making up the sunnah along with the fard establishes that the sunnah is made up only as a follower. The phrase 'taba‘an' indicates subordination.
The original principle is that qada is specific to obligations; the hadith creates an exception.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any disagreement? Among the founding imams, no. Among later mashayikh, there is disagreement on whether the sunnah can be made up as a follower after zawal (midday). The correct view (as in Ghayat al-Bayan) is that it is not made up, because repelling harm (dislike of praying at prohibited times) takes precedence.
The mufta bihi position follows the earlier view: only when the fard is missed, and then only within the same general time frame.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفجر إن أدى سنته أتمها وتركها وإلا فلا ولم تقض إلا تبعاً (أي لم تقض سنة الفجر إلا إذا فاتت مع الفرض فتقضي تبعاً للفرض سواء قضاها مع الجماعة أو وحده لأن الأصل في السنة أن لا تقضى لاختصاص القضاء بالواجب والحديث ورد في قضائها تبعاً للفرض في غداة ليلة التعريس فبقي ما وراءه على الأصل، فأفاد المصنف أنها لا تقضى قبل طلوع الشمس أصلاً ولا بعد الطلوع إذا كان قد أدى الفرض. وشمل كلامه ما إذا قضاهما بعد الزوال أو قبله ولا خلاف في الثاني. واختلف المشايخ في الأول على قولهما والصحيح كما في غاية البيان أنها لا تقضى تبعاً لأن العمل قصداً منهي ودرء المفسدة مقدم على جلب المصلحة ا هـ.
Fajr: if he performs its sunnah, he completes it and leaves it, otherwise no, and it is not made up except as a follower. That is, the sunnah of Fajr is not made up except when it is missed along with the fard, so it is made up as a follower of the fard, whether he makes it up with the congregation or alone, because the principle is that sunnah is not made up, since making up is specific to obligations. And the hadith came about making it up as a follower of the fard on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris, so what remains beyond that remains on the original principle. Thus the author indicated that it is not made up before sunrise at all, nor after sunrise if he had performed the fard. And his statement includes whether he makes them up after zawal or before it, and there is no dispute in the second. The mashayikh differed in the first according to their statement, and the correct view as in Ghayat al-Bayan is that it is not made up as a follower, because the action is prohibited intentionally, and repelling harm takes precedence over bringing benefit. End.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the sunnah of Fajr. The matn states that the Fajr sunnah is not made up except in conjunction with the fard. The commentary explains that the original principle is that sunnah prayers are not made up because qada is specific to obligatory acts. However, an exception is established by the hadith of the night of al-Ta'ris (when the Prophet ﷺ and his companions missed Fajr prayer and made up both the fard and the sunnah together). Hence, if a person misses the Fajr fard, he should make up both the fard and the sunnah with it. But if he only missed the sunnah while performing the fard on time, the sunnah is not made up at any time—neither before sunrise nor after. There is no disagreement on this. The commentary also notes a difference among later scholars regarding making up the sunnah after zawal when the fard was missed before zawal; the sound view is that it is not made up even as a follower because acting intentionally in a prohibited time is avoided.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up an obligatory or sunnah prayer after its prescribed time has passed.
تبعاً (taba'an): As a follower; here meaning the sunnah is made up together with the fard prayer, not independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the sunnah of Fajr be made up?
A) At any time after sunrise
B) Only when the Fajr fard is also missed, and then along with it
C) Only before sunrise on the same day
D) It is never made up under any circumstances

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of Fajr is an exception to the rule that sunnah prayers are not made up; it is only made up when the fard is also missed, and then as a follower.

Making Up the Four Sunnah Before Zuhr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of Zuhr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on making up the four rak'ahs before Zuhr and identify the preferred view (mufta bihi) regarding their nature and order.

Core Idea
All Hanafis agree the four before Zuhr are made up, but they differ on whether they remain sunnah and when to pray them.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we encounter a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the four sunnah rak'ahs before Zuhr. While there is consensus that they should be made up if missed, the imams differ on two points: first, whether the make-up prayer retains its sunnah status or becomes nafil, and second, the order of making them up relative to the two sunnah after Zuhr. Understanding this dispute sharpens our appreciation of how the school's internal reasoning works and how later authorities (like the author of Fath al-Qadir) resolve such differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed point
All Hanafi imams agree that the four sunnah rak'ahs before Zuhr are to be made up (qada) if missed, based on the hadith of 'A'isha that the Prophet ﷺ would make them up after Zuhr.
2
Recognize the first dispute: nature of the make-up
Abu Hanifa holds that when made up, these rak'ahs become nafil (supererogatory), not sunnah. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that they remain sunnah. The author of Fath al-Qadir argues that the agreement on making them up implies they are sunnah.
3
Recognize the second dispute: order of prayer
Should one pray the two sunnah after Zuhr first, or the four make-up first? There are conflicting narrations: in some sources Abu Yusuf advances the two after, Muhammad delays them, and in others the opposite. Fath al-Qadir prefers advancing the two after because the four have already missed their sunnah time.
The shaf' (pair) refers to the two sunnah after Zuhr.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
Fath al-Qadir gives preference to praying the two sunnah after Zuhr first, then making up the four before Zuhr. This is because the four have already missed their optimal time, so they should not delay the two from their proper position.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is: if one misses both the four sunnah before and the two sunnah after Zuhr, one should first pray the two after (with intention of sunnah), then the four before (with intention of sunnah), because the four are still considered sunnah when made up.
The same ruling applies to the four sunnah before Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقضى التي قبل الظهر في وقته قبل شفعه بيان الشيئين: أحدهما القضاء والثاني محله . أما الأول ففيه اختلاف والصحيح أنها تقضى كما ذكره قاضيخان في شرحه مستدلاً بما عن عائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا فاتته الأربع قبل الظهر قضاهن بعده وظاهر كلام المصنف أنها سنة لا نفل مطلق، وذكر قاضيخان أنه إذا قضاها فهي لا تكون سنة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما سنة، وتبعه الشارح، وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه من تصرف المصنفين فإن المذكور من وضع المسألة الاتفاق على قضاء الأربع، وإنما الاختلاف في تقديمها أو تأخيرها والاتفاق على أنها تقضى اتفاق على وقوعها سنة إلى آخر ما ذكره. وأما الثاني فاختلف فيه النقل عن الشيخين فذكر في الجامع الصغير للحسامي أن أبا يوسف يقدم الركعتين ومحمد يؤخرهما. وفي المنظومة وشروحها على العكس. وفي غاية البيان: ويحتمل أن يكون عن كل واحد من الإمامين روايتان. ورجح في فتح القدير تقديم الركعتين لأن الأربع فاتت عن الموضع المسنون فلا يفوت الركعتين عن موضعهما قصداً وحكم الأربع قبل الجمعة كالأربع قبل الظهر كما لا يخفى.
And he makes up that which is before Zuhr in its time before its shaf'. Explanation of two things: one is the making up and the second is its place. As for the first, there is disagreement, but the correct view is that it is made up, as Qadikhan mentioned in his commentary, citing 'A'isha that the Prophet, when he missed the four before Zuhr, would make them up after it. And the apparent meaning of the author's words is that it is a sunnah, not an absolute nafil. Qadikhan mentioned that when he makes them up, they are not sunnah according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) they are sunnah. The commentator followed him, but was criticized in Fath al-Qadir, saying it is a misrepresentation by the authors, for the established matter is agreement on making up the four, and the only difference is in advancing or delaying them, and the agreement on making them up is agreement that they occur as sunnah, etc. As for the second, the transmission from the two shaykhs differs: in al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Husami, Abu Yusuf advances the two rak'ahs and Muhammad delays them. In al-Manzumah and its commentaries, the opposite is stated. In Ghayat al-Bayan: it is possible that each of the two imams has two narrations. And in Fath al-Qadir, preference is given to advancing the two rak'ahs because the four have missed their sunnah position, so the two should not miss their position intentionally. And the ruling of the four before Jumu'ah is like the four before Zuhr, as is clear.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the four sunnah rak'ahs before Zuhr. The matn states that these are made up in their time before the two rak'ahs after ('shaf'). The commentary explains two issues: first, whether they are actually made up, and second, the order of making them up relative to the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. On the first issue, the correct view is that they are made up, supported by the hadith of 'A'isha. There is a disagreement among Hanafi imams about the nature of these made-up rak'ahs: Abu Hanifa holds that they become nafil, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that they remain sunnah. The commentator in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq follows Qadikhan on this, but Fath al-Qadir criticizes this, arguing that the agreement on making them up implies they remain sunnah. On the second issue, there is a transmission from Abu Yusuf that he advances the two rak'ahs (after Zuhr) and Muhammad delays them, but other sources state the opposite. Fath al-Qadir prefers advancing the two because the four have already missed their preferred time. The same ruling applies to the four before Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
شفع (shaf'): The two sunnah rak'ahs after Zuhr; literally 'pair' or 'even number'.
سنة (sunnah): A confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) that the Prophet regularly performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view (mufta bihi), what is the nature of the four sunnah before Zuhr when made up?
A) They become nafil.
B) They remain sunnah.
C) They become fard.
D) They are not made up.

Key Takeaway
The four sunnah before Zuhr are made up after Zuhr, and the preferred order is to pray the two after first, then the four before, all with intention of sunnah.

The Status of Qada for Missed Sunnah Prayers: Sunnah or Nafl?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of qada for sunnah prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed sunnah prayers, identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on its status (sunnah vs nafl), and explain why the mufta bihi opinion considers it sunnah.

Core Idea
Missed sunnah prayers are made up after time, but their status (sunnah or nafl) is disputed within the Hanafi school.

This lesson examines a practical issue: if you miss the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr, can you make them up, and do they retain the reward of sunnah or only nafl? The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa considers the qada to be nafl, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold it to be sunnah. We will analyze the evidence and determine the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
The act is making up a missed sunnah prayer (specifically the four before Dhuhr) after its time. The ruling is that it is recommended (sunnah) to make it up, but there is disagreement on the category of the made-up prayer.
The base ruling comes from the hadith of Aisha.
2
Notice the Consensus on Qada
All Hanafi imams agree that the missed sunnah is made up. The dispute is not about whether to make it up, but about the reward: does it count as sunnah or nafl?
The hadith provides a textual basis overriding the general qiyas that qada is only for fard.
3
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that the qada is nafl (not sunnah). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold it is sunnah. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq indicates that the apparent meaning of the matn is that it is sunnah.
4
Examine the Evidence
The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of Aisha (the Prophet's action). Abu Hanifa's reasoning is based on qiyas: since the original time for sunnah has passed, the qada cannot retain the same status. The Hanafi response is that the hadith is specific and overrides the qiyas.
The Shafi'i school rejects qada of sunnah altogether, relying on general qiyas.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, that the qada is sunnah. This is supported by the majority of later Hanafi scholars and the commentary in al-Hidayah.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the hadith and the principle that a specific text overrides qiyas.

وقته قبل شفعه ولم يصل الظهر جماعة بإدراك ركعة بل أدرك فضلها وتطوع قبل الفرض
النص ورد بقضائها في الوقت المهمل بخلاف القياس، وما ورد على خلاف القياس فغيره عليه لا يقاس وهي واردة على المصنف، فلو قال ولم تقض إلا تبعاً قبل الزوال» لكان أولى. وقيد بسنة الفجر لأن سائر السنن لا تقضى بعد الوقت لا تبعاً ولا مقصوداً. واختلف المشايخ في قضائها تبعاً للفرض في الوقت والظاهر قضاؤها وأنها سنة لاختلاف الشيخين في قضاء الأربع قبل الظهر قبل الركعتين أو بعدهما كما سيأتي قوله: (وقضى التي قبل الظهر في وقته قبل شفعه بيان الشيئين: أحدهما القضاء والثاني محله . أما الأول ففيه اختلاف والصحيح أنها تقضى كما ذكره قاضيخان في شرحه مستدلاً بما عن عائشة أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان إذا فاتته الأربع قبل الظهر قضاهن بعده وظاهر كلام المصنف أنها سنة لا نفل مطلق، وذكر قاضيخان أنه إذا قضاها فهي لا تكون سنة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما سنة، وتبعه الشارح، وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه من تصرف المصنفين فإن المذكور من وضع المسألة الاتفاق على قضاء الأربع، وإنما الاختلاف في تقديمها أو تأخيرها والاتفاق على أنها تقضى اتفاق على وقوعها سنة إلى آخر ما ذكره. وأما الثاني فاختلف فيه النقل عن الشيخين فذكر في الجامع الصغير للحسامي أن أبا يوسف يقدم الركعتين ومحمد يؤخرهما. وفي المنظومة وشروحها على العكس. وفي غاية البيان: ويحتمل أن يكون عن كل واحد من الإمامين روايتان. ورجح في فتح القدير تقديم الركعتين لأن الأربع فاتت عن الموضع المسنون فلا يفوت الركعتين عن موضعهما قصداً وحكم الأربع قبل الجمعة كالأربع قبل الظهر كما لا يخفى.
Book of Prayer, Chapter: Catching the Obligatory Prayer. Its time before its [the sunnah's] duplicate, and he did not pray Dhuhr in congregation catching a rak'ah, rather he caught its virtue and performed voluntary prayer before the obligatory. The text [of the matn] came with its [the sunnah's] qada in the neglected time, contrary to qiyas. And what comes contrary to qiyas, nothing else is analogized to it. And it [the ruling] applies to the author [of the matn]. So if he had said 'and it is only made up as a following [tab'an] before zawal' it would have been better. And the mashayikh differed regarding its qada as a following of the obligatory in the time. Explanation of two things: one is the qada and the second is its place. As for the first, there is ikhtilaf and the correct is that it is made up as mentioned by Qadikhan in his commentary, using as evidence what is reported from Aisha that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when he missed the four before Dhuhr, he made them up after it. And the apparent meaning of the author's statement is that it is sunnah, not absolute nafl. And Qadikhan mentioned that when he makes them up, they are not sunnah according to Abu Hanifa, but according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] they are sunnah, and the commentator followed him. And it was objected in Fath al-Qadir that this is from the authors' own interpretation, for the mentioned issue is agreement on making up the four, only the ikhtilaf is in their precedence or delay, and agreement that they are made up is agreement that they occur as sunnah, etc. As for the second, the transmission from the two shaykhs differs. It is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir of al-Husami that Abu Yusuf gives precedence to the two rak'ahs [of Fajr] and Muhammad delays them. And in al-Manzumah and its commentaries, it is the opposite. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: It is possible that from each of the two imams there are two narrations. And in Fath al-Qadir, precedence of the two rak'ahs was preferred because the four were missed from their sunnah place, so the two rak'ahs do not miss their place intentionally. And the ruling of the four before Jumu'ah is like the four before Dhuhr, as is not hidden.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of making up missed sunnah prayers after their time, specifically focusing on the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr and the two rak'ahs of Fajr. The author explains that the matn's text indicates that these are made up only as a following (tab'an) to the obligatory prayer before zawal. The restriction to the sunnah of Fajr is noted because other sunan are not made up. Then an intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: According to Abu Hanifa, if one makes up the four before Dhuhr, they do not count as sunnah (rather as nafl), but according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, they do count as sunnah. This is a point of ikhtilaf within the school. The commentary also discusses the timing of making up the four before Dhuhr relative to the two rak'ahs of Fajr: Should the four be made up before or after the two? There are different narrations from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and the preferred view (as per Fath al-Qadir) is to give precedence to the two rak'ahs of Fajr because the four were missed from their proper time. The ruling for the four before Jumu'ah is analogized to the four before Dhuhr. The passage uses hadith evidence from Aisha and relies on the principles of qiyas and istihsan.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that is not obligatory but consistently performed by the Prophet.
نفل (nafl): A voluntary, supererogatory act of worship, lower in rank than sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is sunnah and carries sunnah reward.
C) It is not made up at all.
D) It is wajib and must be made up.

Key Takeaway
Missed sunnah prayers are made up after their time, and the relied-upon Hanafi view is that the qada retains sunnah status.

Catching a Rak'ah and Oaths for Congregational Prayer
Ruling on idrak and its application to oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that catching one rak'ah suffices for congregational reward and how the same principle is applied in oath rulings, including the ikhtilaf with al-Sarakhsi.

Core Idea
Catching one rak'ah is like catching the whole prayer – but for oaths, missing any part may break the oath unless trivial.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two interconnected issues: the legal definition of 'catching' (idrak) a congregational prayer and its implications for oaths. The author establishes the primary ruling via the well-known hadith, then examines a nuanced case where a man swears to pray Dhuhr in congregation and misses part of it. An intra-Hanafi disagreement with Imam al-Sarakhsi is presented and resolved through qiyas with general oath principles and an exceptional case from al-Khulasah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and its proof
Locate the hadith: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' Note that it is mutaffaq 'alayh. This establishes that catching one rak'ah with the imam gives the virtue of congregation.
The hadith is the core dalil naqli for the ruling.
2
Analyse the oath case from al-Jami' al-Kabir
Examine the scenario: a man swears his slave is free if he prays Dhuhr in congregation. He misses some part (rak'ah or more). According to the majority (including Qadikhan), he does not break the oath because he did not pray the entire prayer with the imam.
This shows that 'catching' in oaths requires full participation; missing any part prevents hanth.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with al-Sarakhsi
al-Sarakhsi holds that if the missing part is a minority (i.e., he catches most), he breaks the oath because 'the majority has the ruling of the whole'. Understand his reasoning and the majority's response using the loaf of bread analogy.
The majority's position is strengthened by the agreed-upon principle that the majority is not equivalent to the whole in oaths.
4
Apply the exception from al-Khulasah
The exception: if one swears not to read a surah and leaves out only one letter, the oath is broken; leaving out a long verse does not break it. This clarifies that the threshold for 'trivial' omission is very low – only a single letter is considered negligible.
This exception is used to rebut al-Sarakhsi's position: missing a rak'ah is not trivial like a letter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولم يصل الظهر جماعة بإدراك (ركعة) لما في الجامع الكبير : إذا قال عبده حر إن صلى الظهر بجماعة فسبق ببعضها لم يحنث وهو شامل لما إذا سبق بركعة أو بأكثر . وذكر قاضيخان في شرحه أن الظاهر الجواب أنه إذا فاتته ركعة مع الإمام وصلى الثلاث معه لا يحنث لأنه لم يصل الكل مع الإمام، فلو قال المصنف بإدراك بعضها لكان أولى لكن ذكر الإمام السرخسي أنه يحنث لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، ولا يحنث إذا صلى ركعتين فقط اتفاقاً كما لا يخفى. أما على الأولى فظاهر، وأما على قول السرخسي فلأنه ليس بأكثر حتى يقام مقام الكل. ومما يضعف قول السرخسي ما اتفقوا عليه في باب الأيمان أنه لو حلف لا يأكل هذا الرغيف لا يحنف إلا بأكل كله فإن الأكثر لا يقام مقام الكل لكن في الخلاصة من كتاب الأيمان: لو حلف لا يقرأ سورة فقرأها إلا حرفاً حنث ولو قرأها إلا آية طويلة لا يحنث .
قوله : (بل أدرك (فضلها أي فضل الجماعة لأن من أدرك آخر الشيء فقد أدركه، ولحديث الصحيح من أدرك ركعة من الصلاة فقد أدرك الصلاة »(۱) وهو مجمع عليه. وإنما
قوله : (لكن) في الخلاصة الخ) قال العلامة نوح أفندي: الفرق بين الحرف

His statement: (And he did not pray Dhuhr in congregation catching [a rak'ah]) because in al-Jami' al-Kabir: If he says to his slave 'You are free if I pray Dhuhr in congregation' and he misses some of it, he does not break the oath. This includes whether he missed one rak'ah or more. Qadikhan mentioned in his commentary that the apparent answer is: If one rak'ah with the imam is missed and he prays the three with him, does not break the oath because he did not pray the entire prayer with the imam. So if the author had said 'catching some of it', it would have been better. But Imam al-Sarakhsi mentioned that he breaks the oath because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And he does not break the oath if he only prays two rak'ahs by agreement, as is not hidden. As for the first [view], it is apparent. As for the statement of al-Sarakhsi, it is because it is not a majority to be considered as the whole. And among what weakens al-Sarakhsi's statement is what they agreed upon in the chapter of oaths: If someone swears not to eat this loaf of bread, he does not break the oath except by eating all of it, because the majority is not considered as the whole. But in al-Khulasah from the Book of Oaths: If someone swears not to read a surah and he reads it except one letter, he breaks the oath; and if he reads it except a long verse, he does not break the oath.

His statement: (Rather he caught its virtue) meaning the virtue of congregation, because whoever catches the last part of something has caught it, and due to the authentic hadith: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' And it is unanimously agreed upon.

His statement: (But in al-Khulasah etc.) Allamah Nuh Afandi said: The difference between the letter... [text incomplete]
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the legal definition of 'catching' (idrak) a congregational prayer. It begins by examining a specific case: a man swears that if he prays Dhuhr in congregation, his slave is free. If he misses part of the prayer (e.g., one rak'ah or more), does he break his oath? According to al-Jami' al-Kabir, he does not break the oath if he misses any part, because he did not pray the entire prayer with the congregation. Qadikhan supports this view. However, Imam al-Sarakhsi holds that if he misses only a minority (i.e., he prays most of the prayer with the imam), he breaks the oath because the majority is treated as the whole. The commentator then discusses the strength of each argument, citing the general principle from oaths that the majority is not equivalent to the whole (e.g., eating most of a loaf does not break an oath not to eat that loaf). However, an exception from al-Khulasah is noted: if one swears not to read a surah and leaves out only a letter, he breaks the oath, but leaving out a long verse does not break it. This indicates that the ruling depends on what is considered significant.

The second part addresses the hadith 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of the prayer has caught the prayer.' This hadith is mutaffaq 'alayh (agreed upon). It establishes that catching one rak'ah with the imam entitles the follower to the virtue of congregation. The commentator then transitions to a discussion about the four rak'ahs before Jumu'ah (mentioned later). The passage also includes a footnote giving the hadith references.

Key Terms
إدراك (idrak): Catching or attaining a part of the congregational prayer such that one is considered to have prayed with the congregation.
حنث (hanith): Breaking an oath or vow, incurring expiation.
سبق ببعضها (sabaqa bi-ba'diha): To miss part of the prayer (i.e., not to pray the entire prayer with the imam).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best summarises the rule for breaking an oath to pray in congregation according to the Hanafi majority?
A) If you catch any part of the prayer, the oath is fulfilled.
B) If you catch at least one rak'ah, the oath is fulfilled.
C) If you catch most of the prayer (more than half), the oath is fulfilled.
D) You must catch the entire prayer (all rak'ahs) for the oath to be fulfilled.

Key Takeaway
Catching one rak'ah earns the reward of congregation, but fulfilling an oath to pray in congregation requires completing the entire prayer with the imam.
