Qada of the Four Sunnah Before Jumu'ah
Critical refinement of the proof for qada of sunnah before Jumu'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not require making up the four sunnah rak'ahs before Jumu'ah, and distinguish this from the sunnah before Dhuhr using the specific hadith and principle.

Core Idea
The sunnah before Dhuhr is made up due to a specific hadith; Jumu'ah is not analogized, so qada is not required.

The Friday prayer has a sunnah of four rak'ahs before the congregational prayer. But what if you miss them? Are they made up like the sunnah before Dhuhr? This lesson examines a critical refinement of the proof, showing that the hadith 'when the imam comes out' does not automatically imply that qada is abandoned, but the original principle of no qada for sunnan applies, and the exception for Dhuhr is specific to Dhuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The question is whether the four sunnah rak'ahs before Jumu'ah, if missed, are to be made up after the Friday prayer, analogous to the four before Dhuhr.
The Hanafi school generally holds that sunnan are not made up after their time, except for some specific cases.
2
State the apparent analogy
Some scholars, based on general texts, analogize Jumu'ah to Dhuhr, arguing that since Dhuhr's sunnah is made up, Jumu'ah's should be too.
The analogy is superficially plausible: both are four rak'ahs before the fard.
3
Present the counter-proof
A hadith states: 'When the imam comes out, there is no prayer except the obligatory.' This is used to argue that the four before Jumu'ah are dropped entirely, including qada.
The source is Rawdat al-Ulama, a Shafi'i work, but the hadith is accepted.
4
Analyze the author's critique
The author (Ibn Nujaym) critiques that the hadith only prohibits praying after the imam's appearance, not that the sunnah is completely abandoned. He analogizes to Dhuhr: the prohibition at iqamah does not prevent qada.
The author shows that the hadith is not definitive against qada.
5
Identify the determinative principle
The original principle is that sunnan are not made up after their time. Dhuhr's sunnah is an exception due to the specific hadith of Aisha. Jumu'ah is not covered by that exception, so the original principle applies.
Thus, the four before Jumu'ah are not made up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وحكم الأربع قبل الجمعة الخ) أقول قال شيخنا الشيخ محمد السراجي الحانوتي: وأما كونها هل تقضى أو لا؛ فعلى ما قالوه في المتون وغيرها من أن سنة الظهر تقضى يقتضي أن تقضى سنة الجمعة إذ لا فرق لكن في روضة العلماء في باب فضل من سمع الأذان : وإذا جاء الرجل إلى الجمعة في وقت الإمامة هل يصلي أربع ركعات التي يصليها قبل الجمعة أو لا؟ قال: لا يصلي بل يسكت ثم يدخل مع الإمام في صلاته وسقطت عنه هذه الأربع لما روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال «إذا خرج الإمام فلا صلاة الا المكتوبة ا هـ . ذكره في فتاواه التي وقعت له والله أعلم خير الدين الرملي. أقول: وفي هذه الاستدلال نظر فإنه إنما يدل على أنها لا تصلى بعد خروجه لا على أنها تسقط بالكلية حتى إنها لا تقضى بعد فراغه من المكتوبة وإلا لزم أن لا تقضى سنة الظهر أيضاً إذا جاء ووجد الإمام أنه شارعاً في الظهر مع ورد النهي عن الصلاة عند الإقامة كما في حديث الصحيحين وغيرهما «إذا أقيمت الصلاة فلا صلاة إلا المكتوبة (۲) نعم قد يقال إن الأصل عدم قضائها إذا فاتت عن محلها، وأما سنة الظهر فإنما قالوا بقضائها لحديث عائشة أنه كان إذا فاتته الأربع قبل الظهر قضاهن بعده كما قدمه المؤلف فتكون سنة الظهر خارجة عن القياس للحديث المذكور فلا يقاس عليها سنة الجمعة فتأمل
His statement: (And the ruling of the four before Jumu'ah etc.) I say: Our teacher Shaykh Muhammad al-Siraji al-Hanuti said: As for whether they are made up or not; based on what they said in the texts and others that the sunnah of Dhuhr is made up, it would necessitate that the sunnah of Jumu'ah is also made up since there is no difference. But in Rawdat al-Ulama in the chapter of virtue of hearing the call: If a man comes to Jumu'ah at the time of the imam's leading, should he pray the four rak'ahs that he prays before Jumu'ah or not? He said: He does not pray, rather he remains silent, then enters with the imam in his prayer, and these four are dropped from him due to what is reported from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he said: 'When the imam comes out, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' He mentioned it in his fatwas that occurred to him, and Allah knows best. Khayr al-Din al-Ramli. I say: In this deduction is consideration, for it only indicates that they should not be prayed after he comes out, not that they are dropped entirely to the extent that they are not made up after he finishes the obligatory prayer. Otherwise, it would necessitate that the sunnah of Dhuhr also not be made up if he comes and finds the imam commencing Dhuhr, despite the prohibition of prayer at the iqamah as in the hadith of the two Sahihs and others: 'When the iqamah is made, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' Yes, it may be said that the original principle is that it is not made up if it misses its place. As for the sunnah of Dhuhr, they said it is made up due to the hadith of Aisha that he used to make up the four before Dhuhr after it, as the author presented. Thus the sunnah of Dhuhr is outside analogy due to the mentioned hadith, so the sunnah of Jumu'ah is not analogized to it. So reflect.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement addressing whether the four sunnah rak'ahs before Jumu'ah are made up if missed, in analogy with the four before Dhuhr. The author initially cites Shaykh Muhammad al-Siraji al-Hanuti, who notes that the general ruling from matns suggests that since the sunnah of Dhuhr is made up, the sunnah of Jumu'ah should also be made up as there is no apparent difference. However, a report from Rawdat al-Ulama provides a hadith: 'When the imam comes out, there is no prayer except the obligatory one.' This hadith is used to argue that the four before Jumu'ah are not prayed even before the imam comes out? Actually the context: a person arrives when the imam is about to lead; he should not pray the four but enter directly. This implies that the four are dropped entirely, and thus not made up. The author then critically analyzes this deduction, stating that the hadith only prohibits praying after the imam comes out, not that the sunnah is completely abandoned so that it is not made up after the obligatory prayer. He draws a parallel to Dhuhr: if one arrives during the iqamah, the prohibition 'When the iqamah is made, there is no prayer except the obligatory' applies, but the sunnah of Dhuhr is still made up after the fard. So the prohibition during the imam's appearance does not necessarily preclude qada afterward. The author finally suggests that the original principle is no qada for sunnan that miss their time, but Dhuhr's sunnah is exceptional due to the specific hadith of Aisha, and Jumu'ah's sunnah is not analogized to that exception. Thus, the four before Jumu'ah are not made up after the Friday prayer. The passage ends with an invitation to reflect (ta'ammul).

Key Terms
الأربع قبل الجمعة (al-arba' qabl al-jumu'ah): The four sunnah rak'ahs performed before the Friday congregational prayer.
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
خروج الإمام (khuruj al-imam): The imam coming out to deliver the Friday sermon or leading the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's conclusion, what is the ruling on making up the four sunnah rak'ahs before Jumu'ah after the Friday prayer?
A) They are made up, just like the four before Dhuhr.
B) They are not made up, because the original principle is no qada for sunnah after its time, and the exception for Dhuhr does not extend to Jumu'ah.
C) They are made up only if one intentionally missed them.
D) They are wajib to make up.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require making up the four sunnah rak'ahs before Jumu'ah because the exception for Dhuhr does not apply and the original principle of no qada for sunnan governs.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Catching the Imam in Ruku': Participation Required for the Rak'ah
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on catching the rak'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on catching the rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku', explain Zufar's opposing view, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
Catching a rak'ah requires sharing both qiyam and ruku' with the imam.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute about what constitutes catching a rak'ah. The matn rules that a latecomer who joins during ruku' but does not bow with the imam has not caught the rak'ah. Zufar, a Hanafi scholar, argues otherwise. We will examine the proofs and the practical difference between the two positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What exactly is the scenario being ruled upon? The latecomer (masbuq) catches the imam while the imam is bowing (ruku'), says the takbir, and stands (remains standing) until the imam raises his head from ruku'.
Note: The latecomer does not bow at all during the imam's ruku'.
2
State the Hanafi majority position
According to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the latecomer does NOT catch that rak'ah. He is a masbuq and must complete the missed rak'ah after the imam finishes the prayer.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State Zufar's opposing view
Zufar holds that the latecomer DOES catch the rak'ah. He argues that ruku' has the 'ruling of standing' (hukm al-qiyam) in some respects, so participating in ruku' alone suffices. In Zufar's view, the latecomer is a lahiq and performs that rak'ah before the imam finishes.
The term 'lahiq' is used differently by Zufar than the majority.
4
Analyze the proof (Hanafi response)
The majority condition for catching a rak'ah is actual participation in the actions of prayer (sharikat fi af'al al-salat). Since the latecomer participated in neither the qiyam (he did not stand with the imam before ruku') nor the ruku' (he did not bow with the imam), the condition is not met. The imam's ruku' cannot substitute for the missing qiyam.
This is a rational (aqli) argument based on the definition of 'idrak'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to Zufar, the latecomer is a lahiq and performs the missed rak'ah BEFORE the imam's taslim; according to the majority, he is a masbuq and performs it AFTER the imam finishes. This affects the sequence and whether the imam's prayer has ended when the latecomer prays.
The text also notes that both sides agree on two subsidiary points: if he catches the imam standing and bows after him, he catches the rak'ah; if he joins only during the transitional movement, he does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أدرك إمامه راكعاً فكبر ووقف حتى رفع رأسه لم يدرك الركعة) خلافاً لزفر . هو يقول أدرك الإمام فيما له حكم القيام، ولنا أن الشرط هو المشاركة في أفعال الصلاة ولم يوجد لا في القيام ولا في الركوع . وذكر قاضيخان أن ثمرة الخلاف تظهر في أن هذا عنده لاحق في هذه الركعة حتى يأتي بها قبل فراغ الإمام، وعندنا هو مسبوق بها حتى يأتي بها بعد فراغ الإمام، وأجمعوا أنه لو انتهى إلى الإمام وهو قائم فكبر ولم يركع مع الإمام حتى ركع الإمام ثم ركع أنه يصير مدركاً لتلك الركعة وأجمعوا أنه لو اقتدى به في قومة الركوع لم يصر مدركاً لتلك الركعة ا هـ . وفي المصفي : وهذا إذا أمكنه الركوع، أما إذا لم يمكنه لا يعتد به عند زفر أيضاً. وفي حيرة الفقهاء : إمام افتتح الصلاة فلما ركع ورفع رأسه من الركوع ظن أنه لم يقرأ السورة فرجع وقرأ . ثم علم أنه كان قرأ السورة فجاء رجل ودخل في الصلاة ثم ركع ثانياً فإن هذا المسبوق يصير داخلاً في الصلاة لكن عليه أن يقضي ركعة لأن الركوع الأول كان فرضاً تاماً والآخر نفلاً فصار كأن المسبوق لم يدرك الركوع من هذه الركعة ا هـ. وفي فتح القدير : ومدرك الإمام في الركوع لا يحتاج إلى تكبيرتين خلافاً لبعضهم، ولو نوى بتلك التكبيرة الواحدة الركوع لا الافتتاح جاز ولغت نيته ا هـ . ثم اعلم أنه إذا لم يكن مدركاً للركعة فإنه يجب عليه أن يتابع الإمام في السجدتين وإن لم يحتسبا له كما لو اقتدى بالإمام بعد ما رفع الإمام رأسه من الركوع. صرح قاضيخان في فتاواه بأن عليه المتابعة في السجدتين وإن لم يحتسبا له وصرح به في العمدة. وصرح في الذخيرة بأن المتابعة فيهما واجبة ومقتضاه أنه لو تركهما لا تفسد صلاته.
And if he catches his imam bowing and says takbir and stands until [the imam] raises his head, he has not caught the rak'ah, contrary to Zufar. He (Zufar) says: he caught the imam in what has the ruling of standing. For us, the condition is participation in the actions of prayer, and it did not occur neither in standing nor in bowing. Imam Qadikhan mentioned that the practical consequence of the dispute appears: according to him (Zufar) he is a lahiq in this rak'ah, so he performs it before the imam finishes; according to us he is a masbuq in it, so he performs it after the imam finishes. And they are unanimous that if he reaches the imam while he is standing and says takbir and does not bow with the imam until the imam bows and then he bows, that he becomes one who caught that rak'ah; and they are unanimous that if he follows the imam during the standing of ruku' (i.e., when he is about to bow or rising), he does not become one who caught that rak'ah. In al-Musaffa: this applies if he was able to bow; but if he was not able, it is not counted even according to Zufar. In Hayrat al-Fuqaha': An imam started the prayer, then when he bowed and raised his head from bowing, he thought he had not recited the sura, so he went back and recited. Then he realised he had recited the sura. Then a man came and entered the prayer, then [the imam] bowed a second time. This masbuq becomes a participant in the prayer, but he must make up a rak'ah because the first bowing was a complete obligatory [part] and the second was supererogatory, so it is as if the masbuq did not catch the bowing from this rak'ah. In Fath al-Qadir: The one who catches the imam in bowing does not need two takbirs, contrary to some; and if he intends with that single takbir the bowing and not the opening, it is valid but his intention is void. Then know: when he has not caught the rak'ah, he must follow the imam in the two prostrations even though they are not counted for him, just as if he followed the imam after he raised his head from bowing. Qadikhan stated in his Fatawa that he must follow in the two prostrations even if not counted for him; it is also stated in al-Umdah. And in al-Dhakhira he stated that following in them is obligatory, and its implication is that if he abandons them, his prayer is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute about catching the rak'ah when joining the imam during ruku'. The matn states: if a person catches the imam bowing (i.e., while the imam is in ruku'), says the takbir, and stands (meaning he remains standing without joining the ruku' until the imam raises his head), then he has not caught that rak'ah. Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagrees, arguing that being present during the ruku' is equivalent to having caught the standing because the ruku' has the 'ruling of standing' in some sense. The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rebut: the condition for catching a rak'ah is actual participation in the actions of the prayer; since this person neither participated in the qiyam (standing) before the imam's ruku' nor in the ruku' itself (he remained standing), he has not caught the rak'ah. Qadikhan then explains the practical difference (thamara): according to Zufar, the latecomer is a 'lahiq' (one who follows after the imam finishes) in that rak'ah, meaning he performs that rak'ah before the imam completes the prayer; according to the school, he is a 'masbuq' (one who missed a rak'ah) and must perform that rak'ah after the imam finishes his prayer. The text then reports a consensus (ijma') among the Hanafi imams (excluding Zufar) on two subsidiary points: (1) if someone catches the imam while he is standing (qiyam) and then bows after the imam bows, he catches the rak'ah; (2) if someone follows the imam during the 'qawmat al-ruku' (the transitional movement from standing to bowing or from bowing to rising), he does not catch the rak'ah. The passage then cites al-Musaffa, which qualifies Zufar's position: if the person was unable to bow (e.g., because the imam raised his head immediately), even Zufar agrees he does not catch the rak'ah. Another scenario from Hayrat al-Fuqaha' illustrates: an imam who mistakenly repeated the bowing after reciting after ruku' — a latecomer who joins during that second bowing does not catch the first rak'ah because the first bowing was the obligatory one. The text also mentions a ruling from Fath al-Qadir: the latecomer who catches the imam in ruku' does not need two takbirs (one for ihram and one for ruku'), contrary to some; if he intends both with one takbir, it is valid but his intention is voided. Finally, the passage addresses the obligation of following the imam in the two prostrations even if they are not counted for the latecomer: Qadikhan's Fatawa, al-Umdah, and al-Dhakhira affirm this obligation, but if one abandons them, the prayer is not invalidated, indicating it is a wajib (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar).

Key Terms
مسبوق (masbuq): A latecomer who missed one or more rak'ahs of the congregation and must complete them after the imam's taslim.
لاحق (lahiq): A latecomer who caught part of the congregation but missed some rak'ahs; according to Zufar, a person who catches the imam in ruku' is a lahiq and performs the missed part before the imam finishes.
إدراك الركعة (idrak al-rak'ah): The legal ruling of having caught a rak'ah by participating in its essential actions (qiyam, ruku', and if applicable, prostration) with the imam from the beginning of the rak'ah.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarat al-khilaf): The practical consequence or outcome of a legal dispute between scholars or schools; it shows how the difference in interpretation affects actual practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority, what is the ruling for a person who catches the imam in ruku', says takbir, and remains standing until the imam raises his head?
A) He catches the rak'ah and continues with the imam.
B) He does not catch the rak'ah, and must perform it after the imam finishes.
C) He does not catch the rak'ah, and must perform it before the imam finishes.
D) He catches the rak'ah only if he also bows before the imam rises.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, catching a rak'ah requires sharing both qiyam and ruku' with the imam; mere presence during ruku' is insufficient.
